wearing **official headdress and sash** (具冠简),
in **purple robes** (紫衣),
with **all attendants following as prescribed** (如法诸卫从),
according to the **three diagrams of Han Hong** (如含弘等三图).
**Store them only after donning the prescribed attire and headdress** (存之，唯加具衣冠简).

**The Six Methods** (六法),
are to be performed on the **fixed hour of Regal Monkey** (庚申初夜),
*[Note: the first watch is Regal Monkey]* (注：初夜一更是).
On **Earthly Horse’s initial night** (己未日初夜),
enter the **fifth watch** (入五更是).
**Regal Monkey’s day is set for this** (庚申日定之也).
When **storing thoughts** (思存出),
follow the **Han Hong diagram** (如含弘图).

This is to **sever and cut off calamities of the Three Realms** (断截三界灾厄),
**the Three Corpses and Six Demons** (三尸六魔),
**the Three Officials and Nine Earths** (三官九地),
**root out sinful causes** (落灭罪根),
**augment life longevity** (添益寿算),
**remove the death ledgers of the Three Officials** (落除三官死簿),
and **inscribe the True Spirit’s celestial register of birth** (注上生历神真之位).

Upon completion, **knock the teeth thirty-six times** (毕，叩齿三十六通).
**Hold firm** (握固),
then **twirl the talisman of one’s own life span and sovereign fate** (即捻本身司命诀),
and **ingest the talisman dispelling the Three Corpses** (服去三尸之符).
*[Note: the talisman is found in *The Sacred Scriptures of the Fifty Generals* (符在《五十将军灵书》中).]*

Upon completion, **lie down in repose** (即任安卧).
**Awake before and after the second watch of Earthly Horse** (卧起五更二点前后).
**Again store thoughts** (又思存),
as before.

After **one cycle** (一度讫),
**swallow the talisman** (吞符).
**Practice this twelve times** (行之一十二度),
and the **Three Corpses demons will depart forever** (三尸虫永去),
**even in death, they dare not return** (死亦不敢来),
thus becoming **a person of the Highest True** (上真之人),
**worthy of honor and protection** (可贵可保).

This method is **subtle and profound** (微妙),
**unfit for reckless transmission to the unworthy** (不可妄传非人),
lest calamity befalls the **seven ancestral masters** (殃及七祖矣).

---
**End of the Fifteenth Chapter of *The Golden Lock and Flowing Pearl* (金锁流珠引卷之十五竟)**
**End of the Sixteenth Chapter of *The Golden Lock and Flowing Pearl* (金锁流珠引卷之十六)**.

**The Complete and True Great Immortal Sovereign Master Zhang Fangping, Founder of the Daoist Tradition, Zhao Sheng, King of the Celestial Command, Li Zhongfu, and Master Mao Ying, Xu Yufu, and Others—Transmitted Across Generations**

**Master Li Chunfeng, the Daoist Sage of the Han, Annotated**

**The Supreme Mysteries of the Six Jia: The Yin Function**

The **Six Jia** are the offspring of the Five Phases.
*Annotation:* The Dao gives birth to primordial *qi*; one generates two—Yin and Yang.
Two generates three—the Three Primordials.
Three generates four—the Four Seasons.
Four generates five—the Five Phases.
The Five Phases generate the Six Jia: *Jiazi, Jiaxu, Jia Shen, Jia Wu, Jia Chen, Jia Yin.*

The Six Jia generate the Seven Stars,
The Seven Stars generate the Nine Essences,
The Nine Essences generate the Ten Celestial Stems,
The Ten Celestial Stems generate the Twelve Earthly Branches,
The Twelve Earthly Branches generate the Twenty-Eight Constellations.
The Twenty-Eight Constellations generate the Thirty-Five Divine Officers,
The Thirty-Five Divine Officers generate the Forty-Nine Stars,
The Forty-Nine Stars generate the Sixty-Four Coalescent Stars,
The Sixty-Four Coalescent Stars generate the Eighty-One Extremity Stars.
The stars are measured in Yin and Yang,
Thus they are called the **Ultimate of the Small Numbers**,
And are known as the **Ancient Method**,
With eighty-one as their extreme limit.
Now, these eighty-one generate the myriad phenomena of the revolving heavens—
A number beyond comprehension.

There are three grades.

**The Highest Grade:** The talismans enter the **Upper Primordial**,
*Annotation:* Known as the **Lord Lao’s Six Jia Talismans**—those used today.
Called the **Lord Lao’s Inner Secrets: Three Talismans, Six Jia Scriptures.**
When mortals encounter them,
With sincere devotion and diligent practice,
They are freed from a hundred ailments,
And the Six Spirits arrive.
*Annotation:* The Six Spirits are:
1. The Six Jia Generals,
2. The Six Jia Day Officials,
3. The Six Jia Jade Boys and Jade Girls,
4. The Day Official Attendants,
5. The Direct Talisman,
6. The Talisman Clerks—six in total.
They capture evil and inspect the essences—
None are without spiritual efficacy.
For those who tread the Daoist path,
None can succeed without them.
If there are those with sincere devotion and joy in the Dao,
They must first master the talismans,
Stabilize the soul and calm the spirit,
Anchor the essence and solidify the form,
And forever secure the root of longevity,
The gateway to attaining the Dao.
The seals of invocation are opened—
Whatever is summoned, stored, or employed,
This is the **Chief Messenger of Announcement**,
The **Commander-in-Chief of the Three Officials**.

The **Preface to the Lord Lao’s Six Jia Talismans** states:
*"All the myriad gods of Heaven and Earth are the subordinates of the Six Jia."*
*Annotation:* Within the vast cosmos,
There are myriad gods and spirits,
Ten thousand evils and myriad essences,
All recorded and commanded by the Six Jia,
And all are the servants of the Six Jia.
Thus, mortals who know this
Receive the Six Jia Scriptures,
Serve the Six Jia Talismans,
And wear the **Six Jia Direct Spirit Plaques**—
This is to measure the depth of their merit,
To drive the myriad spirits,
And to aid the nation and save the people.

In the ancient past, all who cultivated the Dao
Attained it through the Six Jia.
*Annotation:* The Six Jia are the foremost of the **Six Primordial Methods**—
The sacred path of the **Ancient Sage Lord Lao** and the **Later Sage Jade Emperor**,
The gateway and the thoroughfare of cultivation.

**The Middle Grade:** The Six Jia are called **Lingfei**,
Commanding **1,360 Jade Boys** and **2,440 Jade Girls.**

The **Lord Lao’s Secret Six Jia Talismans** include:
Eleven Great Generals,
1,200 Attendants,
970 Jade Boys, Jade Girls, and Talisman Clerks,
And countless soldiers, beasts, and messengers—
Sufficient to field **120,000 troops** for the Highest Grade.

The **Most High Lord Lao** established the **Six Jia of Heaven and Earth**,
With six camps, each divided into four divisions.
One division resides within the human body—
*[Note: Further annotations to follow.]*

「Lingfei is of the Middle Grade, included in the count of the **Upper Pure** (上清).

The Five Phases and Six Jia form the **Lower Grade**, hence this is called the **Three Grades of Six Jia**.

Those who practice the Dao must all cultivate and revere the **Three Grades of Six Jia**.

*Annotation:* The Upper and Middle Grades—
Taking them daily for **fourteen years** grants ascension to the Dao.

The **Lower Grade Six Jia** expel misfortune from the body,
And are used in calculations for **decrepit kings** (算衰王).

The **Later Sage Lord Lao** instructed the **Jade Boys and Ladies of the Rectangular Array** (方诸童君夫人):
*"For those who wish to cultivate the body and prolong life,
First, they must cultivate and ingest the divine talismans of the Six Jia.
This was the most sacred method of the **Earlier Sage**,
Commonly known as the **Lord Lao’s Secret Six Jia Talismans**.
The method of ingestion is as follows:
Each time one recites the names of the **Divine Officials** (神直官),
One summons the **Talisman Clerks of the Decade** (旬将),
And the names of the **Jade Girls**.

Upon summoning, one must recite the **Earlier Sage’s Long-Life Incantation** (前圣长生咒) twice,
Then swallow the talisman.

After **three years** of swallowing the talisman,
One then ingests the **Lingfei Six Jia Talismans**,
Swallowing them in the same manner as the **Lord Lao’s Secret Six Jia Talismans**.
Once finished, proceed to swallow the **Lingfei Six Jia Talismans**.

The talismans must all be inscribed with the names of the **Divine Officials**, **Talisman Clerks**, and **Jade Girls**.
One must call upon each by name.

The Master says:
*"The secret lies in this:
The Six Jia deities have many repeated names and surnames,
And one cannot remember them all.
Thus, small wooden or bamboo plaques are made,
Upon which the names of the deities, generals, clerks, and jade girls are inscribed,
And each is recorded accordingly.
Whether standing, walking, sitting, or reclining,
One must always bear their names in mind.
In urgent matters, one must blow upon and invoke the talismans,
To rescue people, subdue ghosts, expel evil, and repel harm.
If one’s life is in peril, the plaques should be taken out,
And the names invoked immediately—
The response will be instantaneous.

However, when sleeping at night or entering a woman’s chamber,
One must hang them in a secure place on the wall or pillar,
And they will still be effective.
Do not hang them on the doorframe,
For the **Doorframe Deities** (门户神) may fear them,
Causing unrest.

One must commit their names to memory.
When urgently invoking them,
It must be done as swiftly as **hand responds to heart** (手应心),
And as decisively as **heart commands the mouth** (心制口).
*Annotation:* In the **Upper Ancient** (上古) era, great Daoists practiced **direct heart-mouth control** (直心制口),
Where their words were never misspoken.
Thus, a heart’s vow is the same as a mouth’s vow—
It must be genuine.
This is the practice of the **Dao Immortals** (仙人).

The talismans will arrive immediately upon invocation.
One must remember their names and surnames,
And keep them in mind during leisure hours.
When urgently invoked,
Their power will manifest instantly.
Moreover, before eating or drinking,
One must first mentally invoke them,
And maintain the presence of the **Divine Officials**, **Talisman Clerks of the Decade**, and **Jade Girls** throughout the day.
If one shares food and drink with them as subjects,
They will bestow the **Mysterious Sweet Offerings** (玄甘飨).
When consuming various foods, drinks, or fruits,
One must always mentally invoke them daily,
And share in the same food and drink.
This practice, when consistently applied,
Will yield great efficacy.

They can also suppress **army disasters** (兵害) and subdue **heavenly demons** (天魔).
*Annotation:* In antiquity, a Daoist in the mountains named **Li Boyao** (李伯药),
Often cultivated the **Six Jia Method** and ingested the talismans.
He stayed in the mountains for five years without emerging.

One day, suddenly, he saw a man in green robes,
Riding a leopard, offering a small bottle.
The man said:
*"This is the **Great Elixir Master Boyao** (大丹伯药).
You have nearly attained the Dao,
But your form and spirit are withering.
You must ingest this elixir,
And you will achieve long life.
I have come today to bestow this medicine upon you—
This is the **True Great Reversion Elixir** (真大还丹).
Here is a golden bottle.
Look, the bottle contains the **True Golden Elixir** (真金丹),
With pills of a **purple-gold hue** (紫金色).
I tell you, my disciples:
I have now attained the Dao.
The **Daoist Messengers** (仙使) have brought me the **Great Elixir** (太丹).
I will take it and ascend to the heavens.
You must follow my practice,
And never waver in your resolve—
You will surely also obtain this elixir.
On the day of my departure,
Come to the heavens to seek me out."

Li Boyao’s disciple, **Wei Xiang** (韦祥), did not yet understand,
And only heard voices in the forest,
As if from hundreds of people,
Including the sounds of women.

In a short while, one voice issued orders:
*"Seize him!"*
Immediately, over ten men in red robes,
Clad as **leopard-riding messengers** (乘豹使者),
Captured and threw the man to the ground.
He transformed into an **Old Dragon** (老龙),
And the leopard into an **Old Tiger** (老虎).
They struck him with twenty blows.

With a stern command, they declared:
*"Li Boyao has attained the Dao,
Though he has not yet gained renown—
He has long been inscribed in the **Daoist Register** (仙籍).
How dare he act as a **malevolent ghost** (为祟),
Seeking to harm with poisonous elixir!"*

Li Boyao knew this was not a true person,
And questioned them about their origins.
The **Jade Girl of Jia-Shen** (甲申玉女) responded:
*"The **Heavenly Demon Poison Ghosts** (天魔毒鬼),
Transformed into an Old Dragon and Old Tiger,
To harm you.
If you do not diligently cultivate the Six Jia,
You will surely fall to their poison and die."*

In a short while, the **Dragon and Tiger Poison Ghosts** (龙虎毒) all dissolved into ghosts and perished.
Were it not for the **Six Jia Deities’ power** (六甲神之功),
Li Boyao would not have been saved,
And would have been poisoned by the **Heavenly Demon’s elixir** (天魔进药) and died.

Now, this account is recorded for the world.
People should not presume to refuse or neglect them—
The **Heavenly Demon** will take back the elixir,
And depart in submission after bowing.
They will no longer dare to harm others,
And such instances often occur.
This allows one to earn merit and attain the Dao.»

「You, among the various teachings, have shown true earnestness.
Thus, you must first diligently cultivate the **Three Elements** (三元) and **Six Jia** (六甲),
And over time, you will naturally attain communion with the gods.
This method is subtle and profound,
And should not be carelessly transmitted to those unworthy.

**Laozi** (老君) said:
*"This method possesses six divine powers (六通神力).
First, it grants passage into the **Great Dao’s Gate** (大道之门),
Skillfully leveraging the **Dao’s authority** (假道威),
Subduing gods and enslaving ghosts,
Quelling and annihilating malevolent spirits and **Jiao-demons** (精妖),
Severing and dispelling **Feng-spirits** (凶祟).

Second, it allows communion with the **Heavenly Realm** (通天),
Inspiring the **Heavenly Gods** (天神) and **Heavenly Dragons** (天龙)
To exterminate demons and subdue **Heavenly Conflicts** (祆).
It can gather clouds and summon rains,
Countering the **obstructive and malevolent qi of rebellious spirits** (逆横祆恶之炁),
And effectively dispel such calamities.

Third, it grants communion with the **Earthly Realm** (通地),
Inspiring the **Earthly Gods** (地神) and **Earthly Dragons** (地龙),
As well as the **Wind and Cloud Lords** (风云雷公),
**Lightning, Rain, and Wind Officials** (电师雨师风师),
The **Five Sacred Mountains** (五岳) and **Four Celestial Constraints** (四镇).
*Note: The Four Celestial Constraints are also called the Four Rivers (四渎), the official waters that constrain the mountains.*
The **Nine Regions and Ten Thousand States, Myriad Countries** (九州千邦万国),
And all **terrestrial deities** (土地山川神灵),
**Ancestral shrines and city gods** (社庙城隍),
*Note: City God (城隍神) is a deity appointed by the later Sage Emperor (后圣君) to oversee the Underworld (地府).*
As recorded in the **Sū Brū** (苏吴纪纪云): *"King Fú of Wú"* (吴王苪是).
The **Left Ancestral and Right Harvest Deities** (左社右稷神官).
They will assist the realm,
Protect your person and family,
And aid all living beings.

Fourth, it grants communion with the **Watery Realm** (通水),
Inspiring the **Water Gods** (水神) and **Water Dragons** (水龙),
As well as the **Water Officials** (水中君官),
**Generals and Spirit Ministers** (将军灵吏),
And all **fish, scales, and beasts** (鱼鳞兽等).
They will assist the **Dao** and protect your person,
Help your family and realm,
And aid all living beings.

Fifth, it grants communion to **guard and shield** (通感卫) the person.
If one persistently cultivates and practices it,
One’s body and family will transcend the **Five Phases** (五行),
And achieve eternal harmony.
It removes the **Five Sufferings** (五苦),
**Eight Hardships** (八难),
And **Nine Calamities** (九厄),
And all diseases will naturally vanish.
One will rise above the **Three Realms** (三界),
Attain **Long Life** (长生),
And command the **Three Officials of Heaven, Earth, and Water** (天地水三官神灵),
With distinct and clear results.

Sixth, it grants communion to **command the Seven Stars of the Northern Dipper** (七星北斗君),
**Divine Consorts and Ladies** (神妃后女),
*Note: Within the Northern Dipper (北斗), there is one Principal Lady (正后),
Three Consorts (三妃),
Two Ladies-in-Waiting (二夫人),
And two Delicate Damsels (并二娇女),
All holding titles as the Seven Officials of the Northern Dipper (北斗之七君位号).*
And others, to oversee the **register of human deaths** (主世人之死簿).
When people learn of this,
They often take **Six Jia Days** (六甲日) to create diagrams,
First following the **Earthly Measure** (地纪),
Then the **Heavenly Measure** (天纲),
And finally the **Yǔ Steps** (禹步).
*Note: The Three Measures (三等) correspond to the Three Elements (三元数).*
Common folk follow the **Heavenly Measure** (步纲),
Using the **Earthly Measure** (地纪) as the **Upper Element** (上元).
Immortals follow the **Heavenly Measure** (步纲),
Using the **Heavenly Measure** (天纲) as the **Upper Element** (上元).
As **Yǐn Shòu** (尹寿子) said:
*"For common folk, whose bodies have not yet transcended the Three Realms (三界),
They follow the Earthly Measure (地纪) first,
Thus making it the Upper Element (上元).
For Immortals, whose bodies have transcended the Three Realms of Water, Fire, and Earth (水火三界),
They follow the Heavenly Measure (天纲) first,
Thus making it the Upper Element (上元).
Moreover, the practice of the Heavenly Measure (步纲法),
Must be completed in three full sets of steps,
Called the Heavenly Measure Steps (步纲数).
This is referred to as the **Heavenly, Earthly, and Human** (天地人),
Which corresponds to the method of transcending the Three Realms and Three Calamities (三界三灾),
And entering the path of **Divine Immortality** (神仙),
The **Dao of Long Life and Non-Death** (长生不死之道).
There is a secret formula within the *Líu Zhū Shàng Yǐn* (流珠上引).
*Note: The formula is found in the first volume of the *Líu Zhū Shàng Yǐn* (流珠上引).*
All who learn the **Dao** (学道者),
Should understand this principle,
And thus know the **Six Jia’s Six Powers** (六甲六通),
To transcend the Three Realms of Water and Fire (离水火三界之法),
And avoid the calamities of the **Seven Mansions** (去七宿之灾害).
*Note: The Southern Dipper (南斗) oversees the vital qi (王炁) of all people,
Causing them to attain early birth, longevity, and prosperity (早得生荣长年),
And wishes that people do not die.
The Northern Dipper (北斗) oversees the declining qi (衰炁) of all people,
Causing them to fall ill early and die from severe disease (早得疾病，病极而死).
The later Sage Emperor (后圣君) greatly abhorred this,
Thus he reversed the roles of the Northern and Southern Dippers (前后易身出世),
And revealed the **Divine Talismans and Secret Dao** (告命灵符秘法),
Interpreting the *Jīn Suǒ Líu Zhū* (金锁流珠) as a new name,
Changing the old terminology of *Jīn Luó* (金箓),
Clarifying the method of following the Heavenly and Earthly Measures (明出天纲地纪步蹑之道),
To subdue and control the **six yin deities of the Northern Dipper** (制伏北斗中六阴之神灾害炁),
Eternally attaining the **Dao of Long Life and Divine Immortality** (永出长生仙道),
And avoiding the influence of the Northern Dipper (得离北斗之下).
When common folk encounter this,
They all know to practice and cultivate it.
If they do so with sincerity and achieve results,
The six yin deities of the Northern Dipper—
The **Consorts, Ladies, and Delicate Damsels** (神君妃后娇女等)—
Will fear and submit to their commands,
Using them as **divine garments** (为衣),
And following their hand gestures to open the **Heavenly Gate** (转天关),
Subduing all **Heavenly Demons and Earthly Conflicts** (摄天魔地祆).
This is what the later Sage Emperor (后圣君) taught in his great transmission.
It allows one to attain the Dao (得道),
And ascend to the heavens (上升云天).

**Laozi, the Most High Sage** (太上老君),
Explained the **Secret Talismans of the Six Jia** (六甲秘符文) as follows:
*"I practiced the Six Jia Talismans (服六甲符),
First receiving the **Preceptor’s Instructions** (先师令服授文).
For sixty days (六十日),
I gradually began to understand.
After one hundred and twenty days (一百二十日),
All hundred diseases retreated (百病退).
After two hundred and forty days (二百四十日),
All hundred diseases were eliminated (百病消除)."*」

「Three hundred and sixty days,
The **Celestial Maiden** (玉女) attends and guards the **soul and vital essence** (魂魄),
Often appearing in dreams as if in person.

At one thousand days,
The Celestial Maiden will manifest during the day,
Guarding both the **Divine Essence** (神) and the **Divine Officials** (官).
*Note: There are often signs of spiritual efficacy and verification (灵瑞征验事), which are not limited to this account.*

At two thousand days,
The talisman’s efficacy manifests—
The body enters the realm of the **Immortal Deities** (神仙),
And the Divine Essence appears as a human being,
Often seen in person.

But the spoken words (言) are only for the self;
The body does not often appear.
The **Polarity** (冲) is near to humanity.
*Note: According to this, Laozi does not often appear in human form,
But is seen through the talismans of soldiers, officials, and Celestial Maidens (玉童玉女等).
Fearful that people might doubt his words,
And slander him as a demon (妖), destroying the true Dao,
Hence the transmission through generations.*

Thus, the **Direct Transmission of the Single Mind** (正一心直) is passed down,
Entering the **Way of Non-Action** (无为之道),
Free from confusion and perversity (无惑无邪),
Free from error and loss (无非无失),
Attaining **Oneness** (得一者也).

At three thousand days,
The Six Jia Celestial Maidens (六甲玉女) often appear in person.

After fourteen years,
One ascends to the heavens (上升天),
Entering the **Shaking Light** (摇光),
And bowing to the **Big Dipper** (北斗).
*Note: When a person’s steps align with the Dao (步纲得道),
They must first ascend to the Big Dipper’s realm (北斗),
Then enter the heavenly palaces (天宫).
Hence, the Big Dipper must welcome this person,
And the phrase "entering the Shaking Light, bowing to the Big Dipper" (入摇光，低昂北斗) is used.*

The Big Dipper **lowers once** (北斗一为低),
And the Shaking Light **welcomes below** (摇光之下迎).

Laozi says:
*"If one wishes to tread the **Seven Stars** (步七星),
The Six Jia must first be perfected."*

*Note: For humans, the soul and vital essence (魂魄) all fear the Big Dipper (北斗).
Thus, those who swallow talismans and practice the Six Jia (吞符服六甲)
Can be reborn in humanity,
And the soul and vital essence no longer fear the Big Dipper.
Hence, the Six Jia can bring rebirth in humanity (生於人),
And the soul no longer fears it,
Yet still fears the Big Dipper.
Therefore, the Sage Emperors of each generation (代代圣人)
Intended this as a means to align with the Dao (为纲步之一),
So that the soul and vital essence do not fear it.*

To **subdue the Big Dipper** (伏北斗),
Use them as **divine garments** (为之衣),
And command them as if they were obedient servants (如从仆),
Respecting them like kin (敬之如兄妹).

To tread the **Nine Steps** (步九迹),
The Six Jia must first be **accumulated** (先积).
*Note: "Accumulated" (积) refers to the practice of swallowing talismans and cultivating (服符修行积).
All are functions of the Six Jia.*

The Six Jia have three ranks of **Divine Armies** (三等军),
And also three ranks of **Divine Offices** (三等府院).
*Note: The Divine Offices (府院) resemble the three ranks of armies (三军营),
And there are also three ranks of offices.*

The highest rank is the **Supreme Unity Office of the Upper Element** (上元太一府),
The Six Jia **Divine Army** (六甲军).
*Note: Within the Supreme Ultimate (太极),
This is called the Heavenly Upper (天上),
The Six Jia Divine Army’s encampment and office (六甲军营府).*

With three **Divine Generals** (三官将) overseeing,
The generals and their subordinates—Celestial Maidens and Maidens (玉童玉女)—
Are named as recorded in *Laozi’s Secret Talismans of the Six Jia* (《老君六甲秘符箓》).

The **soldiers** (兵士) number **three million six hundred thousand** (三百六十万人众),
To subdue the **inverted forces of Yin-Yang and the Five Phases** (阴阳五行之逆炁).
Hence, they are stationed in the Supreme Unity Office (上太一之府),
The **Upper Divine Official of the True Middle** (上真中官),
The **Middle Divine Official of the River Source** (中镇河源),
And the **Lower Divine Official of Humanity** (下镇人世),
So that the four seasons follow their commands without error (四时行令不失),
And the Five Phases transform in accordance with their due times (五行变化得时).

The **Supreme Unity Messenger** (太一使者) commands one army,
The **Upper Divine Official of the Heavenly Palace** (上镇天宫),
To subdue demons and protect those who attain the Dao (保举得道之人).

The Supreme Unity Messenger (太一使者)
Each year presents **three offerings** (三奏) to the **Supreme Daoist Sovereign** (太上道君)
And the **Later Sage Emperor** (后圣君).

The **Heavenly Master** (天师) says:
*"The highest rank of Laozi’s Six Jia (上等老君六甲) is one Sovereign (一君),
Assisting and guarding at the **Golden Threshold of the Later Sage Emperor** (太平金阙后圣玉皇上道君殿)
On the left staircase below (左阶下立).*
*Note: Like the worldly sovereign (世天子),
They stand in the proper court assemblies (会立正朝之卿),
With left and right distinctions.*

Each year, they hold **three great assemblies** (三大朝),
Raising the **flags and banners of the Immortal Deities** (仙真旗仗旌节),
Commanding the **Divine Forces of Demons** (魔威神) to restrain the hearts of ghosts (制鬼之心),
So that they submit to the **Daoic威** (道威),
And the **Ten Heavens** (十天) are properly revered by gods, humans, and deities (天地人神),
The **Dragons and Ghosts** (龙鬼) subdue demons (制魔),
And protect those who attain the Dao (保举有道),
Eliminating faults and transgressions (消伏愆过).

Within one year,
There are three assemblies of reverence and offering.
*Note: The first assembly (上元) is on the fifteenth day of the first month (正月十五日).
The second assembly (中元) is on the fifteenth day of the seventh month (七月十五日).
The third assembly (下元) is on the fifteenth day of the tenth month (十月十五日).
In one year, these three days (三日)
Are when the gods of the Ten Heavens, the Five Phases, the Six Jia (十天之内，三元五行六甲等),
And the Immortal Deities’ officers and soldiers (神人真仙官兵将玉童玉女等)
All, one by one, follow the **Heavenly True Immortal Sovereign** (天真大仙),
Assisting and guarding in the assemblies before the **Later Sage Emperor’s Heavenly Palace** (玉皇上道君殿前),
To inspect the Ten Heavens (明检十天),
Driving and dividing left and right (驱分左右),
Marking those with intent (点记有心),
And before them, the true cultivators who have attained the Dao (前言成道之真人),
Their number seen in the present and future,
And afterward, they inspect the living populace (后检生民).

Within the Ten Heavens,
All good and evil deeds and merits are reported to the Jade Emperor (玉皇).
The Jade Emperor then commands the **Three Officials** (三官),
Each to subdue the wicked and evil (制伏凶恶),
To record the fate of life and death (令部生死),
To entrust the inspection of the virtuous and foolish (托受巡内贤愚),
To judge and classify crimes and goodness (分判罪善),
And to maintain fairness and equality (允其平等),
Listing their records in the Ten Heavens (列记十天).

Do not allow the **rebellious hearts** (死心) to submit to the world of life and death (屈於生死世界),
And clearly entrust them to the **Divine Official of Fate** (司命).

The middle rank is the **Six Jia of the Soul’s Flight** (灵飞六甲),
Assisting and guarding at the **Golden Threshold of the Later Sage Emperor** (太平金阙后圣君玉皇上道君殿)
On the right staircase below (右阶下立).
*Note: The same as the left, in terms of timing and month.*

The lower rank is the **Yin-Yang Six Jia** (阴阳六甲),
Assigned to human life according to the **Five Phases’ correspondences** (金木水火土),
To match the **life-giving and life-subduing cycles** (得人之命),
And to correspond with the **auspicious and inauspicious timing** (相生相克之候),
Judging fortune and misfortune (候吉凶) and matching accordingly (而相匹配).
*Note: This refers to the affairs of Yin-Yang correspondence in humanity (世人夫妻水火相刑相克之事).
In practicing the Great Dao (行大道),
One naturally dissolves this cycle of subjugation (自消此相克).*

The latter two ranks of the Six Jia (右些二等六甲),
For those who study in the world (世学之人),
Knowing the methods of these three ranks of the Six Jia (三等六甲之法),
The **Six Functions of Practice and Cultivation** (六功修服步蹑)
Make all matters align with intent (万事应心),
Naturally dissolving the **Yin’s rapidity in Water and Fire** (自消阴速於水火),
And the **Yin’s attainment of longevity** (阴取长生),
Swiftly accomplished through the **Nine Steps** (疾於步蹑).
*Note: Those who speak of the Yin attaining longevity (阴取长生)
Refer to practicing the Six Jia talismans of Laozi (服老君六甲符),
And the Six Jia talismans of the Soul’s Flight (灵飞六甲符),
Accumulating their efficacy (功着更着),
And further practicing the Nine Steps to align with the Dao (步蹑天纲地纪之功着),
Swiftly achieving the **subduing of the Nine Steps** (疾成於步摄).

Thus, the highest and middle ranks of practice and cultivation (上中二等修服之功),
The first rank’s function of matching fate and destiny (一等以命运匹配),
Mutually supporting, generating, and following (相扶相生相顺),
Encourages humans to act virtuously (志人善行),
*Note: The lower rank has its own distinct function,
As mentioned earlier in the passage regarding the Five Phases (下等别自有引，在上巷中言五行).*

And to establish the **Way of Longevity** (立入长生).

The second rank is the **Six Jia of the Soul’s Flight, Supreme Unity Office of the Upper Element** (灵飞六甲上元正一府),
Called the **Six Jia Divine Army of the Soul’s Flight** (灵飞六甲军).

The **encampment and its officers** (右营营中官将),
Are the same as those of the left office (一同左府具),」

「*Note:* The **encampment and its officers**, soldiers, and ranks
Are identical to those of the **Left Office of Laozi’s Six Jia Divine Army** (左老君六甲軍營官品人數是也).
Only the **Ten Pure Ones of the Jade Maiden** (玉女一旬十人直) serve directly under the **sacred ordination** (經箓).
Moreover, within the **Six Jia Inner Talismans of Laozi** (老君內符六甲), one attends per decade (一旬一人), the Jade Maiden’s direct retinue (玉女直也).
Two **Decade Commanders** (旬將二人) oversee them.

The **Jade Maiden of the Six Jia Soul’s Flight** (靈飛六甲玉女)
Is the **Ten Pure Ones** (即十人直),
Yet lacks a **Divine Commander** (神將) to serve under the sacred ordination (當直經箓).

However, those in the world who study the **Dao** (學道之者),
All remain unaware of this **method of the Six Jia Left and Right Armies** (六甲左右軍之法).
Thus, their distance from the **Dao** grows (去道漸遠),
And they do not know by which **gateway** (門) to enter and see the **Way** (道).

This **gateway** (門) has been known by the **ancient sages and later saints** (前聖後聖),
All of whom attained the **Dao** (道) through this very path (皆因此門成道).
Yet the common world knows only the **Ge lineage** (葛氏),
Which alone has preserved this knowledge across generations (繼代總自知之).
For though they practice the **Way of Immortality** (不死之道),
They fail to ascend to heaven (不得升天),
And are confined to the ranks of the **Immortal Officials** (仙官之位).
The **Wind** (風) continually reflects on their cultivation (修行),
Searching for those who earnestly seek the **essential gateways of the Dao** (志要門戶之人),
Yet none have truly found the proper gateways (門戶).

Even if some encounter them,
They often employ the methods too excessively (用之太多),
Or fail to follow their principles (不依其理).
Therefore, I now present the **sacred ordination** (舉箓),
To record the **true nature of the Great Dao** (大道之性),
So as to enlighten future generations (以曉後生).

The **officers, commanders, soldiers** (官將兵士) are also included.
And it is called the **Six Jia Soul’s Flight Right Army for Guarding the Dao** (靈飛六甲衛道右軍).
*Note:* The **Right Army** (右軍) refers to the **Heavenly Soldiers** (天兵).
The **Master** (師) takes **Lord Taiyi** (太一君) as the **Left Heavenly Master** (左天師),
And the **Lord** (君) as the **Right Heavenly Master** (右),
Each recording their deeds of merit and transgression (各舉功過之事).

---
**End of Volume Sixteen: The Golden Lock, Flowing Pearl Talisman Scroll** (金鎖流珠引卷之十六竟)
**End of Volume Seventeen: The Golden Lock, Flowing Pearl Talisman Scroll** (金鎖流珠引卷之十七竟)」

The **Sovereign Celestial Master** of the **Great Perfected** of **Zhonghua**, **Zaiwang Fangping Zhang Daoling**, **Zhao Shengwang**, **Chang Sishiming**, **Li Zhongfu**, **Mao Ying**, **Xu Yufu**, and others, compiled and transmitted across generations.
**Li Chunfeng**, the Daoist Immortal, annotated.

**Supreme Lord Laozi** eternally commands the **Left and Right Armies**, recording their merits and transgressions.
*Note:* Those whose merits reach **three thousand** may ascend to a **Daoist rank**. Those with **thirty offenses** are demoted one rank.
Thus, the **Three Officials** are perpetually ordered to report on **Jiazi days** in written petitions.

Among the **Six Jia officers, generals, and officials**, many falsely claim merits on **Jiazi days**.
These merits are **hidden merits** (*yīn gōng*).
There are **six hidden merits**:
*Note:*
1. Each day, **reverentially recite** before the **Celestial Worthy, Forebear Saints, the Supreme Dao Lord, the Heavenly Emperor, and the Three Sovereigns**.
   These merits are **spoken**—when receiving the **precepts**, one must **verbally inquire** and **memorize** them from the Master’s **oral instructions**. Do not forget—this is the **first secret method**.
   Without this method, even **hundreds of rituals** are meaningless.
   If one does not follow the proper order, the **Heavenly Tribunals** will not record their deeds.
   One must **receive the Master’s oral instructions** and **embody them** in both **mind and body**.
   Upon completion, **swallow the talisman**, and the merits will be **recorded in Heaven**.

   Each merit is **counted individually**, and their **reports never cease**.
   Now, I enumerate the **hidden merits and hidden virtues**, as well as the **manifest merits and manifest virtues**, all clearly laid out.

   There are **seven墨书 (*mòshū*)**—granted by the **Forebear Saint, the Supreme Emperor of the Great Dao**, to those **whose fate aligns with Dao**.
   *Note:* The **Forebear Saint** refers to **Supreme Lord Laozi**.
   **朱书 (*zhūshū*)** are granted by the **Later Saint, the Jade Emperor of the Supreme Dao**, to those **whose fate aligns with Truth**.
   *Note:* When a Master transmits the **precepts**, one must **carefully test the disciple**, observing their **nature and disposition**.
   If they possess **excessive manifest merits**, they should not be **recklessly granted** the **precepts**.

   Among the **hidden merits**, there are **three**:
   The **Forebear Saint** granted them to the **Three Sovereigns** and the **Forty-Nine True Persons**, all attaining **Daoist immortality**.
   The first is: **After receiving the Dao**, internally cultivate with **sincere heart**, healing the **suffering of all beings**, while **personally ingesting** the remedies.
   The second: **Six Jia officers** calculate daily merits—**prior cultivation** under **Lord Laozi’s Six Jia**, **three years of talisman ingestion**, **Dao-qi subduing the spirit**, **calming the heart-qi**, **illuminating the five viscera**, and **manifesting divine efficacy**.
   *Note:* **"Efficacy"** refers to using talismans to **test and heal** others’ calamities—those who recover are said to have **divine efficacy**. **Rescuing lives and things** counts as **meritorious efficacy**, **adding to the service of the *Lingfei Six Jia* talismans**, and **calculating the years, months, and days of cultivation**—this is the **first hidden merit**.

   The **Later Saint Lord** instructed the **Eastern Sea Qingtong Lord** and all **Heavenly and Earthly beings** to **align with** (*héwéi*).
   *Note:* **"Align with"** refers to those who, at the time of receiving this method, **had not yet attained Daoist immortality** but **aspired to cultivate**. After receiving the precepts, they **attain Dao in ten, fifteen, fourteen, eight, or nine years**, becoming **Great True Persons**.
   The **Later Saint Lord**, knowing their **nature and disposition**, grants them the title of **Great True Person**.

   The **Great True Person** says:
   *"Those who sincerely seek the Great Dao must internally cultivate **hidden merits and manifest virtues**, accumulating these **merits and virtues** to become **True Persons**.*
   *Note:* **Hidden merits and manifest virtues** are fully explained in the later annotations.
   Those who seek **Truth** must have **nature and disposition aligned with Dao**—this is not from **past karmic causes** or **pre-planted life forces**, nor is it **merely a matter of fate**.
   *Note:* **Past karmic causes** determine **official rank in life**, while **pre-planted** implies **some connection**, but if one speaks of **seeking Truth**, their **nature and disposition are lost**.
   This is called **external planting of merit-fields**, benefiting **future lives**, receiving **human rebirth**, but unrelated to **attaining Dao in this life**.
   Those who truly seek **Truth** must have **nature and disposition of a True Person**—this is **not mere speech**.
   Now, I **delineate this method** within the *Six Jia Induction Scripture*, establishing **three grades of hidden merits** and **three grades of manifest virtues**, transmitting to those of **recognized nature**.
   *Note:* **"Recognized nature"** means **knowing the Dao’s essence without delusion**, perpetually practicing **hidden virtues and hidden merits**, thus **dragons, spirits, and ghosts** fear and revere them—this is called **recognizing Truth**, succeeding as **True Persons** across generations.

   **First-grade hidden merits**: Cultivation within the **Six Jia**, practicing the **Five Phases and Three Realms’ methods**.
   *Note:* These include **talisman ingestion, sacrificial rites, petitions, and step-alignment**—each has its own **scriptures and transmitted traditions**. Though the world has these texts, none truly **record merits**.

   **Second-grade hidden merits**: Within the **Seven Stars**, **treading the Earthly Measures and Heavenly Rites**, descending the **Nine Essences**, commanding the **Nine Spirits**, donning the **Seven Battles**, dispelling the **Five Toxins**, averting the **Three Calamities**, and entering the **True Realm’s methods**.
   *Note:* Each method has its own **scriptures**; these are the **cultivation practices** detailed in the *Golden Lock, Flowing Pearl*.

   **Third-grade hidden merits**: Transforming **three, five, seven, nine**—
   *Note:* **Three** refers to the **Three Sovereigns**, **five** to the **Five Phases**, **seven** to the **Seven Stars** (Heavenly Rites and Earthly Measures), and **nine** to the **Nine True Ones**, the **Nine Ancestral Lords of the Supreme Dao Lord**.
   Internally, it explains the **step-alignment method**, the **essential key to commanding ten thousand spirits**.
   The **essential key to the *Yǔ-bù* (Turtle Steps)**.
   *Note:* **Three** refers to the **Three Sovereigns**, performing the **nine-track *Yǔ-bù***.
   **Five** refers to the **Five Phases**, using the **upper *Yǔ-bù* of the Three Fives**, or **twelve tracks**, or **fifteen tracks**—all varying the **Heavenly Rites and Earthly Measures**, primarily transmitted from **Mù Yóu’s descendants**, later refined into the *Yǔ-bù*.

   These **three grades of hidden merits** are all **granted in墨书 (*mòshū*)**, originally bestowed by the **Forebear Saint** upon **Upper Swangnu, the Three Sovereigns**, **Middle Swangnu, the Yellow Emperor and Xia Yu**, and **transmitted uninterrupted across ages**.

「The **Later Saint** then bestowed this upon the **Eastern Sea Blue Boy** and the **Lesser Lord**, and upon all the **Heavenly Lords and Great Truths** of every realm—this is the **Red Scripture**.

   The **first-grade hidden merit** has **ten conditions**.
   **Lao Jun** says: The **first condition of hidden merit** is that one may **cultivate and wear the Six Jia Armor**—beginning on the **Jiazi day**, ending on the **Guihai day**, and then repeating in cycles.
   On the **Jiazi day**, whenever the **decade is complete**, upon encountering a **Jia day**, three great talismans shall appear.
   *Note:* One is the **Jade Maiden Talisman**, one is the **Jia Straight Day Talisman**, and one is the **Jiazhou Day Officer Talisman**—all three are **swallowed whole**.

   Swallow them whole.
   Then, every day, **invoke the spirit and the decade’s lord**, the **decade’s Jade Maiden**, the **Six Ding Jade Maiden**, and the name of the deity of the **straight day**—
   *Note:* For example, on **Jiazi day**, one invokes **Wang Wenqing**.
   along with the **official ranks**, the **names of the talisman scribes**, and so forth.
   One then recites the **Forebear Saint’s Supreme Lord Lao Jun’s Longevity Spell** once, before beginning the incantation:
   *"May your hair turn black from white, and your fallen teeth regrow.
   The **spiritual efficacy** of the **Immortal Path** shall unfold—your mind shall open like the moon’s radiance.
   Ten thousand spirits shall witness your comings and goings.
   All your requests shall be granted, all your wishes fulfilled.
   You shall **ward off a hundred demons**, **dodge the Five Armies** (of calamity).
   Remove the record of your death, and inscribe you as **Dark Immortal**.
   Riding the clouds, harnessing the dragon, you shall ascend to the **Celestial Court**.
   **Swiftly, swiftly, as the command decrees!***
   After the invocation, **wear the talisman**.
   Count the **days, months, and years**—each talisman is worn without ceasing.
   This is the **daily merit**; in one year of **three hundred sixty days**, the merit shall also be **three hundred sixty**.
   Practice this merit year after year without pause, regardless of month or day—your body shall grow **unyieldingly strong**, like **gold**, impervious to all **hundred diseases**, and you shall **forever avoid decay and ruin**.
   This is the **first-grade hidden merit**, the **supreme condition** of the **Forebear Saint’s teachings**.

   The **second-grade hidden merit** is to **constantly act with compassion**, **saving people and benefiting all beings**.
   *Note:* When a person suffers from illness or is **harmed by malevolent ghosts**, use **talismans, medicine, and techniques** to rescue them, **alleviating their disease**.
   Let the **ghost be lightly exonerated**, and **separate the person from the ghost**, so they are no longer **bound by mutual grudges**.
   This is called **great merit toward humans**, **great grace toward ghosts**, whereby both **achieve mutual release and separation**, free from harm—thus named the **great merit toward humans and ghosts**.

   **Dissolving enmity and releasing grudges**, one must act with **the resolve to halt such deeds in darkness**.
   Always **determine the words of the prior person** (to be saved).
   After nightfall, **in darkness, resolve the grudge** between the person and the ghost—command them both to **retreat and repent their wrongs**, no longer plotting **vengeance or hatred**.
   Then, **perform the Yǔ-bù (Turtle Steps)**, **specialize in the Great Mountain Isolation** to sever the **two souls and spirits**, so they no longer harbor **resentment or malice**, and their **poisonous qi** shall each disperse.
   As the days and months pass, they shall naturally **dissipate their ill will**.
   Such a merit is **exquisitely subtle**, the **supreme subtlety**.
   *Note:* **Lao Jun** metaphorically describes this hidden merit—when one person knows the **Dao/Way**, they can **mediate and resolve** the **grudges and enmity of the two parties**; yet the **Dharma Master** takes the words of that person and **immediately resolves the dispute**, so that the two no longer harbor grudges—this is called **supreme merit and virtue**.
   **Trace the Heavenly Rites Diagram**, **step upon the Earthly Measures Diagram**, and perform **three cycles**—**forward, backward, and reversed**.
   Conclude with the words: *"Now, there is in **State County Village** a certain **official**, or among the **common folk**, a certain **person**."*

「Now, I invoke the **Heavenly Rites Diagram** upon the **State County Village** of the aforementioned **official** (or **common folk**),
   and the **person** whose name is [given]—together they conspire, seeking to harm each other,
   yet their plots are thwarted and they turn to **conspire and murder** one another.
   I now perform the **Yin Rites** to **sever their enmity**.
   The incantation reads: *"Let those under this curse feel no resentment,
   and may they each rejoice in taking turns to suffer.
   Let mountains and seas obstruct their paths with difficulty.
   I now turn the **Heavenly Rites Diagram**—each shall bear their due retribution.
   Those who harbor forward intentions, may their **heart and body grow cold**,
   and each must **suppress their heart** to find peace.
   Violators of this decree shall have their **soul and vital essence bound to the Heavenly Punishment Diagram**.
   The **Heavenly Punishment Diagram** is a **ritual of retribution and guilt**.
   *(The following steps are performed:)* Twelve steps to the **Right Star**,
   thirty-four steps to the **Heavenly Punishment Diagram**.
   The ancient method says: *"Two cycles—forward and backward—upon the Heavenly Rites Diagram,
   and the deed is done."*
   But now, we perform **three cycles**—forward, backward, and reversed.
   According to the **posterity’s incantation** given by the **Saintly Sovereign** to the young disciples **Xiao-tong Jun** and **Wang Jun**:
   *"Two cycles—forward and backward—are complete.
   Then, beginning from the **Sun Yang Star** at the head of the **Heavenly Rites Diagram**,
   scatter three cycles to the right."*
   When finished, **step with the left foot upon the Sun Yang Star**,
   then **step with the right foot upon the Yin Jing Star**.
   Again, first **step with the right foot upon the Xuan Ming Star**,
   then **step with the left foot upon the Dan Yuan Star**.
   Next, **step with the right foot upon the North Pole**,
   then **step with the left foot upon the Heavenly Rites Diagram**,
   and **step the right foot forward**, aligning with the left foot.
   Now, **unify and bless the qi**, saying:

   *"Metal overcomes Wood, Wood is felled by Fire.
   Water extinguishes Fire, and the **mouth of bronze** and **tongue of iron** are silenced.
   The forward-thinking one is broken, the two hearts retreat.
   The two tongues speak no more, both hearts are subdued.
   They shall not slaughter each other—
   I now summon the **Yin Forces** to constrain you two,
   and let your **grudges and enmity** cease.
   As it is decreed by the **Heavenly Mandate**."*

   When the blessing concludes, **twirl the fingers of the left and right hand’s fifth digit** for a short while.

   *Note:* The **finger joints** are fully annotated in the previous section.

   This further states: *"On the **right side of the third joint of the left hand’s fifth finger** is the **key incantation**."*
   This method is for **practitioners** to cultivate,
   so that those harboring **grudges and enmity** do not harm each other,
   nor conspire against one another’s life—
   the **self** shall act upon this.
   Or, if one fears that the other may act upon them,
   and they dread future **retribution and blame** upon their own body,
   they may **pray for obstruction and separation**, so that the other never comes again.
   *(This is done)* over **three nights**, without letting others see it.
   If seen, the **spiritual efficacy** will not manifest.

   *Note:* When a person cultivates **Yin Merits** and **Yin Virtue**,
   if their **Yin Merits** and **Yin Virtue** are not yet fulfilled,
   they will be exposed by a **Yang Person**—once seen,
   a thousand tongues will stir, and it becomes a **Yin Fault**.
   How much more so if they dare to **cultivate Yin Merits to aid others**,
   only to be **accused by Yin Officials**?
   If one **cultivates Yin Merits** for **protecting the state, safeguarding life, and rescuing others**,
   they should first perform **three cycles upon the Earthly Measures Diagram**.
   When finished, **three cycles—forward, backward, and reversed—are complete.*"

Then perform the **Flying Heavenly Ropes** three times, and upon completion, disperse with **three steps of the Nine Traces Yu Step**, striking to halt them. If fearing they will not stop, perform **twelve steps of the Yu Step** once more, then take **fifteen steps**.

Summon the **Three Marshals of Upper, Middle, and Lower** realms, each commanding **three hundred million troops**, along with the **Six Jia deities**, invoking them as in the *Hunpeng Diagram* and the *Liuzhu* [scroll]’s **Three Marshals of Yuanxia and Yuanxia-inferior** diagrams. Strike three times—all matters will dissolve, and no harm will befall that person. If done **six times**, the person will fall ill; do not act recklessly, lest your **Yin Virtue** be diminished. If done **nine times**, they will perish instantly.
*Note:* Do not act recklessly—this diminishes your **Yin Virtue**, turning it into a **Yin Fault**.

The **three grades of the Yu Step** are illustrated above in the diagrams referenced earlier. Now, with this Yu Step, you may **invoke the Mountain Barrier** to sever the enemy, following the **Array Formation Step Diagram**. Turning right once, summon the **Ninefold Mountains** to isolate their spirit and soul, so they dare not approach.

This is called the **Earthly Axis Yu Step**, invoking the **Twenty-Four Earthly Axis Deities**, opening a **one-cun** space to encompass **ten thousand li of rivers and mountains**, or **ten thousand li of rivers and mountains** condensed into a **one-cun step**. This Yu Step is subtle and profound—it can **subdue and gather** within a person’s body, allowing them to soar through the void without knowing distance.

The secret lies within the **three horizontal marks** at the base of the **left hand’s first finger**; this is the **Earth-Core Secret**. *Note:* One may also receive the teacher’s revelation of its ultimate principle, uncovering the true secret where it is exposed.

After completing the **three cycles of the Step Ropes**, pinch the **left hand’s central secret** with the right, then stamp the ground, lifting the foot to invoke the **Earth-Core Secret** and the **Earth-Inner Secret**. Then recite the incantation:

*"Heaven is clear, Earth is level,
The sun and moon move in order,
All beings thrive in harmony,
The land is ruled by a virtuous sovereign.*

Now, there is a certain person defying Heaven with clamor.
I tread the Yu Ropes’ path,
ever severing their way.
Through **thousand mountains and ten thousand chasms** they cannot pass—
to pass is to perish, body and soul undone."

Take **original-colored stone** and cast it—this will halt them.
The **original-colored stone** is found in the *Six Jia Talismans*; once seen, it is obtained.

This **Step Rope** is not merely for **Yin Merits** in saving others—if practiced daily, within **three years**, one may shorten the **Earth’s pulse**, often moving faster than flight. *Note:* In antiquity, **Master Gou** (surname **Shi**, given name **Cun**), a disciple of **Confucius**,...

With the Master Kong’s teachings,
he sought office repeatedly yet failed.
Then, gazing heavenward, he sighed:
*"My heart still yearns—
to seek the Supreme Dao, the Most Exalted,
as a minister beneath the Jade Emperor’s throne,
in the lofty halls of the Ten Thousand Clouds, the Left Palace of the Celestial Capital.
How much harder, then, to seek even a lowly official
beneath the worldly emperor’s rule—
such a thing is so rare!
Thus, I abandoned Confucian texts
and turned to the Dao, seeking a worthy teacher.*

*First, I met Master Zhao of the Western Prefecture,
and followed him as teacher, studying scriptures.
My voice chanted the rites of morning reverence—
my resolve never wavered.
For thirty-seven years,
I grew ever more enveloped in murky ignorance,
weakened by age, powerless to act.
Again, I sighed to Heaven:
‘How fortunate that Heaven granted me this foolish body—
I studied Confucianism, mastered its ways, yet gained no honor.
I sought the Dao, my heart labored in vain, my wisdom never brightened.
Was it not because my past virtues were meager,
my fate unkind?
How could I now grow old and die?’

In a sudden flash, I fainted and died.
Yet in death, I saw a woman of surpassing beauty,
who spoke to me, saying:
‘You sought the Dao but lacked a true master.
You did not cultivate wisdom with iron resolve,
nor temper your body like adamantine.
You toiled only over the Five-Colored Flower’s hidden teachings,
singing idle tunes, reciting frivolous words,
like a child playing with hollow syllables.
Your path grows ever more distant from the Dao.
If you truly wish to attain it,
abandon these ways and seek another path.
Go to Mount Shaoshi,
and find Master Jiuling—
Jiuling is the Lord Lao’s emanation.
Or some say he is Master Wang’s disciple, the Lady of the Six Jia.’

‘A mortal who cultivates meritorious deeds in secret
may now find the Dao complete—
yet you must depart swiftly, not linger.’

Thus, Shi Cun awoke
and journeyed to Mount Shaoshi,
searching for three months without success.
Yet with a pure heart, unwavering resolve,
he suddenly encountered an old man on the road—
seventy or eighty years old, with snow-white hair,
walking like a tiger, strong enough to bear another man.
Shi Cun gazed long, recognizing him as a divine being,
and hurried forward to bow in reverence.
The bystanders were astonished and asked:
‘Why do you bow to this old man?’
One among them replied:
‘When encountering a True Person, one must pay homage with haste.’

Then Jiuling Master scolded:
‘Why have you come so late?
I wished to take you to Mount Wangwu,
to pay respects to the Lady of the Six Jia.
I have waited long—
Heaven’s records have decreed
that I should instruct you in cultivating the Six Jia’s meritorious deeds,
and prescribe the talismans to heal your body.
Yet you are already old—
why did you not begin sooner?’

Shi Cun fell to the ground, kowtowing twice,
declaring he had been reborn only to meet this master.
He begged:
‘I humbly pray that the master teach me the art of immortality,
so that my wretched body may endure.
I would serve as your slave,
regardless of years or months—
only grant me this life.’

Jiuling Master then led him into Mount Wangwu,
and for three years,
taught him the method of *stepping the Celestial Halter and Earthly Measures*,
to swallow the *Six Jia’s Soul-Soaring Scriptures*,
and bestowed the *Twenty-Four Stages of the Earth’s Axis Talismans*,
always turning the Earth’s Axis and Heaven’s Gate.
After fourteen years of secret cultivation,
his Dao was complete.

He then took a jar—
a vessel of two *sheng* capacity—
which could contain the entire world beneath the Great Luo Heaven,
within the Great Polarity’s embrace,
and sealed it inside.
Or the jar was the Six Jia’s encampment,
and the *Scriptures of Qi-Sealing Arts* were its talismans,
to transmit to mortals for cultivating meritorious deeds in secret.

Was it not because his heart was most sincere
that the divine master took him as a disciple,
and guided him to attainment?

Later, he wandered the world for seven hundred years,
until the Jin Dynasty, when Fei Changfang encountered him
and learned the method of *shortening the Earth’s pulse*.
For three days, he hosted Fei in his jar to receive the teachings.
Upon returning, three years passed,
when one day, the Most Holy Jade Emperor of the Golden Threshold
sent celestial maidens to welcome him,
and he ascended to the rank of *Left Celestial Marshal*,
akin to the worldly Grand Councilor.

Truly, the Supreme Dao was fulfilled—
his wish to be granted the Celestial Marshal’s rank was answered.

**The Third Rule of Yin Merits:**
When the Dao’s power is manifest,
one observes the world—
if malevolent spirits, poisonous dragons, or demons
unleash raging winds and torrential rains,
harming all beings, whether on land or sea,
one must tread the *Celestial Halter and Earthly Measures*
three times each, as described in the *Diagram of Stepping Heaven and Earth’s Measures*.
Dissolve into the *Yugbu Steps*—
nine strides, twelve strides, or fifteen strides—
and always align with the Heaven’s Gate.
Raise the hand and point with three, six, or nine fingers.
*Note: Some say three times—
the poisonous spirits will then cease,
and no lives will be harmed.*

Six strikes for illness,
nine for imminent death—
do not recklessly invoke these prohibitions to kill,
for that is not the Dao.

One must first discern the truth—
if harm is being wrought by malevolent spirits,
and they act with demonic fury three or two times,
then all beings will be at peace,
and only then may the *Step-Halter Method* be applied.
The demons will then cease.

Cease and release them—
do not kill outright.
If you kill, pluck the *dragon-spirit’s vital thread* from their demonic beasts—
the beasts will die within three days.

Later, the Sage Monarch revealed the *Golden Lock, Flowing Pearl* manual,
where all methods for subduing dragons and beasts are recorded.
Use this to verify.

The Sage said:
‘Do not act recklessly—
those who do will harm others’ lives,
and bear guilt before all beings.
If beings are unsettled,
or lives are lost to drought or flood,
the lawful method must be applied to execute judgment.
*Note: The “Heaven’s Gate” cessation refers to the nine strikes—
this is the execution.*

To save one life and gain ten is called *double merit*.
When three thousand are saved,
one ascends to Heaven in broad daylight.
*Note: Regarding the wind, as recorded in the *Book of Jin* and *Strange Records of the Divine*,
Xu Xun served as the magistrate of Jingyang County,
yet mastered the Dao of the *Yugbu Steps*.’

The Great Serpent of Shu, with three coils,
and the Six Poisonous Dragons of the Han River,
together plagued the people as *spirits of calamity*,
blocking the river and ridges fore and aft,
seizing humans to devour.
When Heaven learned of this,
Xu Xun’s *Dao/Way* was perfected in the *Yugbu Steps*,
and he treaded the *Yugbu Steps’* path,
turning the *Heaven’s Gate* strike—
he captured and slew them.
He did not exceed the *nine strikes’* limit on *spirits of calamity*,
yet saved over ten thousand lives.

This serpent appeared in a dream to the Jin Emperor:
*"I now consume the people of Jianghuai—fifteen hundred thousand."*

The Jin Emperor was greatly alarmed.
Within two years,
Xu Xun alone received the *irresistible execution* decree,
and was posthumously honored as a *rightfully appointed* magistrate.
He declined the title, refusing to accept it.

The *Earthly Tribunals* reported to the *Heavenly Court*,
the *Heavenly Court* to the *Celestial Sovereign*,
the *Golden Threshold of Great Peace* to the *Jade Sovereign of the Later Saints*,
who dispatched an envoy to welcome Xu Xun.
He was granted *ascension in broad daylight*,
and his household was lifted from their homes to depart this world.

Thus, his killing was without blame,
and he earned *hidden merit*.
Again, if there are *refined spirits* or *malevolent spirits of calamity*
plaguing people,
binding them across generations without release,
or if they are *yin-precise* malevolent spirits,
causing illness and death among the populace,
unrest in homes,
and widespread suffering,
with no end in sight—
this follows the *符命* (divine mandate) of the *Supreme Venerable Lord Lao*,
using the *符* (talisman) to heal diseases,
and the afflicted recover.

Turning the *Heaven’s Gate* strike—
the *nine degrees* of the *irresistible execution*,
and saving those on duty for the *Six Jia* (days) and their corresponding *directing officials*,
as well as the *attendant officials*, *talisman scribes*, etc.—
urgently summon and compel them.

Thus, the healing talismans can transform into *spirits* or *officials*,
beheading those malevolent spirits,
and the illness is immediately cured.
Such deeds are *most exalted* in Heaven,
and the *Jade Sovereign* rejoices from afar.
Keep this secret—do not use it recklessly.

**Right: The Three *Yin-Functions* of the Six Jia.**
The remaining seven are in the Fourteenth Volume.

---
*End of the Golden Lock, Flowing Pearl Manual, Volume Seventeen.*
*Begin the Golden Lock, Flowing Pearl Manual, Volume Eighteen.*

**Fourth Condition of the Six Jia Yin-Functions**

The Most High Lord of the Dao, the Sovereign of the Great Perfection, Zhai Wang Fangping, Zhang Daoling, Zhao Shengwang, the Long Official Li Zhongfu, Mao Ying, Xu Yufu, and others, compiled this in succession.
The Daoist Master Li Chunfeng annotated it.

The Lord Lao said:
*"Those who study the Dao and cultivate in the world—when their Daoist practices are refined and their talismanic power is perfected—
suddenly, if commoners or officials fall ill with epidemic pestilence, miasma-induced sickness, or contagious disease, causing death or injury among the afflicted,
one may pinch the *pestilence spirit’s eye*,
take nine *Yujia steps* in three strides,
align with the *Heaven’s Gate*,
and point toward the sick person’s dwelling in a certain direction—
three times.
Then, one may issue the talisman,
saving each afflicted person instantly.*

*If a household of ten has three, four, or five stricken, near death,
they may swallow the talisman and recover immediately.*

*Those not yet sick may wear one talisman,
ensuring none in the household contract the illness—
the sick recover, the healthy remain untainted.
A household of ten earns ten merits;
a household of twenty, twenty merits.
This is the supreme Yin-Function of the talismanic method.*

*Keep this secret—do not recklessly transmit it to the unworthy.*

*This is the tenth condition of merit.
Its efficacy is verified,
and the Later Sage Emperor bestowed this chapter
upon the Six Jia and their consorts.
The chapter is in *The Flowing Pearl: Upper Section*.*

*The Later Sage Emperor instructed the Heavenly Master Zhang Daoling:
‘Among the Six Jia, the tenth condition of merit—
the talisman that exorcises pestilence spirits and saves lives—
is of great power.
You and your disciples must observe the world:
if any are afflicted, treat them urgently.
The people fear this sickness greatly,
yet few can cure it.
When they see their lives saved, they will rejoice,
praising the marvelous efficacy—
worthy of Heaven’s hearing.
All sins of bodily obstruction shall be erased.
Guard this treasure carefully—do not reveal it to the unworthy.*

*Before Master Zhang Daoling practiced this method,
when Chinese people sought treatment from foreign masters,
those who went perished with their entire households—
not even minor exorcisms could save them.*

*Note: In the past, a third-generation foreign master entered China
and attempted to exorcise this spirit.
The spirit resisted,
and its qi struck him down.
This is fully recorded in *The Flowing Pearl: Middle Section*—
no need to repeat it here.*

*The pestilence spirit’s *eye* is located on the left hand’s fourth finger, third joint.
To the right of the joint, near the fingernail,
lies the *pestilence spirit’s blade*—
if struck, the spirit dies within three days.
This is highly verified.*

*In antiquity, Zuo Ci, styled Yuanfang, of Jiangdong,
was skilled in restraining spirits.
When Wei Wen Di heard of him, he commanded the exorcism of pestilence spirits.
The spirits, weeping, said to one another:
‘The Jiangdong Master Zuo will pinch our eyes with copper claws—
we must leave.
If we do not, he will strike us with his blade—
we will die immediately.’
They wept and departed together.
Within three days, all illnesses in the palace vanished,
the healthy remained untainted,
and none contracted the sickness.*

*The Most High Lord Lao bestowed the *Eight Barbarian Scriptures*,
which contain talismanic officials to subdue spirits.
Preserve them as in the diagram—
the pestilence spirits will flee.
If they do not flee, they will die.
This is highly verified."*

The fifth *yin* virtue: The Most High Lord Lao said: *"Those who cultivate the Dao with a focused mind must take compassion as their foundation, rescuing and delivering all beings as their primary purpose, and subduing evil while establishing the rectified qi as their intent. If there is evil, the rectified qi cannot flow or descend. If one can employ talismans and medicines to treat malevolent spirits without harming the rectified, then even those whose hearts are steeped in evil may be given one or two talismans to swallow and purify them. For those afflicted with chronic evil illnesses—lingering, dim-witted, and enfeebled for ten or five years—these are the spirits of old *lao* (precocious) ghosts and demons, fox, weasel, or rat *jing* (essence-spirits). They may be pursued and beheaded with talismans without hesitation. Saving one person earns one virtue; exterminating a spirit earns two virtues.

The method for extermination involves reciting the *Di Ji* (Earth Memorization) once and the *Fei Tian Gang* (Flying Heaven Rope) once. Then, perform the *Yu Bu* (Flood Step) nine times, align with the *Pei Yi* (Configuring Garment) of the Seven Stars, turn the *Tian Guan* (Heavenly Lock), and point toward a specific village or household in a certain place. With three six nines (27) finger-pointings, summon the Six Generals of the Middle and Lower *Yuan* (Origins) to that person’s residence, commanding them to unleash water and fire, leading three hundred million troops as depicted in the diagram. If the Three Generals of the Middle *Yuan* are invoked from the *Liu Zhu Zhong Wai Pian* (Flowing Pearl Inner and Outer Chapters), they will arrive at the door to capture and exterminate the ghost, circling the residence with a great shout. Often, after three such invocations, the spirit will die, and the illness will abate. This *yin* virtue is also great, and the world will revere it.*

The sixth *yin* virtue: When a practitioner’s cultivation is complete, they may sit and rescue those thousands of miles away. With a talisman, they can save people in battle, binding it to a person’s body to ward off blades and swords, preventing harm. On a *Liu Jia* (Six Jia) day, one may invoke the *Liu Jia* deities, take three steps of the *Yu Bu* (nine traces), align with the *Pei Yi*, and point three times with the hand. This grants the *Xing Jun Huo Fu* (Marching Army Fire Talisman) and the *Dai Jue* (Bound Avoidance), ensuring the wearer will never be harmed by bandits. If a great general seeks to annihilate enemy forces for the state, they may be given the *Wan Sheng Shen Fu* (Ten-Thousand Victory Divine Talisman) to bind, rendering blades and swords powerless to harm.

For those commanding armies to strengthen the state, one may recite the *Di Ji* nine times, the *Fei Tian Gang* three times, disperse the *Yu Bu* in nine traces three times, twelve traces three times, and fifteen traces three times. Then align with the *Pei Yi*, turn the *Tian Guan*, and point toward the enemy’s direction nine times, pinching the *dao zhi* (claw support) of the person in that direction.
*Note: If the enemy is in the East (Wood), use the Wood-person *dao zhi*; West (Metal), Metal-person *dao zhi*; South (Fire), Fire-person *dao zhi*; North (Water), Water-person *dao zhi*; Seasons (Earth), Earth-person *dao zhi*. Alternatively, one may also correspond with the Five Phases (Metal, Water, Wood, Fire, Earth) as needed.*

These two methods are the same. Additionally, sprinkle water in accordance with the direction, and the enemy will self-destruct. This method must be kept secret and not used recklessly. The ancient sage-kings revealed this method to save those who cultivate the Dao, aiding them in times of difficulty and assisting Daoist states in peril. It must not be used lightly—without proper mandate, even a moment’s misuse is forbidden.

The ancient sage-kings further instructed: *"Realgar of a red hue—write the two *Da Jie* (Great Calamity) talismans, which are detailed in the *Li Fa* (Ritual Method). Also write the *Ru Jun Fu* (Entering Army Talisman) and the six *Liu Jia Yin Fu* (Six Jia Yin Talismans), binding them to the soldiers. In battle, they will suffer no injury for every ten thousand. These talismans are found in the *Liu Zhu Zhong Wai Pian* military methods."*

The seventh *yin* virtue: If the heavens endure prolonged rain without ceasing, and floods devastate the people—drowning villages, towns, and individuals—one may, in secret at night, recite the *Di Ji* three times and the *Fei Tian Gang* three times. Then disperse into the *Yu Bu* of nine traces, reaching twelve and fifteen traces, align with the *Pei Yi*, turn the *Tian Guan*, and point three times toward the darkest clouds. After three repetitions, issue a talisman to the local shrine, stipulating a specific day and hour for the rain to cease. If it does, pinch the *Long Mu* (Dragon’s Eye).
*Note: The eye is on the left side of the second joint of the left hand’s index finger, near the claw nail. Pinch it urgently.*

The eighth *yin* virtue: If the heavens withhold rain for too long, caused by the *Kang Long* (Proud Dragon), and crops wither and die—unless this drought is a heavenly decree—
*Note: If the drought is a heavenly command, do not act recklessly, lest you harm the Dragon’s mandate. The heavens punish the Dragon, and retribution follows naturally.*

If the drought is caused by the *Tu Di Long Shen* (Earthly Land Dragon Spirit) refusing to rain, one may, at night in an unoccupied courtyard, recite the *Di Ji* and *Fei Tian Gang* each three times, disperse into the *Yu Bu* of three steps and nine traces three times, align with the *Pei Yi*, turn the *Tian Guan*, and point three times toward a deep pool.
*Note: The pool must contain dragons or water deities, the officials of the Water Palace, to ensure immediate efficacy and swift rain as urgent as fire.*

At dawn, write the *Zhi Ri Fu* (Direct Day Talisman) and the *Jiu Long Shui Fu* (Nine Dragons Water Talisman), affixing them to the local shrine and land gods.
*Note: In ancient times, there were no *Cheng Huang* (City Gods); today, one must first invoke the City God officials and the land boundary shrine and water palace spirit officials, along with the Direct Day deity, to assemble the assembly and command the rain to fall at the appointed time. Urgently, as the law decrees. The deities will swiftly cause the rain to fall within the stipulated days, nourishing all rivers and streams, fulfilling the oath of hand and mouth.*

The Most High Lord Lao said: *"I have transmitted this method to the world, so that those who cultivate the Dao may save others and achieve great merit. Those who save all under heaven will attain peace and joy beyond measure. This virtue is unfathomable, and those who uphold it will ascend the ranks of the immortals. This eighth virtue is what all sages and true ones have long kept in mind for those who earnestly study. Mastering this method and accumulating merit leads directly to the Dao.

The later sage-kings further transmitted the three *Long Fu* (Dragon Talismans), including the second method of the *Liu Jia Lu* (Six Jia Scriptures) and the talisman of the *Zhi Ri Shen* (Direct Day Deity)."*

「Annotation: Within the *Six Jia Scriptures*, the method is selected as follows: One talisman is used to summon the Dragon Talismans, in accordance with the law, swiftly as water and fire. The Dragon Talisman is invoked by the *Long Jue* (Dragon Decision), located on the left hand’s second finger at its first joint.

The Most High Lord Lao said: *"Those who earnestly cultivate the Dao and seek verification must first understand this method of employing the Way to subdue dragons and enslave ghosts. Those who fail to grasp it will drift ever farther from the Dao, and must not presume to practice it. This method aids and assists the human body. I observe that in the present age, those who study the Dao merely take sound and image as the Dao.

Annotation: The wind carries the teachings of the ancient *Wu Wei* (Non-Action) Dao; now, they have entered the realm of *You Wei* (Action).

Nowadays, when people hear the Dao’s teachings, their ears and eyes are filled with devotion, and when they see its symbols, their hearts and spirits rise in faith. Though they may briefly awaken to goodness, their actions do not align with the Dao’s source, nor with the Dao itself. They merely labor at constructing mountains of merit that span the skies, only to exhaust themselves in vain and dissipate their efforts. Thus, the truly wise do not take sound and image as their instruction.

This is the hollow merit of the petty-minded, who vainly practice in the world. To recognize one’s true nature as *virtue* (德),—

Annotation: Lord Lao’s words here instruct the students, stating that in the present age, people mistake the forced cultivation of knowledge and true nature as the heart of *You Wei* (Action) virtue, rather than the natural virtue of *Wu Wei* (Non-Action). Throughout their lives, they exhaust themselves in futile, arduous striving. Such people, though the world may count them by the ten-thousand, will not achieve a single success. I often lament this, hence I have left ten conditions of hidden merit, and this is the foremost.

In the time of the ancient sage-king Shun, there was a drought lasting one hundred days. The emperor commanded his ministers to pray for rain. After fifty days, the sun’s midday heat scorched people with thirst and want, and many died—spread across all nine regions, with mountains blazing, grasses withering, and stones glowing like embers, making it unbearable for people to stand. Suddenly, two immortals arrived, and one sighed: *"What kind of people are these, finding joy in such agonizing heat? Why?"*

The other replied: *"Let us pray for rain to descend."*

The immortal said: *"Rain is the dragon’s movement; why should it concern your prayers?"*

The official answered: *"We pray that the dragon descends and moves to bring rain."*

The immortal asked: *"Do you recognize the dragon?"*

The official said: *"I recognize it."*

The immortal then said: *"Since you recognize the dragon, where is it? Why do you pray for its rain?"*

At this, the officials knelt in unison, asking the immortal to indicate the dragon’s whereabouts. The immortal suddenly pointed at one man’s foot, and the dragon moved with tiger-like strides—

Annotation: The act of pointing with the hand is the turning of the Celestial Gate.

The man’s foot became the dragon’s and tiger’s steps, resembling the *Wu Bu* (Avoiding Steps) of today. After three strides, the immortal shouted: *"Why does the dragon not move to bring rain?"*

At that moment, the dragon bowed and said: *"The Celestial Sovereign forbids rain for one hundred and eighty days. I have already twice secretly brought rain to save people, but both times I was summoned by the Underworld to report. This time, I dare not move, for if I do, I will be summoned, and my transgression will be heard by the Supreme Deity. The Celestial Talisman will descend to punish my body as a dragon."*

The immortal immediately sought paper and brush, writing a Celestial Talisman decree. He affixed it to the shrine deities and the dragon, commanding them to bring rain together. At that time, the shrine deities and the dragon, having received the decree, brought rain as ordered, and the limit was fulfilled within one day.

Annotation: Though the limit was fulfilled within one day, this method is too harsh. The dragon and deities, in their urgency to bring rain, must use violent winds and torrential downpours, uprooting trees. The immortal’s original intent was to secretly bring rain, but fearing that the Celestial Sovereign might forbid it and assign all the blame to the dragon, he ordered the storm to be swift. If the Celestial Sovereign did not punish the dragon, it would be spared. If he did punish it, the immortal feared damage to the dragon. At that time, the dragon was not punished, which was due to the immortal’s compassion, saving all beings in the world. Thus, the Celestial Sovereign did not blame the dragon. Instead, he rewarded the shrine deities, the dragon deities, and the eight departments of the river and sea spirits, granting them promotions. From then on, all of them thanked the immortal one by one.

Now, if one obtains this method, the rain limit is set within three to five days, and this is already considered a great merit. Both the deities and the people rejoice, and according to the limit, the rain will be fulfilled, and promotions will follow. The merit’s efficacy lies with the Daoist master, who assesses the merit and may bestow rewards of wine and music.

Later, there are three *Hui* (Assembly) days, where separate offerings are made to declare the merit’s efficacy.

Annotation: There is a method that does not require offerings; one simply submits the merit declaration and petition. This is not permissible. The three Assembly days are the days of the grand *Jiao* (Offering), when one must set up generals, officials, and soldiers, as if the world’s emperor commands his vassals and ministers, overseeing the three armies in a similar manner. Each year, these rites must be performed in spring and winter; failure to do so violates the imperial command. This is the *San Yuan Lu* (Three Primordial Scriptures), which takes the Three Primordial days for the offering, along with one petition and merit declaration. It is not necessary to submit all petitions and documents, lest they trouble the Supreme Deity and Lord of the Dao.

The ninth condition of hidden merit: The Most High Lord Lao instructed the male *Zhen Ren* (True Persons) like *Zhen Wang* (True King) Fang Ping and Han Fei Zheng, and the female *Zhen Ren* like Li the Lady, Wang the Lady, and the Lady of *Zi Wei* (Purple Micro), among the seventy-two great *Zhen Ren*, saying: *"In the world, those who earnestly cultivate hidden merit must strive for the greatest deeds—none surpass saving people and aiding the poor, nor honoring the spirits of the dead and repairing tombs.

Annotation: The honoring of tombs refers to the ancient Yellow Emperor, who during his inspection of Mount Tai encountered a buried corpse whose coffin had been washed away by water, causing the earth to collapse and expose thousands of skeletal remains. The emperor, moved by the suffering of the common people, had them all collected and placed between four large boards, with the space taken from an uninhabited highland and buried in a deep pit. He then built a mound of earth three feet high, naming it a *fen* (tomb). After this, people followed the Yellow Emperor’s example. This burial method involved four large boards, isolating the four sides of the earth, and one large board placed above as a cover—this was the method of constructing tombs. Even to this day, people use coffins as boards and *guo* (outer coffins), adding new embellishments and calling them *mu* (graves).

In his dreams, the emperor saw over a thousand people come to thank him, saying: *"Your Majesty governs the living with the Dao and the dead with virtue. Now, we, your subjects—over a thousand seven hundred in number—have been granted your celestial mercy. You provided shelter for our exposed bones, and we have already yesterday petitioned the Celestial Bureau, stating that we were blessed by your Majesty’s mercy in relocating and burying our remains. The Bureau has rewarded your Majesty’s deeds with double merit."*」

From this point onward, forty-five years passed, and the sun ascended into the clouds of heaven by day—he was indeed to become a supreme true immortal. Later, as foretold, he attained divine communion.

**Annotation:** *Huangdi’s Original Chapter* records the method of erecting tombs and burying the dead to teach the world. When people learned this, their merit spread across the world, delighting gods and ghosts. After death, some with strong and wise spirits became celestial deities, earth deities, deities of the soil, or deities of grain, while the weaker became ghosts. Among ghosts, there were three ranks: superior, middle, and inferior.

The superior ghosts bestow blessings upon the virtuous and repay human kindness. The middle ghosts neither bless nor harm. These two ranks, if they attain rebirth early, are called *shan gui* (benevolent ghosts) in the retribution of human and heavenly realms. The Most High cherished them, forbidding those who received Daoist precepts from harming them, lest they lose the path to heavenly rebirth.

The inferior ghosts, however, constantly bring calamity, misfortune, and disease to the world.
