The Most High and the Sage Lords were enraged and often commanded Daoists to subdue and exterminate them with spells. Once subjected to Daoist judgment, their spirits were bound to the Northern Emperor’s dark and desolate peaks, imprisoned for years without resolution. Even if released, they could not be reborn as humans. Only those judged by the *Huai Tian* (Mars) were condemned to be reborn as venomous creatures—centipedes, scorpions, and snakes—dying a hundred times before being reborn once, never again as humans.

When the human realm rejoiced, the hundred rivers and spiritual beasts presented auspicious diagrams, while the four seas’ dragons offered pearls and jade—was this not the virtue and divine communion of the Emperor’s hidden deeds?

Again, the Celestial Worthy instructed the ascetic practitioners of bitter austerity, such as Guo Jinqing, saying: *"Your austerities save others, none greater than sowing merit. Its fruits will benefit future generations. I grant you treasures and firewood when you are in need—such deeds are vast and verifiable, leading to the Dao."*

Moreover, he taught the forging of copper and iron into counterfeit gold and silver, taking only half the price—**Annotation:** *Half the price* means that genuine gold is worth ten *guan* per *liang* (ounce), but since counterfeit gold is made of copper or iron, one *liang* could be sold for half its value, yielding 2,500 in profit per *liang*. Yet even this, the Sage Lords permitted only for the practitioner’s own sustenance—clothing, food, and household needs—and forbade reckless excess. This method was taught by the Sage Lords of old and new to those on the Daoist path, allowing them to provide for themselves and their families.

Moreover, they also used cloth and silk to make garments, feigning lost clothing along the way to give alms to the poor and the sick, thereby seeking the hidden virtue of *yin-de* (meritorious deeds unseen by others). In the past, several *zhenren* (perfected ones) practiced such deeds. This provided for their own families while also rescuing the poor and the sick—another great merit.

One must not deceive the world by falsely claiming such actions as true gold, nor should one exploit the faithful by inflating the value of treasures and rare artifacts to mislead honest people. Such crimes are grave and cannot be redeemed by seeking hidden merit. **Beware.**

**Annotation:** In the past, *Yin Changsheng* (a Daoist adept) would feign lost money to aid the destitute, thereby earning hidden merit through such deeds. Today, some falsely claim this Daoist method, deceiving common folk by saying, *"This forged gold, when refined, becomes an elixir—unmatched in the world, worthy of immortals’ alchemy."* Yet how could immortals engage in such worldly deceit?

Furthermore, immortals all practice methods of lightening the body, allowing them to transcend physical form at will. They consume elixirs of metals and minerals to achieve levitation—such claims are utterly baseless.

**The Tenth Principle of *Yin-Function* (Hidden Merit):**
A discourse on how *zhenren* (perfected ones) and their disciples practice hidden merit and its virtues.

---
*End of the Eighteenth Section: "The Golden Lock and Flowing Pearl Introduction"*

「The **Grand Daoist Sage** of the **Central Realm**, **Zaiwang** of the **Great Perfection**, **Zhang Daoling**, **Zhao Sheng**, **Wang Chang** (the **Master of Command**), **Li Zhongfu**, **Mao Ying**, **Xu Yufu**, and others, were all later disciples who compiled and expounded upon the teachings. The **Daoist Sage** **Li Chunfeng** annotated them. Below, the **Six Jia** (注: *Six Jia* refers to the six celestial stems, 甲,乙,丙,丁,戊,己, symbolizing a cycle of Daoist practices) **Yin-Function** (Hidden Merit) is discussed.

**Old Lord** (注: *Old Lord*, 老君, refers to **Laozi**, the revered Daoist sage and patriarch) instructed **Donglai Zi** (注: *Donglai Zi*, 東來子, is **Yu the Great’s** son):

*"Donglai Zi, you learned the Dao but did not practice **Yin-Function** (Hidden Merit), only **Yang-Function** (Manifest Virtue). Your craftsmanship was clever and refined—you built a tower in an empty wilderness, carving images of Daoist figures upon it, intending this as your lifelong virtue. You sought to rely on these merits to attain the Dao and transcendence. You claim that I have crafted over ten thousand merits for you, sufficient to make you a **Great Sage** (大仙).

One day, suddenly, two **Ming Officials** (注: *Ming Officials*, 二冥使, are underworld judges or messengers) summoned you to the **Gate of Tai Mountain** (太山門下), questioning why you constructed the tower, slaughtered living beings, and sacrificed them to spirits and ghosts in the rivers and wilds—countless oxen, pigs, sheep, donkeys, and other beasts. They said to you: *'Confess your crimes, or we shall bind your body and interrogate you further.'*

You replied: *'I submit to my transgressions and accept the blame for others.'* Then, I pardoned your offense.

But if you had not submitted, you would have been bound and punished. Your father had merit for managing the waters, now you are a **Tai Ji Perfected One** (太極真人), and cannot be cursed to bear the sin of killing. I shall reduce your father’s blessings to atone for your salvation, allowing you to return to the mortal world. If you now practice **Yin-Function** (Hidden Merit) to an extent surpassing others’ lifespans, you shall attain **perfected humanity** (成人), and for countless kalpas and lifetimes, you will no longer be sought by the underworld for retribution.

**Donglai Zi** responded: *'I submit.'*

Upon completion, the **Ming Official** truly consulted with **Tai Mountain Lord** (太山君), who released you from death, and you revived after seven days.

Afterward, you always acted with sincerity, never harming living beings. You frequently used your own wealth to redeem the lives of the deceased, liberating them without limit. You often did this.

Or, when people were imprisoned and bound, you would joyfully release them. Or, you would give food and clothing to those in jail.

For thirty years, those you had previously killed—oxen, sheep, pigs, donkeys, horses, and other livestock—all took rebirth as humans, forever free of resentment.

Because of these minor merits, you were favored by **Tai Shang Laozi** (太上老君), who revealed the **true teachings of Yin-Function** (Hidden Merit) to you, instructing you in the **steps of the Dao’s celestial principles** (天地纲纪之法) and granting you the **Six Jia merits** (六甲之功).

One day, suddenly, your **divine influence** (通神威) resonated with the heavens and earth, startling both mortals and immortals. **Old Lord** descended again, bestowing upon you the **Great Yin-Function** (大阴功).

You said: *'I have always been fond of constructing towers and altars, killing living beings to sacrifice to spirits and ghosts, intending this as a means to refine my body and seek the Dao.'*

*(As recounted earlier.)*

Now that the **Ming Officials** have informed you, you must reflect and repent. I shall now properly instruct you in **Yin-Function** (Hidden Merit). There are ten merits:

1. **Wearing the Six Jia True Talisman** (服六甲真符) to heal bodily ailments.
2. **True-heartedness** (真心), not causing harm or injury, not killing or wounding, not acting deceitfully or lustfully. *(注: Even if you have wives and concubines, do not arbitrarily change or defile others.)*
3. **Avoiding falsehood, flattery, and theft**, abandoning the nine levels of evil and cultivating the nine levels of good.
   - *One: Benevolence (慈),*
   - *Two: Filial piety (孝),*
   - *Three: Reverence in heart (心有敬),*
   - *Four: Dignity in form (身有礼),*
   - *Five: Practicing virtue (行仁德),*
   - *Six: Sparing speech (少言语),*
   - *Seven: Not acting before others (不为人之先).*
     - *Even if you are greater than others, you must yield and let them act first, so as not to diminish your own virtue (德).*
   - *Eight: Not harming spirits and ghosts unjustly (不妄害鬼神),*
   - *Nine: Always cherishing the Dao (常怀学道).*
4. **After attaining the Dao**, saving all beings.

*(注: **Yan Qing** (昔嚴清) once reduced the weight of charcoal by three or four coins per measure when selling it to the poor, or gave one or two measures to those in need. For over thirty years, one day a **Jade Maiden** (玉女) descended to bestow ten volumes of talismans and scriptures, beginning with the **Six Jia**. She commanded **Yan Qing** to kneel and receive them, explaining each one and teaching him to cultivate the **Six Jia Talismans**. **Yan Qing** replied: *'I do not understand scriptures.'* The **Jade Maiden** said: *'You already understand the nine levels of Yin-Function (Hidden Merit), so why not study and learn to recognize the characters? Once you grasp the scriptures, you will succeed.'*

Thus, **Yan Qing** began reading history books. Though he did not recognize the characters, the **Jade Maiden** taught him. Unable to write, she taught him calligraphy. In three years, he mastered the scriptures, filling his mind with knowledge, and none could question him—he was a sage. He frequently practiced the merit of healing the people’s illnesses and passed this on to his disciples, who all took healing as their practice. At the time, it was called **Yan Jun’s Dao** (嚴君之道).

Later, the **Holy Sage** (聖君) informed the **Heavenly Master** (天師):

*'You instruct your disciples in practicing Yin-Function (Hidden Merit), which has two essentials:*
   - *(注: One, the teacher must discern the disciple’s sincerity; two, the disciple must be filial to the teacher.)*
   - *One: The teacher must first discern the disciple—whether they have sincerity or not, faith or not. *(注: In this age, many disciples have empty words but no sincerity. Such people must not be lightly trusted to pass on teachings.)* You must weigh their sincerity carefully; do not hastily judge them. If you judge them accurately, the teacher will not err, and you may then impart a minor stage of the Dao’s methods. If the disciple has a resolute heart and delights in the Dao, day and night thinking of the Dao and rejoicing in its truth, earnestly offering supplies, the teacher will measure their deeds according to the scriptures, reducing their faults to guide them in practicing Yin-Function (Hidden Merit).*
   - *Two: The disciple must always know the teacher’s sincerity is true and upright, secretly invoking the Dao to honor the teacher. The teacher, in turn, will be moved and often reveal themselves to the disciple. The disciple will call upon the teacher, and the teacher will respond in their heart and mind, fulfilling all their deeds—except for the three rebellions. *(注: One, not rebelling against the sovereign’s words; two, not rebelling against the father’s instructions; three, not rebelling against the teacher’s guidance.)* These three prohibitions are the **Heavenly Master’s** instructions to **Wang Chang** and **Zhao Sheng**, passed on to disciples.*

*Again, the **Heavenly Master** said: 'He who secretly guides others to attain the Dao’s highest truths and honors, is said to have a **heart of benevolent enlightenment** (心願啓善利人), known as **Yin-Function** (Hidden Merit), and as **practicing Yin-Virtue** (行阴德). The heavens reward such deeds, and their descendants will inherit this virtue through generations, never ceasing to hold official positions. *(注: If you guide others in good deeds—such as healing illnesses, delivering them from calamities and misfortunes—always act with sincerity, never committing evil, and frequently practice benevolence to save the nation and people, then your merits will be fulfilled, and you will ascend to immortality in broad daylight.)*'*

If one secretly guides others toward evil, harming people and things, even if they guide them to the Dao’s highest truths and honors, it will never truly prevail. If they secretly guide others to act harmfully, damaging people and things, this is called **Yin-Plotting**, and is known as **practicing Yin-Treason** (行阴贼). The heavens abhor such deeds, and their descendants will surely suffer early deaths. *(Note: Even if descendants do not perish, they will still suffer illness, holding no office nor rank, and will be commoners.)*

I now pass this teaching to you again, knowing you must act as a substitute teacher and instruct future generations. Do not harbor evil intentions—always speak with benevolence. *(Note: Benevolent speech is the voice of teaching; benevolent intentions are the heart’s practice.)* Benevolent intentions are supreme.

The **Celestial Master** told the **True Lord of the Northern Dipper**: "When people secretly guide others, *(Note: guiding with benevolent speech and intentions, wishing to remove demons, evil spirits, and calamities of speech and illness—names unknown to mortals—one may secretly guide them, reciting softly and quietly so as not to be heard by outsiders. If heard, they may be spoken of by one person and spread by a hundred. It must not be heard, lest the Heavenly Tribunals remain unaware, and human rumors falsely transmit it as grievance. The spirits and gods know, fearing that in the clouds or at the Heavenly Gate’s three barriers, they may be intercepted by powerful spirits and gods. The Heavenly Gate’s petitions will not be permitted to reach the **Supreme Sovereign’s** presence, and the decree will descend to the Heavenly Tribunals.)* You must urgently petition the Heavenly Gate and address the **Jade Emperor**. If you wait for both the **Yin** and **Yang** talismans to arrive, you will be accused of grievance, and the **Yin Officials** and **Earthly Tribunals** will intercept you, preventing your petition from reaching the **Supreme Sovereign’s** presence. You must not wait for the **Yin** and **Yang** talismans. *(Note: Talismans are also called **Shi**.)*

When people use proper petitions, idle memorials, and Heavenly Gate petitions, their tone, rhythm, and resonant speech are meant to be known by others. They then gather the **Earthly Tribunals’** and **Legal Talisman** armies, dispatching the **Yin-Yang Gods** of the **Six Jia** with two **Direct Talismans**, first petitioning the **Lord of the Northern Dipper**, who then relays it to the **Heavenly Gate’s** petitioner, only then reaching the **Celestial Master**. The **Celestial Master** is called **Release Teacher** in the **Laozi’s** poem, which the Buddha refers to as **Indra**. The later sage’s title is **Celestial Master**, surnamed **Zhang**, named **Ling**. After the **Celestial Master’s** decree is issued, it is directly conveyed to the **Supreme Sovereign’s** presence. Beware of the **Three Officials of Heaven, Earth, and Water** falsely petitioning before the **Supreme Sovereign**, claiming: ‘So-and-so’s memorial contains falsehoods against the **Supreme Sovereign’s** boundless Dao.’ The **Supreme Sovereign, Laozi**, and the **Jade Emperor, the Way-Bearing Sovereign**, will not permit such petitions to pass. Be cautious. This is why the **Yin-Petition** to the **Heavenly Gate** exists.

The **Celestial Master** told the **True Person of Marvelous Conduct** *(Note: There are eight **Marvelous Conduct** figures; the true **Marvelous Conduct** bears the surname **Zhen**, named **Dingguang**):* "When people study and understand the **Ten Grades of Yin-Function** and apply them to others, they will long endure in this practice. Within five or six years, they will attain **Divine Communication** and **Transcendence**. After achieving **Divine Communication**, they must only act benevolently to save others. As people accumulate their kindness, they will gradually be heard by the **Heavenly Tribunals**, and their petitions will reach the **Heavenly Gate** and the **Supreme Sovereign**. The **Supreme Sovereign** will rejoice and grant each petition, decreeing to the **Heavenly Officials**, who will then record their merits in the **Immortal Register**. When their merits reach three thousand, the **Supreme Sovereign** will bestow ten **Direct Immortal Children**, *(Note: one per day, two **Jade Boys**, one **Jade Girl Official**, and two **Attendant Officials** corresponding to the number of days’ **Direct Talismans**.)* twelve **Direct Jade Girls**, *(Note: two per day, one **Jade Girl Official**, one to record **Yin-Function**, and one to petition the **Heavenly Gate** for matters concerning mortals and petitions to the **Heavenly Tribunals**.)* one **True Official**, *(Note: **Jiazi** is **Wang Wenqing**, **Yichou** is **Long Jiqing**; these are used cyclically within the **Six Jia**, repeating endlessly without bound.)* and **Attendant Officials** corresponding to the number of days’ **Direct Talismans**, summoned by name according to the day to fulfill their duties without transgression. *(Note: Summoning them to fulfill their duties means no transgression. If not summoned to fulfill their duties, it is a violation of the laws.)* two **Direct Talismans**. *(Note: The talismans for the day’s duties are used to save others from calamities and harm.)* The person performing the **Six Jia Yin-Function** duties rotates endlessly without interruption, and none shall transgress. *(Note: Transgressors act falsely, harming others, deceiving people, and leading them to licentious worship. The **Six Jia Yin-Function Jade Girls**, the **Six Jia Lords**, and the **Northern Dipper Lord** will greatly resent this, turning it into misfortune for the transgressor. This is the meaning of **‘the fox assuming the tiger’s威’**—deceiving others for gain. The crime is twofold: first, the great crime of deceiving others; second, the harm done to the deceived person’s body and mind. Though originally free from calamity, they falsely petition the **Northern Dipper**, claiming misfortune, which is a false accusation against Heaven and Earth. The gods of the **Heavenly Gate** resent licentious worship and thus intercept the petition. Next, the finger-star of their original birth is implicated, and the person will instead incur guilt, suffer reduced lifespan, and be consigned to an evil path. If there is genuine calamity, one must still follow the **Northern Dipper’s** rites—any deviation is also transgression. Each offense is calculated, and when **Yin-Function** is complete, one ascends as an immortal.)"

The **Later Sage** told the **Celestial Master**: "The **Six Jia’s Yin-Function** can achieve great merit. All ten thousand gods between Heaven and Earth are the **Six Jia Lords’** subordinates. If they act with righteousness and propriety, benefiting mortals with compassion and reverence, their laws and blessings flow like恩福, nourishing the common people, and their deeds are called **benevolent and efficacious**. They neither kill nor harm, neither practice sorcery nor falsity—this is called **Yin-Blessings flowing to save**, *(Note: whether through talismanic healing or invoking dragons to bring rain, benefiting ten thousand towns and villages, nourishing the nation, and bringing joy to the people—all are at peace, and their merit is great.)*

The ten thousand towns and people rejoice in peace, their merit piled high as mountains.
It is not merely for your single life or family that you inherit the blessings of immortality across generations.

If they act without reliance on scripture and masters, falsely practicing sorcery and deceit, they cause licentious worship of Heaven, Earth, and the starry hosts.
Their crimes will instead invite **retributive decrements**, forfeiting lifespan—both they and others will bear punishment.

The **Rectified-One’s** *jiào* rites have their own origins, their ceremonies drawn from the **Three Celestial Cycles**.

*(Note: The Celestial Master spoke in secret to King Chang Zhao Sheng: The law of **Rectified-One** originated with the **Venerable Lord**. The Venerable Lord concealed this law on the **Celestial Terrace**, then after countless eons, revealed it anew, calling himself the **Later Sage**, descending from Heaven to bestow it upon me. Alongside this, he granted the **Three Assemblies’** rites, offerings, and libations—like the world’s communal sacrifices, like a military encampment’s provisions. All must be performed at the proper time; if missed, it cannot be done. If held on another day, it is no longer the proper *jiào*—it becomes **Three Celestial Cycles** in vain.

On this day, one may gather a **Three Celestial Cycles** assembly, where the **Venerable Lord** and **Later Sage** permit it: the rites convene the **Three Celestial Cycles**, the **Five Phases**, the **Six Jia Lords**, the **Seven Stars**, the **Nine Spirits** and **Nine Essences**, the **Twenty-Eight Constellations**, the **Thirty-Five Officials**, the **Forty-Nine Officials**, and the **One Hundred Twenty Officers**—leading Heaven’s armies in the hundreds of billions, commanding the myriad star-forms. This is the day of their descent to feast, all sated and drunk, bestowing blessings upon the body and family, extending even to the **Lower Celestial Cycle’s** Five Sacred Peaks and Four Great Rivers. The **Community Altars**, **Temple Deities**, and **Spiritual Officials** are likewise sated and drunk, while the host receives blessings.

If not performed on this day, but held as a reckless *jiào* assembly—whether invoking one’s **natal destiny**, the **Six Jia**, or the **Four Seasons and Eight Nodes**—burning money and offerings, this falls under **licentious worship**. Wayward ghosts and wild spirits will come to gluttonously partake, while the **Rectified-One’s** deities and the **starry hosts** will not descend. Only the **three generals of the talismanic spirit** within the body may eat; those in Heaven and Earth cannot descend to feast. They will rage in fury, instead harming the body—how much more could one then seek virtue and blessings?

You are my disciple—be cautious and do not act thus. If you disregard this and stray from the Dao, you will harm your body and family. Be warned.)

The *jiào* rites must be performed strictly according to the prescribed methods, ensuring no failure to harmonize with the **Three Officials of Heaven, Earth, and Water**, thereby invoking the **Dao’s transformative power**.

If one disregards this and instead summons **unauthorized forces**, it becomes a **yin-disaster**—a term for calamity. *[Note: An alternative name for misfortune.]*
In the past, there were those who habitually engaged in licentious worship, their transgressions clear. How much more could they then seek virtue and blessings?

You must understand this clearly: As a disciple instructed in the **Rectified-One’s Three Primordial Talismans**, do not indulge in **licentious sorcery** or deceive the world. Only by adhering to the **Six Jia’s merit** will one naturally attain the Dao without deviation.

The **Venerable Lord** said: This is called the **"Ten Yin-Mercies of the Six Jia"**—those who practice must treasure and conceal it, for only by following this will one naturally attain the Dao.

---
**The *Six Jia Ling Shu* (Sacred Scriptures of the Six Jia) – Yang-Merits**
There is also the *Six Jia Ling Shu*, which expounds on **yang-merits**, comprising ten sections.
Here, the ten precepts are briefly recorded. *[Note: Fully elaborated in *The Transmission of the Venerable Lord*.]*

1. **Broadly gathering causes and conditions**, assembling congregations, constructing earthen and wooden pavilions and halls—accumulating merits numbering in the ten-thousands—this is called **yang-merit**, uncounted among the yin.
   The **Sage Sovereign** said: Such a person, in a future life, will become an official, possess wealth and grand halls, with prosperous descendants yet no noble status.

2. **Observing fasts and reciting scriptures**, accumulating merits numbering in the ten-thousands—this is called **yang-merit**, uncounted among the yin.
   The **Lord** said: In a future life, one will be endowed with wisdom, with clear and upright ears and eyes, having virtuous sons and daughters who are filial, and attaining official rank.

3. **Exhorting others to do good**, prompting almsgiving, and donating wealth numbering in the ten-thousands—this too is **yang-merit**, uncounted among the yin.
   The **Lord** said: In a future life, one will become a leader among people, the chief of those who consume flesh, with descendants inheriting this status across generations.

4. **Acting with sincere devotion and labor**, broadly constructing earthen and wooden structures, erecting frameworks for halls and temples, and rigorously clearing mountain paths—this too is **flourishing merit**, uncounted among the yin.
   The **Lord** said: In a future life, one will be reborn as a male, holding an official position with wealth, slaves, and servants at their command, with prosperity lasting two generations—yet afterward, one’s station will decline. The **Great Dao forbids such ambition**.

5. **Casting and crafting bells and statues**, completing the merit of becoming an immortal—where statues manifest the transient goodness of mortals—this too is **yang-merit**, uncounted among the yin.
   The **Lord** said: In a future life, one will be skilled in song and music, with a well-proportioned body, yet lacking in wealth and sustenance.

6. **Reciting incantations idly**, invoking them loudly and calling out to chastise ghosts and spirits—even if it saves a person—this is **yang-merit**.
   The **Lord** told the **Celestial Master**: Though this merit is not fully attained, it still emerges from the body, yet because the chastisement is excessive, in a future life one will suffer few illnesses but lack descendants.

7. **Digging wells along roads and rivers**, providing water and gruel—this too is **yang-merit**.
   Though this act benefits others, it aligns with **yin-speech of merit**, as it is said, *"So-and-so dug this well."*
   The **Lord** said: Such a person’s descendants will receive half of the yin-merit, while the individual attains yang-merit, transforming into benevolent deeds that aid those in urgent need.

8. **Leveraging official authority or borrowed strength to rescue others from罪**, this too is **yang-merit**.
   The **Lord** said: In a future life, one will receive blessings, or perhaps reap rewards in this very life—this is the merit of **auspicious yang**.

9. **Constructing bridges and causeways**, facilitating passage and transit—this too is **yang-merit**.
   The **Lord** said: In a future life, one will constantly benefit from the kindness of travelers.

10. **Receiving ordination and taking vows**, with a pure mind and spirit, abstaining from marriage, and dwelling in high mountains—this too is **yang-merit**.
   The **Lord** said: In a future life, one will attain the Dao of **non-action**.

---
These ten are called the **"Ten Yang-Merits"**, uncounted among the yin.
In the past, the **Highest True Ones** and **Ascended Immortals** all practiced **yin-merits and yin-virtues**, unlike the ten recorded histories of the ten yang-merits.

In antiquity, the **Divine Ancestor and Sage Sovereign** served as **Three Pillars of History** in the **Yin and Zhou dynasties**, as **Chancellor and Minister** for sixty-four sovereigns over seven hundred and fifty-one years. Then, crossing westward through the pass into the **Barbarian lands**, *[as transmitted:]* he had eighty-four wives and two hundred and forty children. *[As recorded in the Inner Transmission.]*
He transformed the **Barbarian King into a Buddha-Immortal**, later ascending to become the **Emperor of the Golden Gate of Great Peace, the Morning Star of the Supreme Dao, the Posterior Sage, and the Primordial Lord of the Mysterious Origin**. His successors continued practicing **yin-merits**, accumulating **yin-virtues**, and teaching the **Dao of Non-Action** without relying on those who dwell in mountains and forests.

Over time, ascending ever higher, past, present, and future lives—
**receiving unbroken blessings from virtuous deeds**—
*[End of the Nineteenth Volume of *The Golden Lock and Flowing Pearl*]*
*[Beginning of the Twentieth Volume of *The Golden Lock and Flowing Pearl*]*.

The **Grand Sovereign of the Complete Perfection of the Chinese Realm**, namely **Zhang Daoling of the Peaceful Dao**, **Zhao Shengwang**, **Wang Chang**, **Commander Li Zhongfu**, **Master Mao Ying**, **Xu Yufu**, and others, were their descendants who compiled the scriptures.

The **Dao-Immortal Li Chunfeng** annotated the **Six Jiao and Seven Stars**—the talismans and methods for national defense, repelling bandits, and delivering from calamities and misfortunes.

**Lao Jun** said: *"Seven Stars—*
these are the children of the **Six Jiao**,
seven women in total.
Some were once **empresses**, **consorts**, or **Jiao women**,
each adorned in floral garments.
They emerged from the lineage of the **Five Clans and Six Jiao**,
since the time of **Pangu the Primordial**,
and were already visible as seven stars—
seen by both **heavenly beings and mortals**.
This is the very name of the **Primordial Origin**,
the manifestation of the **Great Dao** at its dawn.
Born in the **floating heavens**,
they revolve within the **one-day-one-night cosmic cycle**,
measuring the earth’s degrees with precision—
hence, they are called **Seven Stars**.
They oversee the **registers of death** for the **Ten Thousand Heavens and myriad people**,
and govern the illnesses and misfortunes of the living,
as well as calamities, grief, and harm.
They command and annihilate **ghosts and spirits**,
a division under the **Ancient Sage, the Great Dao Sovereign**.
When one invokes the **Six Jiao talisman’s power**,
combining it to deploy them,
the **Six Jiao** are the parents of the **Seven Stars**,
so those who wear the **Six Jiao talisman**
seek to command the **Seven Stars**.
In ancient times, the **Supreme Dao-Immortal** wore it for longevity,
commanding the **Seven Stars** at will.
He also bestowed upon **Cun, Li Deng, Meng Xian, Li FuRen, the Western Queen Mother, Ma Gu, and Wang Fangping**—
none of whom failed to subdue the **Five Phases and Six Jiao**,
thus enabling the **Northern Dipper to attain immortality**.
Since the **Northern Dipper governs death**,
it is feared by the **yin-officials**,
and **ghosts and spirits** submit to its command.
If the **Northern Dipper’s envoys** refuse to obey,
those it points to die instantly.
It is said that wherever the **Heavenly Gate** is directed,
there are deaths and injuries.
Thus, the **Supreme Sage** commands it to traverse the **cosmic cycle**—
once daily, once nocturnally.
And when paired with the corresponding garments,
the *Golden Lock and Flowing Pearl* refers to this as **paired garments**.
In ancient times, great **Dao-Immortals** practiced without offering sacrifices to the **Northern Dipper**.
Lesser **Dao-Immortals**, with limited vision,
would sacrifice to the **Northern Dipper**.
Why is this?
Because the **Northern Dipper** is a **god of the six yin-forces**,
fond of killing and averse to nurturing life.
The **Supreme Dao Sovereign** loathed its presence,
so he instructed the **Supreme Lao Jun**,
who in turn taught their successors to wear it as **garments of command**,
with twenty-four stipulations—
fully detailed in the **generalized conditions** for all affairs.
All are listed to the left.

---

**First Condition:**
Tread the *Earthly Measure* forward, backward, and reversed—three cycles.
When finished,
forward and backward are the *Earthly Measure’s* framework,
originating from the front—
in accordance with the principle of ascending from earth to heaven.
Recite the *Eighteen Incantations* once.
Tread the *Heavenly Halter* forward, backward, and reversed—three cycles.
When finished,
recite the *Eleven Incantations* once.
For distant national command,
speak while pointing—
even at a thousand *li* away, it shall take effect.
But if directed toward a certain quarter,
perform the ritual remotely,
turning the enemy’s forces back—
strengthening one’s own troops,
while the enemy’s *inverse qi* causes their entire army to collapse in defeat.
Perform this three times,
and bestow the talisman upon the national *Great General*,
who wears it to ensure victory—
the enemy shall be utterly broken.
After reciting the *Step Incantations*,
pass over the talisman,
and pinch the *Key Seal*—
the *Key Seal* is on the third joint of the left fifth finger, on the right side.
With vermilion or ink, mark it for twenty days—
the enemy shall tremble in fear, unable to resist.

The Later Sage Emperor declared:
*"To save the nation and its people,
to pacify and subdue rebels—
this is the supreme yin-virtue.
But if used for treachery,
defying the sovereign,
the Heavenly Lock shall return harm to your own body—
disaster shall strike immediately."*

**The Former Sage’s Military Talisman**—
If entered on the right, the Military Talisman is auspicious,
granting the power to soar a thousand *li*.
**The Former Sage’s Command Talisman**—
If entered on the right, the Command Talisman is auspicious.
The Northern Dipper’s decree turns the Heavenly Lock,
pointing at the enemy who harms us—
the talisman shall fly a thousand *li* on its own.

The **Imperial Edict Talisman** reads:
*"The White Tiger commands ten thousand troops,
the Dark-Subduing Jade Maiden is [designated] as General [Name],
resolving calamities and dispelling misfortune,
commanding Great General [Name],
to achieve victory and military strength—
the enemy, by this talisman’s decree, shall swiftly be defeated and annihilated.
Urgent, as the White Tiger General’s command."*

After inscribing, seal it in a red pouch
and tie it to the *Great General’s* left elbow.
**One talisman for every thousand soldiers—**
one talisman suffices for a thousand troops.
If the *Great General* commands ten thousand,
ten men may wear it—
ensuring overwhelming strength in battle."

The Later Sage Emperor proclaimed:
*"These two talismans were granted by Lao Jun
as a secret method to repel enemies—
worth ten thousand gold pieces and never to be divulged.
[Alternatively,] one may add the *Assisting Seal* to the talisman."*

---

**Second Condition:**
Tread the *Heavenly Halter* forward, backward, and reversed—three cycles.
Recite the *Eleven Incantations* once.
When finished,
tread the *Earthly Measure* forward, backward, and reversed—three cycles,
and recite the *Eighteen Incantations* once.
Scatter into the *Yǔ Steps*—three strides, nine traces—
turn the Heavenly Lock,
and point at the *Six Metal-and-Bronze Talismans*,
one by one, to rescue living beings from illness.

The military method aligns heart and hand,
swifter than water or fire.

The Later Sage Emperor bestowed this talisman upon the Heavenly Master,
declaring:
*"This talisman invokes the Five Phases’ decrees
and dispatches messengers—
the Northern Dipper’s Lock is its key.
There are now nine talismans:
two from the Former Sage,
governing military commands,
as the Nine Stars turn the Lock,
pointing at enemies and saving people.
The Later Sage Emperor further bestows seven talismans—
first, the **Lion-King Talisman**."*

The **Lion-King Talisman** (first) cures the White Tiger’s ailments—painful gout and restless movement—
where pain feels like knife thrusts.
The Daoist adept revives the dead, restoring life—
its efficacy is great, yet it must not be used recklessly.
Those who misuse it will surely incur Heaven’s retribution.

The Later Sage Emperor instructed the Heavenly Master:
*"This talisman must not be given to anyone but those of the utmost Daoist virtue,
or close kin, or sovereigns and regional lords.
It must not be used recklessly."*

The **Green Dragon Talisman** (second) is most potent in summoning dragon spirits,
controlling rain—its effects manifest in moments.
It can also pursue and subdue fox spirits, demons, and celestial malevolent beings,
all with unerring success.

The Later Sage Emperor declared:
*"Only regional governors may wield it—
no ordinary person should dare."*

The **White Tiger Talisman** (third) is supremely skilled in leading armies without casualties,
a weapon of war that crushes foes without fail.
A single general bearing this talisman
can match the strength of a thousand men.

The Later Sage Emperor told Huangshigong:
*"War is the Yang thief of the White Tiger’s spirit,
thus it repels armies—
its power aligns with the Northern Dipper’s Lock-turning force."*

The **Vermilion Bird Talisman** (fourth) is most effective against the Five Metal Spirits,
and in warding off blades and swords in battle.
It harmonizes with the virtue of Wood,
curing malevolent illnesses, silencing slander,
commanding celestial deities, and summoning the Thunder Lord,
pursuing the Lightning Master and the Zero Mother,
ensuring all desires are fulfilled.

The Later Sage Emperor said:
*"This talisman prohibits the use of Yang

The third method: recite the **Threefold Heavenly Circuit Talisman** in forward, reverse, and inverted order.

When finished, recite the incantation as before once, then proceed with the **Earthly Cycle** in forward, reverse, and inverted order.

When finished, recite the **Eighteen Dao Talisman** once.

Then speak aloud: *"I, so-and-so, was born on the [date], under the influence of [such-and-such] star, with the [current] year’s principal destiny and fundamental fate. Throughout my life, misfortunes and calamities shall be measured and dispelled by this talisman. When the heavens are clear and the stars shine brightly, day and night observing my native constellation, then misfortunes shall be obscured. If calamities arise, they must be subdued and appeased by proper ritual—never shall there be failure."*

**Golden Lock, Flowing Pearl**—the twenty-first invocation
**Golden Lock, Flowing Pearl**—the twenty-second invocation

The **Grand Sovereign of All-Pure Daoists**, Zhang Daoling, the **King of Balance** (Zhuangsheng), **Master of Command** (Longji), Li Zhongfu, Mao Ying, Xu Yufu, and others, composed this as a substitute.

**Daoist Master Li Chunfeng** annotated:
*"The method of correlating the **Twenty-Eight Constellations**, observing their luminosity, and determining life’s prosperity or decline through the brightness or obscurity of the **native star**."*

**The Twenty-Eight Constellations’ Monthly Correspondences**

**Spring Months (2nd–7th lunar months):**
1st day: **Kui, Wei, Bi, Shen, Gui, Zhang**
2nd day: **Lou, Mao, Zui, Jing, Liu, Yi**
3rd day: **Wei, Bi, Shen, Xing, Zhen**
4th day: **Mao, Zui, Jing, Liu, Zhang, Jiao**
5th day: **Bi, Shen, Xing, Yi, Yuan**

10th day: **Liu, Zhang, Zhen, Fang, Ju**

14th day: **Zhen, Kang, Fang, Wei, Dou, Wei**
15th day: **Jiao, Xin, Ju, Nü, Shi**
16th day: **Kang, Fang, Wei, Xu, Bi**
17th day: **Xin, Ju, Nü, Wei, Kui**
18th day: **Fang, Wei, Dou, Xu, Lou**
19th day: **Xin, Ju, Nü, Wei, Bi, Wei**

25th day: **Wei, Lou, Mao, Zui, Gui**

30th day: **Shi, Xin, Ju, Xu, Kui**

**Method of Calculation:**
The above corresponds to a full year of twelve months, each with thirty days. One must align the individual’s **native star** with the day’s constellation, beginning from the first day and concluding on the thirtieth. Each month’s sequence is matched accordingly.

The **Supreme Primordial Lord Laozi**, having received instruction from the **Primordial Dao Lord Yuan Shi**, recorded this as the *Scripture of the Twenty-Eight Constellations*, comprising twelve volumes and two hundred sheets—its vastness making it difficult to fully explore.

Later, the **Sage Emperor** descended from **Nanshan** (now **Zhongnan Mountain**), in the **thirteenth year of the Great Achievement** (617 CE), revealing to the **Tang Dynasty’s Li clan**, who ruled under Heaven. Now, this abridged version of the *Twenty-Eight Constellations Scripture* is compiled to correspond with the thirty days of each month, demonstrating how to correlate and observe one’s **native star** to discern prosperity or decline.

Thus, the **Edict of Edging Through** is condensed into essential principles, teaching humanity to record and reflect upon it.

The **Supreme Primordial Lord Laozi** declared:
*"For those cultivating longevity, knowing one’s **native star**—the constellation governing one’s birth—is paramount. The **wandering star** is the constellation of one’s life’s destiny.

If the **native star** aligns perfectly in its proper position, yet a **wandering star** intrudes upon it, this is most malevolent, bringing great calamity. If only the **wandering star** intrudes, the consequences are lighter.

These two matters must be carefully observed: if the star is bright, misfortune will not befall; if it is dim, illness and disaster will arise. One must act swiftly, invoking talismans and rituals to dispel them, thereby eliminating sickness and averting decline.

On one’s **native star’s day**, if the night is clear, observe it secretly when no one is about. If it is bright and clear, it is auspicious; if dim or flickering, disaster is near; if unseen, great misfortune looms.

Then, recite the **Earth-Treading Step** and the **Heavenly Halter** each three times, perform the **Yugaitian Steps**, and turn the **Heavenly Pass**. Point toward the direction of the afflicted person’s **star of decline or ghostly abode**—for all are born into regions of calamity.

For instance, a **Metal-born** individual has:
- **Longevity** in **Si (Peril)**,
- **Bathing** in **Wu (Boiling)**,
- **Crowning** in **Wei (Encirclement)**,
- **Official Duty** in **Shen (Apply)**,
- **Sovereignty** in **You (Jade)**,
- **Decline** in **Xu (Empty)**,
- **Sickness** in **Hai (Hide)**,
- **Death** in **Zi (Self)**,
- **Tomb** in **Chou (Rest)**,
- **Ruination** in **Yin (Conceal)**,
- **Severance** in **Mao (Insult)**.

If any of the **Five Phases’** stars fall into these regions of decline, regardless of whether the **native star** is visible, decline will manifest. One must act to dispel it.

Perform this ritual **three times monthly**. If the star remains bright, one will have no worries—disasters and calamities will vanish."*

「Indeed, those who study with the resolve to follow the Dao must first comprehend this method, only then may they attain the true preservation of life.

If one does not understand the matters of decline and calamity, they will fall ill and die. This method can help people dispel disasters, overcome misfortunes, and ward off sickness, even saving relatives and Daoist companions.

When observing the native star, if it is faint or obscured—whether unseen or displaced by other stars—killing the native star will cause **180 people** to perish in that direction, according to the phase. **180 people** in the East, **136 in the West**, **164 in the South**, **125 in the North**, and **1,200 in the Central Palace**—why so?

The Central Palace belongs to **Earth**, and when Earth loses its position, it multiplies the harm done to all other directions, which people should not fail to recognize. Those who know this method may follow its principles, saving themselves first and then ten others.

But among the **Twenty-Eight Constellations**, each constellation governs countless billions of people beneath it. If one practices this method, they may save a hundred souls, yet the world remains unaware—how much more so for saving just one life or a few relatives and friends, who would still be saved. Yet people remain ignorant, openly receiving the **Ming** (dark) commands from the celestial agents, who come to summon them to death—this is truly a grievous fate!

Those dwelling at the edges of the heavens beneath the native star will also suffer hundreds or thousands of deaths.

Those who cultivate life and preserve their bodies must always observe their native star’s position in the **Twenty-Eight Constellations**, to discern the signs of their own rise or decline. This Dao is of utmost importance: without cause, one’s body will not decline or fall ill.

Moreover, when the star is bright and clear, one need not perform the **步蹑 (Bujie)** steps or the **祭醮 (Jijiao)** rituals. If they do, they will instead invite disasters and calamities upon their entire household, not just themselves.

The **Laozi (Lao Jun)** has universally commanded this prohibition, and those in **white robes** (laypersons) do not accept it, while those who invert the Dao (false teachers) often allow the **天关 (Tian Guan)** agents to turn and point at the native stars of people.

The later sage-emperor declared: *"White robes do not accept"* refers to those who invoke the **七星 (Qi Xing, Seven Stars)** or **六甲 (Liu Jia, Six Jia)** in the *金锁流珠 (Jin Suo Liu Zhu)* scriptures and borrow from teachers—those who falsely claim to teach, yet write out entire texts without proper transmission, or even if they receive them, do not verify with the teacher’s seal or voice, or lightly assume the teacher’s authority, or have the teacher’s name appended without genuine transmission—such are the crimes of **罔师 (Wang Shi, false teaching)**, and they will not die naturally.

How much worse for those who further seek this Dao, yet fail to attain peace even for themselves! The deceivers of the Dao are known to the **三官 (San Guan, Three Officials of Heaven, Earth, and Water)**, who will surely report them to the **道祖 (Dao Zu, Daoist Patriarch)**, and the **天师 (Tian Shi, Celestial Master)** will be notified. Both the patriarch and the master will censure these deceitful thieves of the Dao, and their entire families will be struck down by Heaven’s punishment, dying unnatural deaths.

In ancient times, there was a man named **张山子 (Zhang Shanzi)**, whose given name was **初见 (Chu Jian)**. His daughter was **小王夫人 (Xiao Wang Fu Ren)**, also known as the **阿母 (Amu, Mother) of the Six Jia**.»

「If one possesses this book and reveres it with a single-minded devotion, never failing in its observances, yet after five years of practice, the **Celestial Master (天師)** still does not press his seal upon it—if he instead secretly uses the **San Guan (三官)**’s talismans of *Shuangxian Guan (天纲)* and *Dieji Guan (地紀)*, mastering the art of divine communication—then the transmission will never cease for a thousand years.

When the **Xiao Wang Fu Ren (小王夫人)** saw this, she did not consider it a flaw but allowed him to proceed. Suddenly, one day, she was in her mountain retreat (*shanfang jing, 山房靖*) when seven men clad in garments of five colors appeared, claiming to be **heavenly emissaries (天使)**, sent to investigate **Zhang Shanzi (張山子)** for the crime of **stealing the Dao (盗道)**.

The **Xiao Wang Fu Ren** asked: *“What crime does he have?”*

The emissaries replied: *“The crime of **Wang Shi (罔師)**, stealing the Dao.”*

The **Xiao Wang Fu Ren** instructed them to have **Zhang Shanzi** write the *Jin Suo Liu Zhu (金鎖流珠)* scripture and the *Liu Tian (六式九符)* talismans, all paid for with silk, money, silver, and gold to a certain **Bu Ren (某乙)**. **Bu Ren** then petitioned the name of an **immortal (上仙)**, and only then did the writing commence. Once finished, the texts were passed along to the **Chu (楚) man Bo Yue (葛越)**, who received them in the same hall, and then departed.

The seven emissaries questioned the **Xiao Wang Fu Ren**, asking if she had sealed the talismans.

The **Xiao Wang Fu Ren**, pondering, recalled that he had left without receiving the immortal’s seal. The emissaries declared: *“This alone is the crime of **Wang Shi (罔師)**, stealing the Dao. Heaven commands his punishment.”*

The **Xiao Wang Fu Ren** fully realized the gravity of his failure to seal the texts. If he had received them and later defied the Dao, the guilt would have extended to her, and she would have been demoted to a lower stage of **Daoist rank (師階)**. She would then have suffered for a hundred years in the mortal realm, unable to ascend.

Now, because of his own actions, he has incurred this punishment. He falsely claims that I am **Li Si Ming (李司命)**, the **Zhong Fu (仲甫)**, and refuses to accept this law. How could I, a **Daoist Master (師)**, accept the law from a woman’s hands? Even the households of **kings and nobles (王侯)** would not dare speak thus.

We, the seven, then went to **Songgao Mountain (嵩高山)**, to investigate **Bo Yue (葛越)**. His response was the same as that of the **Xiao Wang Fu Ren**.

We reported this to the **Supreme Sage (後聖君)**, who was enraged. How could he have knelt before a woman at that time, bowing to her as his master?

Now, because of his defiance of the Dao, this is the crime of **Wang Shi (罔師)**, stealing the Dao. We were ordered to afflict him with illness, but we feared that the **Xiao Wang Fu Ren** might seal these talismans for him, using the law to rectify the situation. If she did so, it would implicate him in another crime, burdening her as well.

Thus, the **Supreme Sage (太上)** commanded us to question the **Xiao Wang Fu Ren** again.

The **Xiao Wang Fu Ren** answered: *“Indeed, I did not seal them.”*

「When the celestial emissary was about to depart, he next declared: *“I am the **Supreme Marshal of the Northern Dipper (Northern Dipper Marshal)**, as well as the envoy of the **Twenty-Eight Constellations (Twenty-Eight Mansions)**. The **Supreme Sage (Taishang Xuan Yuan Shang Dao Jun)**** had instructed me to descend and investigate; this matter is not trivial. The **Xiao Wang Fu Ren** has indeed not sealed these talismans for all concerned—she rejoiced, and she rejoiced again.”*
Having spoken, he left.

Within half a year thereafter, **Zhang Shānzǐ (張山子)**, dwelling on **Mount Tai Bai (太白山)**, saw his entire household afflicted by an epidemic plague, all perishing—even to the last fowl and beast, all slain by **demonic forces (鬼)**. Thus, **Feng (風)** searched within the *Inner Transmission of the Mother and Daughter (Amu Xiaonü Neichuan)* and found its composition, intending to instruct the world.

Let mortals be cautious not to act thus with **intentionality (行心)**, lest they betray their **master (師)** below and deceive the **Dao (Way)** above, and thus be struck down by heaven. How much more so if they seek the **Dao (Way)** itself! The **Dao (Way)** and its laws are impartial, allowing no transgressions. The **Great Dao (Way)** is without bias, taking only those who are without fault. The **Great Dao (Way)** is without favoritism, not permitting mortals to deceive one another. The **Dao (Way)** and its laws are without deceit, forbidding the disrespect of **masters (師)**. As noted before, do not repeat such offenses.

Such crimes must be heeded by those who study the **Dao (Way)**. The **Supreme Sage (Laojun)**** then told the **Forty-Nine True Persons of the Highest Grade (上品四十九真人)**: *“This **Northern Dipper Marshal (北斗君)** is the overseer of the **Four Cardinal Mansions (四方宿)**. He governs the affairs of the **Eighteen Constellations (十八宿)**; all matters are known to him first, and he does not allow lesser constellations to act as their superiors. For those who are **filial (孝)** yet defy the **Dao (Way)**, betray their **master (師)**, and rebel against their **lord (君)**, failing to honor their parents, even if they seek vengeance in this lifetime, their **crimes (罪)** will be repaid in the depths of time by the **celestial laws (日月)**—their punishment will be swift as **water and fire (水火)**, yet they will still not escape their fate.”*
Be cautious, be cautious.

**Daoist Rituals (醮祭) for the Northern Dipper and Twenty-Eight Constellations to Invoke the Celestial Laws (日月時法)**
**Laojun (老君)** said: *“Those who practice the **Dao (Way)** and perform **rituals (醮祭)** must follow the **Five Marshal Laws (五斗君法)**. All must abide by the **scripted rites (科仪)** and observe the **auspicious times of the moon, day, and hour (月日时)**.”*
The *Scripture of Illuminating Truth (Mingzhen Ke)* states: *“In the **Spring (春)**, the **First Month (正月)** has the **Native Star Day (本命日)**; in **Autumn (秋)**, the **Seventh Month (七月)** has the **Native Star Day (本命日)**; in **Winter (冬)**, the **Tenth Month (十月)** has the **Native Star Day (本命日)**. The **hour (更)** should be the **second watch (二更时)** when the **stars and moon are clear (星月明朗)**—this is supreme. If not, then the **ritual platform (坛)** should be moved beneath the **house (屋)**, spread with **yellow earth (黄土)** to form the **platform (坛)**, shaped according to the **land’s contours (随地关挟长短曲直)**. Light **dozens of lamps (数十灯)** to illuminate the platform, mirroring the **intent of stars and moon (月星之意)**.”*

The **Supreme Sage (Taishang Jun)**** then told the **Celestial Master (天師)**: *“You wish to perform **rituals (醮祭)**. Within the **Daoist scriptures (道法箓)**, the **Generals of the Five Pecks (五斗)**, the **Celestial Officials (仙灵官)**, and **Taiyi (太一)** and **Eryi (二仪)**, the **Three Elements (三元)** and **Four Seasons (四时)**, the **Five Phases (五行)** and **Six Celestial Stems (六甲)**, as well as the **Seven Stars (七星)** and **Twenty-Eight Constellations (二十八宿)**, all must be invoked during the **Spring, Autumn, or Winter (春秋冬)** **First Month (孟月)**, on the **Native Star Day (本命日)** or a **selected auspicious day (吉日)** that harmonizes with their **Native Star (命)**. The ritual must be conducted under **clear skies (晴明)**—if **wind, thunder, clouds, or rain obscure the sun (风雷云雨星宿不见日)**, it is **inauspicious (凶)**. You previously chose a day, but I fear that **nighttime wind, rain, or clouds (夜风雨云)** may darken the **earthly coordinates (蹑地纪)**. Thus, the **Heavenly Mandate (天纲)** must be invoked in **three sequential (顺)、inverted (倒)、and reversed (反)** cycles. Upon completion, disperse in **Yubu Steps (禹步)**—three steps, nine traces—and don ritual attire. Point diagonally toward the **direction of wind and rain (云雨之处)**; if the timing is right, the **ritual will open (应时有开)**. Then **twist the talisman (捻诀)**, holding the **fire knife (火刀)** upright. The **second phalanx of the left hand’s middle finger (左手第二指第三节)** points to the right.

The **incantation (咒)** reads:
*“I wish to cultivate and practice, invoking the **Five Pecks and Thirty-Five Stars (五斗三十五星)**. Today is my **Native Star Day (本命日)**—may the **clouds gather and rain cease (仰云收雨)**, the **wind still (静风)**, and the **seven luminaries (七曜) shine brightly (朗明)**. Swiftly, swiftly, as the **Heavenly Laws decree (如律令)**.”*
**Immediately, the skies will clear (须臾即晴)**.

This method is most secret—do not recklessly transmit it to the unworthy.
To do so recklessly invites Heaven and Earth’s retribution, and the blame will fall upon the teacher.

When the day aligns with one’s fate as auspicious, it is supreme; if inauspicious, it is ominous and must not be used.

In selecting a day, one must choose three **Native Star Days (本命日)** within a year: the first month of spring, the seventh month of autumn, and the tenth month of winter. Days chosen within these three months are supreme; otherwise, the ritual is performed in vain, without adherence to the prescribed rites, and will invite Heaven and Earth’s retribution.

The later sage-king declared: If one truly suffers illness or is as frail as a flickering candle, one may secretly seek a favorable day and perform the ritual for oneself. If unable, a Daoist friend or teacher may act in one’s stead. If none are available, a husband may act for his wife, a wife for her husband, a son for his father, or a father for his son—any such substitution is permissible.

Outsiders must not presume to act, lest the **Yellow Emperor (王皇)** take notice, for the **Marshal of the Northern Dipper (北斗君)** will then hold them accountable.

The **Marshal of the Northern Dipper (北斗君)** and the officials of the **Twenty-Eight Constellations (七宿官)** are most august—women must not go to observe or secretly pay homage. If they do, the Marshal will take grave offense, and the offender will suffer in life: misfortune in officialdom, slanderous tongues, shortened lifespan, and an untimely death.

Beware.

If unable, a teacher, disciple, or parent-child may act in place. The **Celestial Master (天师)** has already composed the rites for the **One Cycle (一元)** within this text.

Herein are recorded the rites for the **Native Star Day (本命日)** invocation of the **Northern Dipper (北斗)** and the **Twenty-Eight Constellations (二十八宿)**.

---
**End of Volume Twenty-One of *The Golden Lock and Flowing Pearl***
**Begin Volume Twenty-Two of *The Golden Lock and Flowing Pearl***

**Volume Twenty-Two of *The Golden Lock and Flowing Pearl***

The **Grand Sovereign of the Dao** Zhang Daoling, along with the successive scribes **Zhuang Wang Fangping, Zhao Sheng, Wang Chang, Li Zhongfu, Mao Ying, and Xu Yufu**, and the **Daoist Immortal Li Chunfeng** in his annotations, have compiled the **Rites for Invoking the Seven Stars and Twenty-Eight Constellations**.

**Offerings:**
Eleven tiers of cakes and fruits—
Cakes must be fresh and pure,
Fruits must be dates and chestnuts, newly gathered.

Two wine jars and forty-five ladles,
Forty-five slices of deer jerky,
Now mixed with fruits and placed.

Three censers, one each of *jian* and *zhi* beans,
Eight lamps, each adorned with tassels.

Three altars, three platters,
Nine cups and one lamp,
Nine *liang* of jerky per slice,
Ten tea leaves,
Fourteen bowls of hot water,
Eight mats,
Two thousand two hundred strings of cash—
If only a minor invocation is performed, these are not required.

Once the small altar is arranged, purification is conducted as prescribed.
Proceed to the platform as usual.

**Ritual Posture:**
Stand upright, then kneel.

First, strike the teeth **twelve times**—
For a minor invocation, **thirty-six times** if performing the greater rite.

Next, ignite the censer.
*"To the Most High Primordial, the Five Spirits, the Venerable Old One!"*

Now summon the **Functionary Officials**, the **Left and Right Dragon-Tiger Lords**, the **Incense-Bearing Attendants**, and the **Three-One Upright Spirits** to swiftly open the **Three Heavens** for the **Primordial Venerable Old Lord**.

*"Your servant now burns incense, arranges the offerings, and performs the invocation in the Dao.
May the Most High’s **Ten Directions’ True Vital Qi** descend upon this servant’s body.
For the invocation on behalf of [specific person], your servant humbly petitions.
Swiftly convey this to the **Supreme Jade Emperor of the True, Boundless, and Limitless** at His throne.
When finished, kneel upright."*

Next, offer wine **three times**.

Then recite the invocation rites.

**Meditative Invocation:**
Visualize the **General and his officers and soldiers**—half arriving from the **Northwest Heavenly Gate**, half emerging from the **forehead**—to attend the ritual feast.

The **Supreme Mystic** proclaims, *"Here, at [location], we solemnly offer the invocation rites."*
The servant responds, *"Today, at [specific place], we reverently set forth the invocation rites."*

**Humbly Invoking the Celestial Lords of the Seven Stars:**
Twice bow to the **Venerable Lords of the Northern Dipper’s Seven Stars**.

Humbly invoke:
- The **Lord of the Greedy Wolf (贪狼) Star, the Yang-Ming Star**
- The **Lord of the Great Gate (巨门) Star, the Yin-Precise Star**
- The **Lord of the True Person (禄存) Star**
- The **Lord of the Ending Return (末回) Star, the Mysterious Darkness Star**
- The **Lord of the Chaste and Pure (廉贞) Star, the Cinnabar Element Star**
- The **Lord of the Martial Curve (武曲) Star, the Northern Pole Star**
- The **Lord of the Shattered Army (破军) Star, the Heavenly Gate Star**
- The **Lord of the Three Altars (三台) Star**

Humbly invoke the **Seven Mansions of the East**:
- **Jiao (角), Heng (亢), Shi (氏), Fang (房), Xin (心), Wei (尾), Ju (箕) Star Officials**

Humbly invoke the **Seven Mansions of the North**:
- **Dou (斗), Niu (牛), Nü (女), Xu (虚), Wei (危), Shi (室), Bi (壁) Star Officials**

Humbly invoke the **Seven Mansions of the West**:
- **Kui (奎), Lou (娄), Wei (胃), Mao (昴), Bi (毕), Zui (觜), Shen (参) Star Officials**

Humbly invoke the **Seven Mansions of the South**:
- **Jing (井), Gui (鬼), Liu (柳), Zhang (张), Yi (翼), Zhen (轸) Star Officials**

Humbly invoke the **Star Officials** and the **Lords of Destiny (司命)**, **Records (司录)**, **Liberation from Calamity (解厄)**, **Abolition of Punishment (解刑)**, **Dispersion of Disasters (消灾)**, and **Scattering of Misfortune (散祸)**, that they may descend and partake in the ritual feast.

*"Your servant [name], prostrates and bows twice."*

Then, kneeling, visualize the deities descending to the seat.
Offer wine and incense **three times**.

Finally, in a long kneel:
*"Your servant [name] humbly petitions..."*

**Supplication to the True Lord of the Northern Dipper (北斗七星真人府君) and the Star Officials (及诸星官)**

Your servant, a mere mortal of low worth,
Who has presumptuously partaken of the **Dao/Way** and **qi**,
And enjoys the honor of official rank,
Having now accumulated many years.

This year, being the **若干**th year of my life, on the **某月某日**,
I was born with my **bāo (胎)** and **qi**,
Unknowing of good or evil.
As my years progress, **zhī gān (支干)**,
I cannot foresee auspicious or inauspicious fortune.
Fortunately, I have been aided by the **Ming (冥)***—
Thus, I have reached this day.

But now, my form and spirit are decayed and weakened,
**Jǐn (疹) and jì (疾)** afflictions assail me,
My soul and **pò (魄)** are restless,
My dreams are empty and false.

Perhaps from my past lives’ karmic debts,
Or from this life onward,
I have accumulated the **qi** of calamitous harm,
And fallen into many punishments—
**Four Kills (四杀)** and **conjoined punishments (兼并)**,
**Five Punishments (五刑)** and **Three Hills, Five Graves (三丘五墓)**,
**Heavenly Yearly Punishments (天年岁杀)** and **Hanging Corpses, Six Calamities (悬尸六害)**,
**Lonely Stars, Few Hosts (孤辰寡宿)** and **Nine Palaces, Eight Trigrams (九宫八卦)**,
**Severed Life Punishments (绝命刑祸)**,
Ensnared by **Heavenly Nets (天罗)** and **Earthly Bonds (地网)**,
Deeply fearing that my life and fate
Cannot be preserved whole.

Without the **Xuan (玄)***—Enlightenment’s salvation,
I cannot be freed.

Your servant, with utmost sincerity,
Petitions for blessings and mercy,
And thus arranges this **jiào (醮)** ritual,
Hoping for your benevolent acceptance.

I humbly pray that the **Seven Stars of the Northern Dipper (北斗七星)**, the **True Lord within the Dipper (斗中真人)**, and the **Star Officials (某等星尊神)** of my lineage,
May receive my humble offerings
And clearly grant my sincere supplication.

Your servant, prostrates and bows twice.
Three times, wine and incense are offered.

Your servant now humbly petitions the **Northern Dipper Star Lords (北斗星君)**—
If this is a **human ritual feast (人醮)**,
Then I invoke the name of that person.

Since my birth, my heart and deeds have erred.
I have either violated **rites and teachings (礼教)**,
Or committed many acts of killing—
Bound by the **Four Records (四司)**, punished by the **Three Officials (三官)**,
My crimes recorded, ever deepening.
Now, through this **jiào (醮)** of thanksgiving,
I beg for pity and forgiveness.

I humbly pray—

「The **Star Lords of the Northern Dipper (北斗七星尊神)**, the **Twenty-Eight Constellations (二十八宿)**, and the **Thirty-Five Star Officials (三十五星官)**—
**True Lord of the Dipper (司命君)**, **Star Official of Records (司录君)**, **Lord of Ease from Calamity (解厄君)**, **Lord of Ease from Punishment (解刑君)**, **Lord of Dispelling Disasters (消灾君)**, **Lord of Scattering Calamities (散祸君)**—
All **Star Lords (诸神君)**, I humbly beseech you to:
Dispel celestial disasters above,
Quell earthly calamities below,
Harmonize **yin** and **yang**,
Transform malevolent fate,
Remove yearly **commanding stars (年命厄会)** and **five-star punishments (三五刑克)**,
Avert sudden misfortunes and **unjustified calamities (非灾横祸)**,
Silence slander from officials and private individuals,
Ward off malevolent humans and vengeful ghosts.

May you grant my **Dao/Way and qi (道炁)**,
And perpetually protect my **chastity and auspiciousness (贞吉)**.

Your servant, prostrates and bows twice.
Three times, wine and incense are offered.

Your servant now humbly petitions the **mighty and numinous assembly of the Dipper Stars and Celestial Lodges (斗星天宿阖座威灵)**—
Though I am a humble novice, unworthy of ritual propriety,
My words are clumsy and my intent impure,
I have offended your sacred presence with countless sins.
Yet I still implore your compassion and forgiveness.

I earnestly pray for **longevity and eternal life (长生久视)**.
Your servant now prostrates and bows twice, offering this petition.

*[Prostrate and kneel, then suddenly rise.]*
Next, recite the **Inner Star Incantation (内神咒)**:
As I complete this **jiào (醮)**, the **officiers and attendants (将吏)** who have entered my body,
The **Functional Officials (功曹)** and **messengers (使者)**, all **Star Officials (诸官君)**—
Each returns through the **Gate of Ten Thousand Miracles (众妙门)**,
To the left if they came from the left, to the right if they came from the right,
Back to their **palaces (宫室)**, encircling my body and bones,
Spanning the heavens and earth, guarding the **hundred channels (百脉)**,
Without confusion or error, until summoned to reappear,
Just as before.

Next, rise and take the **tablets and seals (章函)**,
Recite the **Incantation of the Threefold Furnace (复炉咒)** three times:
To the **Incense Officials (香官)**, **messengers (使者)**,
The **Lords of the Left and Right Dragon-Tiger (左右龙虎君)**,
And the **attending Star Officials of the Incense (侍香诸灵官)**.

May this **jiào (醮)** summon forth:
**Golden Elixir, Lapis Lazuli, Immortal Mushrooms, and Sacred Herbs (金液丹碧芝英)**,
A gathering of **hundreds of True Ones and numinous spirits (众真百灵)**,
All convening before the incense and flames of this furnace.

May it grant me:
To **practice Dao and attain Dao (学道得道)**,
To **seek immortals and attain immortality (求仙得仙)**,
To bring blessings to my household,
To bestow grace upon all under heaven,
So that **ten thousand immortal children and jade maidens (十方仙童玉女)**,
Attending the **incense and smoke (香烟)**,
Convey my words directly to the **Supreme True Lord of the Boundless Dao, the Jade Sovereign of the Great Heavenly Emperor (至真无极玉皇大天帝)**.

Then, scatter the wine and food,
And immediately take the **tablets (简)**, step back,
Exit through the **Southern Angle (束南角)**,
First placing the right foot into the shoes,
Bow and farewell to the altar.

Next, recite the incantation:
*"From **yin** to **yang**, all matters open and flow.
The **Gate of Affairs (关启)** is now complete—
Prepare the **Palaces of the Immortals (仙宫)**."*

When finished, scatter the wine and food at will within the home,
Inviting the **twelve household deities (十二之神)**,
The **door wardens and gate guardians (门丞户尉)**,
The **generals of the dwelling (宅舍将军)**,
The **spirits of the well and hearth (井灶之神)**,
To partake and share in the feast.

May they also:
Array themselves in ranks to guard the home,
Prevent disasters from passing the door,
Avert epidemics from crossing the threshold,
Repel malevolent spirits and thieving ghosts,
So that none dare approach.

The **Great Dao’s sacred oath (大道盟威)** and the **Orthodox One’s secret precepts (正一秘法)**—
The matter is not trifling.
If you **guard and protect with merit (守镇有功)**,
And **promote blessings and assist in goodness (兴福助善)**,
On the **auspicious days of the Three Assemblies (三会吉日)**,
When the **ranked deities (同章)** are invoked for **transference (举迁)**,
Do not slacken—
Follow the law and **admonish or correct (弹纠)**,
Just as the **Heavenly Master’s statutes and commands (天师律令)** decree.

Scatter the wine and food.

If there is any sudden urgency,
Or matters of **illness or affliction (疾病事)**,
And you must **pray for resolution without delay (祈解一不可待)**—
Even if it concerns my **personal fate (本命)**—
Then use this day’s **ritual (此日)**.

*Note: This section is omitted as it appears in the same form in Volume II of the **Ritual for Transference of Personal Fate (醮本命仪)**.*

---
**Miscellaneous Rituals for the Celestial Gate and National Protection, Household Safety, Bodyguard, Disaster Relief, and Human Salvation (杂使天关助国安家护身出灾度厄救人济物众法)**

**The Most High Lao Jun (太上老君)** says:
*"As for the **determined practitioner (志人)**—
All who **seek the Dao with resolve (志人学道)**,
Must always **devote their heart with diligence and caution (切心谨慎)**,
Serve their **master as their teacher (师事於师)**,
And **observe their master’s countenance (视师颜色)**,
Ever fearing their master will not teach them the **refined methods and precepts (妙用之法诀)**.

If they **obtain the precepts (得诀)**,
Their resolve is like **piercing stone (志若穿石)**—
They do not **shift their practice (不移习)**,
Nor **cease their transformation (不休转)**,
Even as the years deepen.
With **unwavering sincerity (至诚不退)**,
They are called **those who take the Dao with resolve (志心取道)**—
The Dao does not **fail such practitioners (道不负人)**.

Nowadays, people have **words without true hearts (有口无心)**,
Their **intentions are not sincere (用心不真)**,
And **without the Dao, they lack spirit (非道无神)**.
Yet **those who seek the Dao with resolve (修学志道)**** attain clarity (生明)**,
And **command the Seven Stars of the Northern Dipper (驱使七星北斗)**.

The **methods (法)** are for:
Aiding the nation, safeguarding the family,
Guarding the body, rescuing the sick,
Saving humans, benefiting all things,
And **communing with the spirits (通神)**.
Thus, **ten thousand soldiers cannot seize them (万兵不能执)**,
Nor **a hundred ghosts dare deceive them (百鬼不能欺)**,
**A thousand disasters vanish on their own (千灾自灭)**,
And **ten thousand calamities are powerless before them (万祸敢为)**—
They **enter water and fire without drowning or burning (入水入火，不溺不烧)**,
And **no realm of terror can measure their dread (惊畏之地莫测)**,
All **knowing it in advance (心皆预知)**.
They **communicate with spirits and attain divinity (通灵通神)**,
And **become immortals without doubt (成仙无疑)**—
Their **wishes are all fulfilled (所愿皆得)**.
Yet **these are not the acts of the determined practitioner (志人不为)**.

The **determined practitioner (志人)**,
With **earnest heart and longing for the Dao (心切慕道)**,
Does not **perform these methods (不为诸法)**,
Except to **rescue others from illness (救人疾病)**—
Then they **act without delay (之外不行)**."*

**The Orthodox One of Later Saints (后圣君)** says:
*"The **Dao’s messengers (大道之使者)**,
None surpass the **Central Dipper (中斗)**—
Below, mortals call it the **Northern Dipper (北斗)**.

It has **nine visible stars (九星)**,
And **two unseen stars (不见二星)**.
Always within the Dipper,
One star is named **Imperial Lord (帝尊)**—
This is the **recorder of virtues and sins (罚恶记善)**,
And the **master of all stars (万星之主)**.

The scriptures say:
*'The Central Dipper has nine stars,
Two stars unseen.
One star rules all celestial stars,
Serving the **Great Dao (大道)**,
Called **Imperial Lord (帝尊)**.*

But the **nine stars of the Nine Wilds (九野中星)**,
Excluding the **Five Elements and Six Yang stars (五行六甲大星)**,
Are all **Imperial Lord (帝尊)**’s single star’s **deputies (差为使)**—
Their **missions are very important (所主使也甚要)**.

The **First Star of Authority (执权一星)**,
Is named **Jade Sovereign (玉帝)**—
It **rules all stars and lodges between heaven and earth (主天地之间星宿)**,
The **heavenly deities and earthly spirits (天神地只)**,
**Human spirits, dragons, and ghosts (人神龙鬼)**,
And **malevolent spirits and deceitful deities (精邪奸祆)**—
All are under this **Star Lord’s command (此星君所部主也)**.

If one has **meritorious deeds toward heaven, earth, and living beings (善功於天地人物)**,
This **Star Lord** governs them all.
If one has **meritorious deeds toward heaven, earth, and living beings (善功於天地人物)**,
This **Star Lord** commands the **Celestial Gate’s messengers (天关使者)**,
To **open the gate and report (关奏)**,
And **petition the Jade Sovereign, the Great Dao’s Supreme Emperor (玉皇上帝道君)**,
So that **meritorious deeds are recorded (以善功立)**,
And **grades are promoted through repeated transference (数迁阶进品禄)**—
Not only **longevity and immortals (长生仙人)**,
But also **officials, generals, and common folk (世之官将人民)**,
All are under this **Star Lord’s governance (皆所主也)**.

If one commits **wicked and rebellious crimes (凶恶祆逆之罪)**,
This **Star Lord** also rules over them.
Thus, the **Celestial Gate’s messengers (天关使者)**,
According to the **lightness or gravity of the crime (随罪轻重)**,
May **demote or execute (贬杀)**.

The **Celestial Gate (天关)** is the **high commander (上将)**.
One star is named **Jade Sovereign Lord (玉帝君)**—
It **supervises the gate’s reporting (上主关奏)**,
And **petitions the Most High Boundless Dao Emperor (太上无极大道玉皇帝大道君)**.
Thus, all **Star Officials (众官)** call it the **Jade Sovereign Star Lord (玉帝星君)**.
As stated in the previous section.

**Lao Jun (老君)** says:
*"To **transform the Celestial Gate (转天关)**,
And **subdue the wicked and rebellious (伐凶逆)**,
And **aid the nation and safeguard the people (助国安人)**—
This is the **method (法)**."*

The **Star General** first enters with the **Military Tiger Talisman (兵虎符)** into the **Hall of Tranquility (靖室)**, stepping upon the **Earthly Stems (地纪)** in forward, reversed, and inverted sequences—each three times—then invoking the **Celestial Rope (飞天纲)** three times.
Forward, reversed, and inverted—each three times.
Upon completion, lower the Rope, disperse into **Yú’s Steps (禹步)**—three strides, nine traces—then reverse into twelve steps, and again into fifteen steps. Beneath the Rope, align with the **clothing talisman (配衣)**, the left hand seizing the **Military Talisman (出军符)** to **transform the Celestial Gate (转天关)**.
With the **Nine Fingers (九指)**, point at the **rebellious traitors of the realm (逆国贼)** and their cohorts. Shout their names—
If near, the voice is small; if many, adjust accordingly.
Then recite the incantation:
*"Wicked and rebellious [name], you rebel against the Sovereign,
Gathering demonic bands, stealing and plundering wealth,
Slaying innocent folk.
The Most High does not permit this—
Great evil, great wrath!
Command the **Celestial Gate’s messengers (勑消转斗关津)**,
Threefold with the Nine Fingers,
To annihilate [name]’s band—
All prohibitions, by oral decree, are now enforced.
I command my ministers to act—
Transform and subdue, kill.
As the Law decrees, swiftly."*

**Pinch the blade talisman (捻刀支诀)**, the formula aligned with the **Five Phases calculations (五方算)**—
*"Eastward, the Wooden Man’s blade talisman—so be it."*
Within one day, invoke the Nine Fingers three times.
Do not exceed one hundred days—
The traitors will self-destruct.
This method is **wondrously efficacious**.
In antiquity, **Yellow Stone (黄石姿)** taught it to **Jiang Ziya (太公姜子牙)**, and it proved most effective.
Later, **Jiang Ziya** did not pass this method down.
The formula remains in the subsequent annotations.

**Lao Jun** says:
*"Humans are born of the **Five Phases (五行)**,
Beginning their fate with the **Six Jia (六甲)**—
There is flourishing and decline.
When flourishing, the **Southern Dipper (南斗)** governs;
When declining, the **Northern Dipper (北斗)** governs.
The Southern Dipper’s six stars—hence, **Six Jia**.
The Northern Dipper’s seven stars—hence, **Seven Mansions (七宿)**.
The Southern Dipper presides over life; the Northern Dipper, over death—
Thus, life and death belong to the **Two Dippers’ jurisdiction**.
If one commits wicked deeds, the **Northern Dipper’s Celestial Finger (天指)** turns against them.
Human flourishing and decline are all under the **Two Dippers’ scrutiny**.
If evil deeds accumulate to their limit, Heaven must punish—
Then the **Southern Dipper records the name (落名)**,
And the **Northern Dipper executes the form (斩形)**.
All human wickedness is slain by the **Northern Dipper**.
Now, if one commits **Five Evils**—
Rebelling against the **Dao/Way**, betraying the teacher,
Betraying the sovereign, betraying one’s father—
Heaven knows this early.
Yet if there are those with **virtuous intent**,
Serving as sovereign or teacher,
Subduing the wicked and rebellious,
Eradicating evil, upholding the **Rectified Way (正道)**,
And bringing peace to all—
Their merit is vast and enduring.
The Most High rejoices, elevating them to **Celestial Officials (仙官)**,
Sharing governance of the **Ten Heavens (十天)**,
Ascending to the **Supreme Clarity’s True Emperor (上清太真之位)**.
Other rites may save one’s family—
But this rite’s use is for **national salvation**.
Employ talismans and methods as prescribed.

**Lao Jun** instructs **Sìmìng (司命)** and his attendants:
*"In antiquity, **Sìmìng** was an attendant of the **Sovereign Lord (隶君)**—
Not the later **Sìmìng**.
Now, **Han Jun (韩君)** has replaced him—
This is his station.
The **Central Dipper (中斗)**, along with the **Southern and Northern Dippers**,
These three Dippers are upright—
They do not meddle without cause, bringing chaos.
If one petitions for blessings but instead invites calamity,
The **learners of the Dao** must first **know themselves** above all.
In days past, there was a **student of the Dao**, **Guō Shēngzǐ (郭声子)**,
Who burned incense day and night, worshipping the **Northern Dipper** without cease.
For seventeen years, the **Northern Dipper Lord** pursued and reproached him:
*'I, the Northern Dipper, am an **Inspector of Virtue and Vice (纠察之官)**,
Upright in enforcing the Law.
Day and night, I patrol the Nine Heavens.
If any star or constellation commits good or evil,
I know first—
Then I report to the **Celestial Sovereign (上帝)**.
The Sovereign frequently commands **Celestial Messengers and Daoist Officials (天使仙官)**,
To investigate and inspect, lest there be **unjust favoritism**.
We, the **Nine Inspectors (九司)**, always fear punishment for ourselves.
Who are you, so base and ignorant,
Burning incense nightly, publicly announcing to Heaven—
What do you seek?
Your actions have unsettled all nine stars.
Now, your deeds disturb the **Five Phases above**,
And alarm the **Twenty-Eight Constellations below**—
All have gathered to question me:
*"This man is harmless—
Why does he, through licentiousness and chaos,
Draw the **Celestial Inspectors’ scrutiny**?
Why not kill him first, then report?"*
Because you are but a mortal, I spare you—
Not that I harbor malice.
But now, bow and apologize.
Your crimes are threefold:
First, **false invocation**—
Without illness or misfortune, you petition the **Celestial Gate (天关)**,
Demanding the **Gate’s messengers (转关使者)** punish some person or thing.
Second, you **burn incense endlessly**,
Worshipping the Northern Dipper from afar—
I fear the **Chen Star (辰星)** will accuse me,
Claiming I **privately accepted your offerings**.
Third, the **Female Star of the Northern Dipper (北斗女星君)** is of **serene and chaste nature**—
To **wrongfully harm her** would invite retribution upon your lineage.
And the **Northern Dipper’s Imperial Lord (北斗帝尊君)**,
As well as the **Jade Sovereign Star Lord (玉帝君)**—
These two stars are upright and difficult to offend.
Now, I release you—
But never repeat this folly."*
Guō Shēngzǐ was spared and lived again,
But died five days later.
His kin asked why—
He never spoke.
Later, this was recorded in the **Ritual Texts of the Seven Stars and Twenty-Eight Constellations (醮七星及二十八宿文仪)**,
To warn future generations.
If one faces **urgent peril**—
Surrounded by bandits, harassed by officials,
Or stricken with grave illness—
After petitioning, step upon the **Celestial Rope (纲)** and tread the **Earthly Stems (蹑纪)**,
Transform the **Celestial Gate (转天关)**,
And dispel the calamity—
It poses no hindrance and is **swift as water or fire**.
The **Later Sage Sovereign (后圣君)** told **Dàwáng Jūn (大王君)**:
*"The **Central and Northern Dippers**,
If invoked in **genuine distress**, will respond.
But **false petitions** bring ruin.
Refer to the previous annotations.
Those who cultivate the **Supreme Dao (至道)** with sincerity,
First **aid the nation and benefit the people**—this is paramount.
If the realm is not purified, **demonic qi (妖气)** lingers.
If the people are not at peace, the **Dao cannot prevail**.
If one’s practice of the Dao fails,
This is not the heart of a **true Daoist."**

This too is the words of **Lǎojūn (老君)**.
