In ancient times, **Fúxià Zǐ (伏夏子)**, the younger brother of **Fúxī (伏牺)**, cultivated the **Dao/Way** and attained immortality. While studying in the mortal realm, he took a small bamboo flute and blew it, imitating the **Fèng (凤)** phoenix’s voice—this is the origin of the **shēng (笙)**.

A **celestial immortal** descended to observe him. Afterward, the immortal informed **Fúxià Zǐ**:
*"You are in danger of military calamity."*

**Fúxià Zǐ** rose and bowed twice, then asked how to avert the military peril. The immortal replied:
*"You may use **Lónghuí (龙回)**, which is the step of the **Earthly Stems (蹑地纪)** method for breaking formations. **Hǔtiào (虎跳)** is the step of the **Fēigāng (飞钢)** today. **Yǐnxīng (引星)** corresponds to the **configuring of ritual garments (配衣)** now. **Zhuǎnshā (转杀)** is done at the fingertips—this is the **Celestial Gate (转天关)** of today. **Cóngjī xiànghuài (从基向坏)** refers to the **foundational alignment (即今之日月建地)** and its **dissolution (即今之日破地)**.

The strategies of martial masters for calculating **isolated and empty formations (孤虚)** resemble these methods, and they are highly reliable. Those of old who were **divine sages (神人)** all employed them. When used correctly, they yield victory.

After **Fúxià Zǐ** learned these methods, he used them to rescue those in **genuine distress (急难)** who practiced the **Dao/Way**. **Lǎojūn (老君)** said:
*"For **Daoist companions (道友)** and **inner kin (内亲)**, surrounded by bandits and facing annihilation—if one can devise a plan to save them, they should employ the **Earthly Stems (金地纪)** method in motion: forward, backward, and reverse, three times. Then configure the ritual garments (**配衣**), turn the **Celestial Gate (转天关)**, and ninefoldly point with the fingers (**指之**). Additionally, grasp the **military talisman (兵符)**, pointing it nine times. Twist the **bandit’s command (贼某命人刀支)**—the **Sword-Support (刀支)** of the **wood-directional bandit (东来木人)** is marked with **metallic-white (金白)**, the **gold-directional bandit (西来金人)** with **flaming-red (火赤)**, the **water-directional bandit (南来水人)** with **earthly-yellow (土黄)**, the **fire-directional bandit (北来火人)** with **water-black (水黑)**, and the **earth-directional bandit (四季上来者土人)** with **bamboo-green (木青)**. The four seasons are represented by **chén, xuǔ, chǒu, wèi (辰戌丑未)**.

When twisting the **Sword-Support (刀支)**, use the hand corresponding to its direction. Then, apply the color as described. Afterward, take out the **military talisman (兵符)** and point it nine times at a distance. The bandits’ resolve will collapse, and they will retreat, lifting the siege without harming your **inner kin (反亲)**. If they refuse to retreat, the **shadow army (阴军)** will strike them, and they will mutually slaughter and destroy each other until none remain.

This method is subtle and of utmost secrecy—do not reveal it to anyone unworthy.

The **Later Sage Sovereign (后圣君)** told the **Celestial Master (天师)**:
*"This talisman is for military use—both to aid the nation in battle and to rescue **Daoist companions (道友)** and one’s own life. There is a talisman, the **Tiger King Talisman (虎王符)**, forged from **gold and copper (金铜)**, measuring either two inches or one and a half inches. The **Celestial Master (本师)** must consecrate and empower it. Then, store it in a **brocade pouch (锦袋)**, ensuring no one ever sees it. Only four may behold it: the **Celestial Master (本师)** and the **protector of the Master (保举师)**. If the protector fails or is struck down remotely, the talisman’s power will vanish, and it will never be seen again. The second category includes **sovereigns receiving subjects (君受臣)** and **subjects receiving sovereigns (臣受君)**. The third are **fathers receiving sons (父受子)** and **sons receiving fathers (子受父)**. The fourth are **husbands and wives (夫妻)**. Others must never see it.

If **Daoist companions (道友)** or **inner kin (内亲)** wish to carry it for healing, seal it tightly and give it to the sick person. The illness will immediately abate. If the sick person secretly examines it, the illness will flare up, and they will die without fail.

**Out-Military Talisman (出军)**
If one personally leads an army and is besieged, and the troops break through the enemy’s formation, the talisman must be tied to the **left elbow (左肘)**. There is another talisman, the **White Tiger Talisman for Breaking Strong Formations (白虎破强阵符)**, also forged from **gold and copper (金铜)**, measuring one and a half inches. Its method of use is the same as the previous talisman’s annotations. All talismans are cast from **gold and copper (金铜)**—the **in-military talisman (入军符)** is tied to the **left elbow (左)**, and the **out-military talisman (出军符)** to the **right elbow (右)**.

Together with the **ritual postures and prohibitions (并式禁制)**, and the **spirit of the talisman (加临相助)**, one will inevitably achieve victory. The enemy will collapse like a mountain—this is highly effective. Do not reveal it to anyone unworthy.

**Lǎojūn (老君)** said:
*"In ancient times, the **Western Hu (西胡)** had a great king who loved the **Dao/Way**. I instructed him through the **Hu Immortal (胡仙)**, and he changed his name to **Fó (佛)**—a different name for **celestial immortal (仙)**. The Hu called him **Fó**.

The Four **Celestial Realms (天国)** did not submit, each fielding **strong armies (强兵)** of four hundred thousand men. They surrounded this king’s realm, layer upon layer. The king begged for deliverance but refused to comply. His **true heart (正心)** and **sincere intent (思存)** were evident—I saw him in the void, calling for my aid.

I used the **Earthly Stems (蹑地纪)** to scatter radiance, the **Yǔbù (禹步)** to turn the **Celestial Gate (关)**, and pointed three times. Then, I released a **military talisman (出军一符)** toward the Hu king’s desk. The king saw it, tied it to his **left elbow (左手肘)**, and later opened the city gates to battle. Those who fought against this king all fell backward, and the enemy armies were utterly defeated, slaughtered by the city’s defenders.

In but a moment, the **heavens and earth (天地)** grew enraged, and thunderous winds shook the heavens and earth. White rain descended, annihilating the Four **Celestial Armies (天军)**. The armies and their king scattered and fled back to their own lands, unharmed in their positions.

Thus, the **virtue/power (力)** of this talisman is supreme. Guard it carefully—do not let anyone unworthy see it. If they do, both parties will face retribution, and the **Heaven’s great wrath (天大威)** will bring death. This is no trivial matter—be cautious, be cautious.

**The Method of the Red Chapter for Aiding the Nation and Subduing Bandits (赤章助国伐贼法)**
**Tàishàng Lǎojūn (太上老君)** said:
*"Rescue is the **virtue/power (功)** of aiding the nation in subduing bandits, saving the nation from difficulty. When **kings and emperors (国王帝主)** dispatch great ministers to attack rebellious bandits, but are instead besieged—if one is a **master of martial law (掌法)** and a **true Daoist (志道之人)**, they should aid the nation in its salvation.

Use the **Red Chapter (上赤章)** to summon the **Heavenly Armies (天兵)**, turn the **Celestial Gate (转天关)** to rescue them—swift as water or fire in urgency. If the nation’s strong bandits retreat, with neither side harmed, this is the highest outcome.

If the bandits are **strong and unyielding (强梁不伏)**, petition the **Heavenly Sovereign (天公)**—now called **Yùhuáng Dìshàng (玉皇上帝)**—and write their crimes. This is **Heaven’s retribution (天施功)**. If the **virtue/power (功)** is great and **Heaven does not strike (天不伐)**, the act of **subduing and killing (蹑杀)** will instead be recorded as the **hidden merit (阴功)** of saving people.

**Nurturing and protecting all beings (安养人物)**.
This pleases **Heaven greatly (此天大喜)**, and **Heaven will devise a plan (与计)** for the **hidden merit (阴功)**.

Later sages changed this to the **Red Chapter (赤章)**—a **chapter of petition against traitors (章奏反臣章)**—saying, *'Tàixuān Dū (泰玄都)' and so forth."*

The Sovereign humbly follows the written petition: *"In such-and-such state and county, a certain person [X] has rebelled for such-and-such reason.*

Now the state commands a certain minister [Y] to lead an army of tens of thousands of soldiers and horses to the border of such-and-such state, to attack the rebel forces numbering tens of thousands. Fearful that their troops are fierce, rebellious, and strong, recklessly slaughtering the innocent and resisting the righteous, refusing to submit, the minister now finds himself besieged within such-and-such city’s encampment, unable to escape, with his life hanging by a thread. He seeks the minister’s salvation.

The minister petitions for **Heavenly troops**: humbly requesting the descent of the **Nine Heavenly Great Mighty Gods**, the **Nine Great Generals**, with **ninety million soldiers**, to unite with the minister’s **talismanic army of ninety million**, summoning the **nine million earthly community temple troops** to secretly deploy and array themselves. When the minister’s [X] **sun-facing troops** sound the battle drum, the troops shall immediately strike in response, aiding in the assault against the rebels. Their fierce and treacherous forces shall collapse in an instant—like mountains crumbling to dust, or stones shattering—sand collapsing, deer fleeing, surrendering and clearing the path for the general’s forces to emerge victorious.

Further, the minister requests the **White Tiger Talisman**, commanding **19,000 officers and soldiers**, capable of subduing vast armies, whose might shakes Heaven and Earth, whose strength can uproot mountains and drain the seas, to assist the minister [Y] and the general in striking down the rebels.

Later, the **Sage Sovereign** instructed the **Heavenly Master**: *"You must act with discernment. If he is truly a rebel against the sovereign, then proceed. If not, do not. Be cautious."*

「Do not rashly grant this military authority, lest the blame fall upon yourself.

The Heavenly Master said: *"The Dao/Way has no impossibilities; act as your heart dictates."* Yet, one must first gauge human intent and measure the feasibility of action, lest there be reckless deeds. When dealing with those whose **志 (aspirations)** align with yours and who are **志道友 (friends in the Dao/Way)**, if they wish to submit this petition, they must first assess that neither the petitioner nor themselves hold any faults, and only then may they present it to the Sage Sovereign.

If the petitioner has faults, and others appear faultless, one must not involve themselves, lest they too incur greater faults. This is the case when two individuals inform Heaven of their own wrongdoings, and the punishment is swift—within moments, disciples may rebel against their teacher, or teachers may invoke the **灵官 (Spiritual Official)** to petition against their own students.

This petition is originally recorded in the *Dà Zhāng Yí* [Great Ritual Code], now further inscribed here for reference. The Sage Sovereign summons the **Spiritual Official** to subdue disciples and malevolent commoners who, through **孤恩 (isolated kindness)** and **负道 (betraying the Dao/Way)**, invoke the Spiritual Official to dissolve the petition and restore illness—just as in the original petition.

The *Zá Zhāng Yí* [Miscellaneous Ritual Code] contains this, so it is not written again; its contents have already been listed.

**Issuing Talismans and Ritual Edicts to Restrain the Three Officials’ Malevolent Forces**

Among the **三官 (Three Officials)**—Heaven, Earth, and Water—there are malevolent forces and malevolent individuals: **神龙 (Divine Dragons)**, **鬼精 (Ghostly Spirits)**, and **妖 (demons)** are such.

The Heavenly Master said: *"The petitioner is **罗文能强 (Luo Wen Nengqiang)**."* His surname is **罗 (Luo)**, his given name is **文能 (Wen Neng)**, and his courtesy name is **强 (Qiang)**.

*"As for mortals, they are the most honored among the **三才 (Three Powers)**—Heaven, Earth, and Humanity. All things of reverence place their weight upon the human body and seek to nurture its nature. One must always ponder the Dao/Way’s principles and safeguard one’s life and vitality.**

**存师 (Preserve the teacher), 想道 (contemplate the Dao/Way).**
**存金箓之师 (Preserve the teacher of the Golden Seal).**
The teacher of the Golden Seal refers to the **度师 (Master of Initiation)** from the *Jīnsuǒ Liúzhū* [Golden Lock, Flowing Pearl]. The Golden Seal’s Dao/Way was later reformed by the Sage Sovereign into the *Jīnsuǒ Liúzhū* [Golden Lock, Flowing Pearl].

In the **上古 (Ancient Times)**, the **真人 (Sage)** revered the Golden Seal talisman and honored the Golden Seal Master of Initiation. The Divine Soldiers of the Golden Seal would summon with a **咄叱 (commanding cry)**, dispersing ghosts and spirits, and the talismans would drive away malevolent forces, always saving lives. These are my disciples.

This talisman, the **玄孙符计 (arcane inheritance of talismans and strategies)**, is used to defend oneself and others, making it easy to attain merit. Later, one will attain the Dao/Way and become a **上等真人 (highest rank of Sage)**.

**Do not rely on mere sound (声).**
Sound refers to the chanting of scriptures, reciting praises during fasting rituals, and the murmurs of Dao/Way contemplation. **Do not rely on mere images (像).**
Images refer to statues in halls of reverence, official shrines, and temple deities—all part of the **像教 (teaching through images)**.

If one can abandon **有为 (worldly pursuits)** and instead turn their heart inward toward the **至道 (Ultimate Dao/Way)**, practicing the silent, ineffable teachings, advancing through **阴功 (hidden merit)**, and refining their conduct, they will attain **无为之德 (the virtue of non-action)** and achieve the Dao/Way.

My Dao/Way is entirely based on **行阴德 (practicing hidden virtue)**, borrowing **阴功 (hidden merit)** to fulfill its requirements. When merit is complete and the Dao/Way is realized, my teachings are passed on, and when the **年劫数 (age and kalpa)** are fulfilled, all receive this transmission based on their **因师 (karmic connection with the teacher)**.

After receiving it, do not rashly transmit to unworthy individuals. In the world, there are **贤达 (virtuous and enlightened)** individuals who, trusting in gold and jade, will pass it on. The Heavenly Master instructed those of good conduct among the Sages:

*"If one’s aspirations align with the teachings and the recipient is virtuous yet lacks faith, then one must rely on their own sincerity. If the recipient’s struggles and joys are understood, then one may transmit to them, provided that the teacher and disciples together fulfill the required offerings. Then, one may inform Heaven and be granted the transmission—do not sever the path of Heaven’s Dao/Way.*

*"If the recipient is virtuous but lacks wealth, the teacher and disciples may assist in providing offerings before transmission. One must not transmit without faith, nor must one transmit to those who are not virtuous and enlightened simply because they possess wealth or treasures. If one accepts wealth and transmits recklessly, both teacher and disciple will die, and Heaven will punish them for revealing its treasures.*

**慎之慎之 (Be cautious, be cautious)."**

End of the **Second Scroll of the *Jīnsuǒ Liúzhū* [Golden Lock, Flowing Pearl] Ritual Edicts.**
Begin the **Twenty-Third Scroll of the *Jīnsuǒ Liúzhū* [Golden Lock, Flowing Pearl] Ritual Edicts.**

The **Grand Sovereign of the Celestial Masters of China**, **Zǎiwáng Fāngpíng Zhāng Dàolíng**, along with **Zhào Shēng, Wáng Cháng, Sīmìng Lǐ Zhòngfǔ, Máoyíng, Xǔ Yùfǔ**, and others, compiled and transmitted this across generations.

**Lǐ Chúnfēng**, the Daoist Sage of China, annotated the **Method of Writing Talismans, Exorcising Evil, and Treating Illnesses**.

The **Most High Lord Lao** spoke to **Luò Tiānshī**, saying:
*"If you wish to perform hidden merit, nothing surpasses granting talismans. The highest merit is to heal demonic illnesses—saving one person earns the merit of ten. For those afflicted by demonic illness enter households, disturbing both people and things. When one falls ill, they can disrupt an entire village, tormenting ten households. Thus, saving ten earns tenfold merit.

By severing the vital essence of demonic ghosts, spirits, and malevolent *qi*, their lives are not taken as punishment but as merit earned.

Later, the **Sage Emperor** spoke to **Zhang Tiānshī**, saying:
*'When you treat people’s illnesses and their afflictions are cured, if the demon is condemned to be slain, it is not a crime but merit earned. If it was not a demon but you recklessly issued a summons and executed it, you risk inviting disaster—this would be a grave and unjust offense. You, teacher and disciples, must pass on the teaching with caution and never do such things. My Dao has no pardon for this.*

**Laozi** said:
*'To prohibit and restrain celestial foxes so they no longer torment humans and Heaven, you must obtain the name of the afflicted person. Then, pinch the celestial demon’s eye—even celestial foxes can be captured.

The eyes of celestial beasts include those of the **celestial tiger, celestial dog, celestial ox, celestial leopard, celestial fox**, and other beasts.*

The **Sage Emperor** said:
*'Celestial beasts such as the **qílín, shīzǐ (lion), and the twelve *gāngfēng* (wind-riding) steeds** are known in the world as the hundred and six *chén* (dusts). Six-legged beasts—such as the **celestial deer, celestial sheep, celestial monkey**, and others—number three hundred and sixty, too many to list individually. All these beasts have secret talismanic eyes and blade-seals (*juédāo zhī*), recorded in the *Seventh Scroll of the Flowing Pearl* under the name *Zhǎngjué* (Palm Seals). These seals and blade-seals can bind and sever all beasts, preventing them from inflicting illness upon humans.

If demonic *qi* lingers within a person’s body, first administer the **Swallowing Demon-Illness Talisman** for twenty-one, twenty-eight, or thirty-five days, wearing the talisman and summons. There is no case where this fails to permanently cure and sever the affliction. These talismans are found in the *Three Sections of Miscellaneous Talismans*.

If demonic spirits have knowledge of divine communication, they will retreat and dare not return to torment.

For those who are stubborn, wicked, and refuse to accept the Dao’s teachings, you may **tread the *Dìjì* (Earth Memorization) three times**, recite the **Reversed, Inverted, and Flying Heavenly Ropes three times**, and take **Yǔbù (Great Flood Steps) three steps with nine traces**. Upon completion, transform the three steps into twelve steps—there is an illustration of this in the earlier scrolls.

Then, **adjust the clothing**: with your left hand, point to the **Heavenly Middle Magic King’s Palace**, invoking the **Golden-Copper Dragon Talisman of the Heavenly Messengers**, and with your right hand, grasp and summon it. Nine times, this talisman transforms into a **ten-thousand-*zhàng* dragon**, rushing to the **Heavenly Bureau of Demons’ Palace** to seize celestial foxes and beasts, swift as water and fire.

Regarding the **Decisive Rod**, the scripture states:
*'Celestial foxes need not be killed—merely strike them twenty times, bind them, and send them to the Eastern Sea, where the Water Official will detain them for ten, five, fifteen, or twenty years, depending on the judgment of the summoned master.*

The decree states:
*'Bind and restrain these celestial foxes. Those who violate this prohibition will be punished accordingly. After binding, send them to the Water Official for detention of so many years.*

The **Sage Emperor** spoke to **Tiānshī**, saying:
*'When treating the illnesses of the common people, you must always enforce prohibitions, measuring the lightness or severity of their offenses before passing judgment. Judgment should spare the ghosts and spirits, lest they suffer grievously. If they suffer grievously, they may lose their original forms—how much more so if they seek rebirth among humans, taking on human bodies!*

According to the *Sūtra on Causes and Conditions of Birth and Death*, these ghostly spirits are already discontented in their forms, yet they further harm and torment others. When summoned by a Daoist master and found guilty, they should be condemned to death but not executed on the spot. If their poisonous *qi* remains unresolved and they are slain, they will transform into venomous snakes, taking a thousand years to escape their serpentine form, only to be reborn as poultry or dogs among humans—having never attained a human life.

You must refrain from binding and restraining others in this manner. Over time, as the months and years pass, they will naturally regret their actions, confess their guilt, and seek release. In dreams, they may warn and guide others to find them, allowing them to depart for another world. After fulfilling their term as ghosts, they may be reborn into human life—but only as lowly, impoverished beings. How could they ever become noble?

You must remember my words and **never recklessly issue talismans or summonses**.

He also said:
*'Talismans are merely the假威力 (*jiǎ wēilì*—false authority) of the Dao, used to pacify and sever demonic spirits so they do not harm people and things. Summonses are curses—using the Dao’s authority to admonish and scold spirits, preventing them from causing mischief. You must practice this well. If done correctly, it brings merit; if done recklessly, it brings guilt.*

**Laozi addressed the Thirty-Three Heavenly Imperial Lords** in the *Sūtra on Guiding Beings Across*:

*'There are thirty-two heavens—why does this differ from other scriptures? The four directions, each with eight heavens, make thirty-two, excluding the Central Heaven. Now, including the Central Heaven, there are thirty-three Heavenly Imperial Lords—this is the correct count.

The **Primordial Heavenly Venerable** possesses **eighty-four thousand golden talismans** and the same number of jade talismans. He is called the **Elemental Sovereign, Most Sacred Great Dao Lord**.

The **Most High Great Dao Lord** has **twelve thousand golden talismans** and the same number of jade talismans. He is called the **Master of Ten Thousand Dao**.

The **Most High Lord Lao** also has **twelve thousand golden talismans** and the same number of jade talismans. He is called the **Emperor of the Void, Great Dao, Jade Dawn**, and is known as the **Former Sage**.

When the **Supreme Lord Lao** ascended, he was titled the **Pacified Heavenly Golden Gate Jade Dawn Later Sage, Primordial Supreme Dao Lord**. As recorded in the *Taiping Jing*, he is also called the **Jade Emperor of Heaven**.

Additionally, the *Jīnquè Yùjīng* states:
*'The Supreme Lord Lao bears the surname **Lǐ** and given name **Ēr**, with the courtesy name **Bóyáng**."*

The **Lord Lao’s Manifested Form** also. The records state: *"Later Body."* He ascended to the **Supreme Pure Dao Lord’s station**, with hair and beard as white as frost, clad in luminous jade robes. His rank surpassed that of the Later Sage, and he was honored as the **Jade Emperor**. In the Dao, he is invoked as the **Jade Emperor of Heaven**; in the secular world, as the **Heavenly Patriarch Emperor**.

He holds **thirteen thousand golden talismans**—originally meant to be four thousand, but the Later Sage Lord declined them, thus elevating the **Primordial Supreme Venerable’s station**. The jade talismans match in number. The **Heavenly Sovereign Lord** has three thousand golden talismans, with the same in jade. The **Celestial Master Lord** likewise holds three thousand golden talismans, with the same in jade. For lesser **True Immortals and High Ascetics**, their allotment is set at three hundred, two hundred, or one hundred talismans.

The **Lord of Life and Records** holds thirty-six talismans. The **Chief Examiners and Summoners of the Orthodox Law**—and the **Nine Regions’ Examiners and Summoners of the Law**—hold the rank of **Orthodox Teachers**, each granted thirty-six talismans. Their distribution follows the ranks of the **Peripatetic Saints**, with talismans assigned according to station; none may reveal them lightly.

The Later Sage Lord declared to the **Great King Lord**:
*"The Chief Examiners and Summoners of the Orthodox Law are granted thirteen additional talismans, totaling forty-nine—thirteen added to the original twenty-six."* Their names are recorded in the *Removal of the Residence* scroll. When distributing talismans in the amount of nine, they must be forged in gold and bronze, and carried by those afflicted with severe illness or grave misfortune—such talismans drive out disease. In military applications, they are sealed in multiple layers of brocade pouches before being given to others. **Never let them be seen by others**, for if viewed, their divine efficacy vanishes. Their nature is direct yet harsh, and their form is coarse and ominous—such that they should not be exposed.

The manifestations of divine powers upon seeing [the talismans] are fierce and boundless in the sky, yet they harm the afflicted—those whose ailments flare up and cannot be endured. **Beware, beware.**

The disciples of **Upper Clarity Three Pure** may be granted seven talismans and five methods. **Lingbao** may be granted six talismans, and **Orthodox Unity Alliance威** five. If the **Law of the Three Elements and Six Methods** is the supreme method of the world, one may, according to the **Precepts of the Most High Lord Lao**, be granted thirty-six talismans. The **Later Sage Lord’s Law** grants forty-nine talismans. These are to be bestowed according to the rank and seniority of the Daoist officials—**none may recklessly receive or practice them**, for heaven and earth forbid it.

In ancient times, **Ge Xuan**, the original master, received ten golden talismans of the **Abundant Dao**, using wooden tablets to inscribe spells and deceive the world. He also forged talismans of gold and bronze, imprinting them on paper to perform magic, killing ghosts and spirits, and bewitching people with transformations—his misdeeds were countless. The **Netherworld reported him to the Celestial Bureau**, which then petitioned the **Most High Later Sage Lord**, who condemned his great evil, demoting him two ranks and granting only the **Way of Immortality**. Because his Dao was false, it brought no benefit to mortals, and in truth, it harmed ghosts. Later scholars must be cautious and not follow his example.

For matters such as **using talismans to heal illness, protect the body, suppress malevolence, avert disaster, and dispel omens**, all methods must be properly observed.

The **Most High Lord Lao** said:
*"Those who practice Daoist methods are called Daoists or revered masters, yet they must abandon these titles. If they teach commoners or officials how to write talismans without proper authorization, recklessly inscribing and distributing them without purpose, they do not even mention the **shrine officials or divine offices**, nor do they know if those who wear the talismans truly believe. Such talismans are mere **precise counterfeit deceptions**—mere **shrine records without substance**. If they are but inked paper or old scraps, how could they cure disease? Such men, who falsely claim to be Daoists, are truly pitiful and lamentable."*

The first three or five lines are the words of the **Most High Lord Lao**; the rest are spoken by **Lu Tianxiang**.

**Talismans and warrants** must specify the number of talismans issued, the destination (e.g., *"to the household of so-and-so to heal illness"*), and the time limit. When finished, report to the **Right Community and Soil Deity**, sending them along with the person.

After recording the year, month, day, and hour, the warrant summons a certain official Daoist master to act.

**Lu Tianxiang** said:
*"I received the oral precepts of the Most High Lord Lao. When giving talismans to others, one must have a **warrant of authority** and seal them properly. The warrant is what we now call the **authorization**. After issuing it, one must recite the **Sealing Ghosts Incantation** twice while stepping on the **Earth’s Veins**, and chant the following three times:*

**‘Most High Lord Lao, born before Heaven and Earth.
Illuminated by the Nine Qi, he dispels all spirits.
The shrine deities tremble—living without form.
The dead assume false names.
They do not appear in the Ghost Register, yet they must be executed.
Upon receiving this warrant, reveal your true form!
Though you are but a mountain ghost, you shall not wrongfully harm the sick.
Cease harming Daoist citizen [Name], and swiftly return their **three souls and seven spirits**.
Wear your true form, as decreed by the Most High.
Urgent, as the Law commands.’**

After chanting this incantation, the talisman’s efficacy is proven. If the illness is caused by a malevolent spirit, the patient shall recover upon speaking the words. Only then may one be called a **Communing-with-Spirits Daoist** and seek immortality."

**Lu Tianxiang** further said:
*"I see Daoists in the world who cannot even heal their own illnesses, yet they still prescribe medicines for others—how much more absurd is it that they would dare to heal others? Such men still dare to seek the Dao of Immortality—how laughable and pitiful they are!"*

**Methods for healing illness, suppressing ghosts, and issuing warrants to banish malevolent spirits** are outlined in the *Precepts of the Most High Lord Lao’s Golden Mouth and Jade Statutes*:

*"The Precepts govern the righteous and suppress the wicked, subdue spirits, and aid humanity. The **Golden Statutes** contain **three hundred and sixty precepts**, and the **Jade Statutes** have **thirty volumes and fifteen thousand conditions**. They regulate gods, humans, dragons, and ghosts—**precise spirits, demons, and malevolent qi**—and impose punishments without leniency.

The **Jade Statutes** originally comprised fifteen thousand conditions, divided into sixty volumes. Now, from these sixty volumes, I have selected the **thirty-six essential incantations and methods**, recorded in the ninth section, to be used in **saving people, suppressing ghosts, and issuing warrants**.

The **warrants** within these conditions are used to **command celestial and earthly deities**, arrest and interrogate, and judge the guilt or innocence of spirits and humans—**to establish merit, protect the living, and suppress malevolent forces**.

**First**, the method for **national defense against evil**—against wicked humans and malevolent ghosts—is to issue a **warrant to the local territorial deity**, beginning with:
*'Consider and summon the Daoist master. Warrant to [Name] of [Mountain/Region] and [Divine Official], etc. The name of the deity must be specified.'*

The warrant states:
*'Regarding the case of [Name], a resident of [County/Region], who has committed [Crime] at [Location], etc.'*

This follows the format of **official state documents**, but the concluding clause must read:
*'By law, this warrant is issued to [Shrine/Deity]. It does not state "investigation required."'* For the **Most High Lord Lao’s methods**, only the word **"Law"** is used.

**Second**, the method for **suppressing ghosts afflicting the sick**—for minor spirits—is to issue a warrant to the **shrine deity and the household deity**, permanently prohibiting their interference. It reads:
*'Consider and summon the Daoist master. Warrant to [County] Duji [Shrine].
Today, Lu Tianxiang first adds the **City God Official**.
Received from the commoners or officials—specify their names.
The petition states:
*"[Name], male or female, suffers from [Illness].
Since [Year/Month/Day], the illness has worsened, with signs of malevolent qi clinging to the body, unresolved despite all treatments.
Now, with sincere devotion, I rely on the Great Dao to heal and suppress the ghostly bandits.
I humbly request your judgment."*

**Translation:**

*"Consider and summon the Daoist master*—now sealed and presented to the Jade Emperor of Heaven, requesting a change in the title of the summoned Daoist master to **‘Summoning Righteous Envoy’**, so that all ghosts and spirits of the land may know and submit.

The judgment reads as follows:

Once the judgment is complete, it is stated:
*'According to the law, a **Day-Symbol Official** must be dispatched to issue a warrant and pursue the malevolent ghost-bandits, with the following decree:

For grave offenses, it shall decree **‘beheaded’**; for lesser offenses, **‘a hundred strokes’**. The afflicted shall be confined and ordered to recover within a set number of days.

After reporting upward, it is further stated:

On the [Year/Month/Day/Hour], the **Day-Symbol Official** Zhao Rui issued the warrant.

Zhao Rui was the son of **Zhao Sheng**, a disciple of **Zhang the Daoist Master** during the reign of Emperor An of Han. Having perfected his Daoist studies, he mastered countless prohibitive arts, yet never used them to kill humans. Instead, he employed them as a jest within human affairs. He casually hunted and executed ghosts and spirits, though he did not consider saving the sick his merit. Often, he would slaughter malevolent spirits and spirits of snakes, insects, dragons, tigers, and leopards—killing them in droves."*

「He could command the rivers to cease their flow, make orange trees bloom with flowers and leaves, and walk upon water as if on land. He would weave reeds into boats and ferry dozens of people across the river—no more. When people were in the water, the boats appeared as real vessels to them; yet once they reached the riverbank, the boats were merely reed leaves.

During the reigns of Emperor Xuan and Emperor Cheng, he was highly esteemed. He was ennobled as a **Hardy Marquis** (硕侯), and the Princess of Xianyang was married to him. His title was further elevated to **Heroic** (雄) and **Efficacious** (用). For over seventy years, he enslaved the ghosts and spirits of the world without cease. The **Dao-spirits** (鬼神) grew resentful and their grievances reached the heavens. The **Supreme Sage** (太上) and the **Holy Sovereign** (后圣君) were enraged, and in retribution, they demoted him two ranks as a **Celestial Official** (仙), granting him an immortal lifespan but condemning him to serve as a **Daoist Summoner** (考召法师) for 1,500 years, recording the deeds of those who invoke him.

The wind requested permission to be listed among the **Daoist Summoners** (考召使). Thus, the wind was again granted favor, and his essence was returned to the **Central Peak** (中岳) for cultivation. His new role was to **Daoist Summoner** (考召使), tasked with performing **Daoist rites** (行法) to heal human illnesses and alleviate sudden calamities, thereby atoning for his past transgressions of taking life. In time, he would surely ascend to become a **Great Sage** (大仙).

For now, his term of punishment has not yet expired, and his lineage continues. Later disciples who attain **Daoist power** (得道力) must not recklessly employ it—be cautious, be cautious. The wind often deceives, and even those in the lineage of the **Celestial Sage Ge Xuan** (上仙葛玄) are not exempt from such errors or failures.

**Third**, when the world suffers prolonged drought, crops wither, and farmers face ruin, there are indeed those who die from scorching heat. In secret, he performs **Daoist rites** (行法) to summon and bind the **Dragon Officials** (龙吏) of the **Community Altars** (社庙), dispatching them to bring rain and save the situation. This is a great virtue and merit.

The **Celestial Master Lao** (老君) said: When the world suffers prolonged drought, there are indeed those harmed by it. One may perform the rite at night when all is still: within a chamber where no one can see, tread the ground three times in **Yujian’s Pattern** (蹑地纪), then three times in **Flying Youth’s Pattern** (飞夭纲), forward, backward, and reversed. Finally, scatter the steps into **Yu’s Three-Step, Nine-Trace Pattern** (禹步三步九迹).

When done, recite the incantation:
*"Supreme Sage Li Lao, in the Ninefold Celestial Realm above,
Amidst the myriad layers of colorful clouds,
Riding the Qilin.
By command, I dispatch the Great True Officials (大真王) below,
Jo, to issue the warrant.
Summon the Dragon Officials (龙吏)—those of the Month, Day, and Hour—
To bring rain."*

When the incantation is complete, don the ritual robes and return. With the right hand, perform the **Heavenly Seal** (天关), pointing toward the Dragon Stream Pool (龙溪潭) within the palm. After pointing, instruct the scribes to prepare the warrant. If there is a grand temple near the pool, the warrant is delivered there. If no grand temple exists, the warrant is issued and dispatched to the Dragon Stream Pool, ordering the dragons to bring rain. The dragons within the pool will respond promptly, and the rain will descend swiftly—even faster than the quenching of water and fire.

If one recognizes the incantation within the **Palm Technique** (掌诀), examine it closely and recite it as transmitted by the **Original Master** (本师) through oral instruction.

**Fourth**, when the heavens bring prolonged rain without ceasing, flooding crops, this is called **Heavenly Illness** (天病), caused by the **Dragon Deities’** (神龙) licentious chaos. One performs the rite to clear the skies.

The **Celestial Master Lao** (老君) said: At night when all is still, in a secluded place where no one can observe, tread the ground three times in **Yujian’s Pattern** (蹑地纪), then three times in **Flying Youth’s Pattern** (飞夭纲), forward, backward, and reversed. When done, lower the **Pattern** (纲), scattering it into **Yu’s Three-Step, Nine-Trace Pattern** (禹步三步九迹). Don the ritual robes, and with the left hand, perform the **Heavenly Seal** (天关), pointing toward the **Ninefold Clouds and Vapor of the Ten Thousand Miles** (万里云气九度). Afterward, recite the incantation:

*"Supreme Sage Li Lao, by the Golden Mouth’s decree,
Today at the [specific hour], I dispatch the clearing—
Thus dissolving the **Heavenly Illness** (天病).
The heavens and earth become clear and bright,
The sun and moon shine forth in their courses."*

When done, lower the **Warrant** (将), and order the scribes to write it. The **Day-Symbol Official** (符官) holds the warrant, and it is delivered to the **City Deities and Community Altars** (城隍社庙), where the deities collectively summon the Dragon Officials (龙王), the Wind Deities (风伯), and the Rain Officials (雨师), commanding them to swiftly gather the clouds and halt the rain. By the [specific hour] today, the skies shall clear—just as swiftly as water and fire parting."

**Fifth**, when a sudden violent wind arises, snapping trees and toppling houses, yet it is not the work of the **Heavenly Dao-spirits** (天神) or **Dao-spirits** (神)—for though the Dao-spirits may create wind and rain, they do not cause harm—

---

**Sixth**, when passing [a place], one may perform the ritual to summon and restrain it, and it shall cease.

The **Laozi** said: "Inform **Heavenly Dao-spirit General** (禁天大将军) **Zhao Boqin** (赵伯禽): Zhao Boqin is a man of Chu, capable of restraining the **Dragon-Lynx** (龙麟), **Sheep-Panther** (羊豹), **Tiger** (虎), and other such beasts from the heavens.

The **Emperor Taiwei** (太微帝) composed the *Chapter of the Stepping Void* (步虚章), stating:
*"Three hundred celestial beasts, the **Lion** (师子) numbering ten thousand *li* (寻).
All manner of beasts and birds—**Phoenix** (凤凰), **Peng** (鹏), **Golden-Winged** (金翅)—
each one restrained and captured, then cast down to the earthly realm for judgment.
They are released to ascend once more.
Together with the winds, clouds, rains, snows, frosts, and dews,
they obey the **Daoist** (道) will and respond to invocation,
and their cessation is immediate and potent.*

For the **spirited beasts and birds** (灵禽兽) that dwell above, they uphold the **Heavenly Dao-qi** (天正气), the **Dao’s** (道) own manifestation. These beasts also assist the **Dao-qi** (正气) and perpetually guard and protect those who embody the **Dao** (有道之人). They must not be recklessly restrained or forbidden.

If restrained, they lose their vigor and strength—
their ability to soar through the clouds and traverse the skies diminishes daily.
When beasts and birds are forbidden from their natural heroic prowess and courage,
they cannot maintain their strength, their soaring through the clouds weakens daily,
and they perish in exhaustion.

**Mischievous beasts and birds** (妖兽妖禽), however, must be restrained.
If not restrained, they descend to the lower realms and wreak havoc (作妖变),
plaguing humanity (祟害人物), causing unrest among all.
Thus, it is appropriate to restrain them.
But if they are not acting maliciously (不为妖祟),
they must not be arbitrarily forbidden—
forbidding them is to defy **Heaven** (反天).
Beware of this.

The **Later Sage Emperor** (后圣君) declared:
*'Among the **Dragons** (龙), there are **Mischievous Dragons** (妖龙);
among the **Tigers** (虎), there are **Mischievous Tigers** (妖虎);
all celestial beasts (天兽) may manifest as **monstrous** (妖怪).
They must be restrained as needed, lest they harm humanity.
The method of restraint: first, tread the **Earthly Memorial** (地纪) three times,
then fly the **Celestial Halter** (飞天纲) three times,
and recite the incantations.
The **Earthly Memorial** has eighteen incantations,
the **Celestial Halter** has twelve.
When the incantations are complete,
perform the **Yubu Steps** (禹步), don the ritual garments (配衣),
turn the **Heavenly Barrier** (天关) nine times,
and point downward nine times (指之九下).
Then issue the **summons** (牒) to follow the beasts,
commanding those of similar kind to capture them,
and bring them to the **Daoist assembly** (道场) for judgment.
When the incantations are complete,
dissolve into the **Yubu Steps** (禹步), don the ritual garments (配衣),
turn the **Celestial Halter** (天关) nine times,
and point downward nine times (指之九度).
Dispatch agents (使者) of corresponding rank,
seize the summons (把牒),
and pursue their capture.
Once they arrive, interrogate and sentence them,
then release them—
do not kill them recklessly.
To halt the **violent wind** (狂风):
The **Laozi** said: First tread the **Earthly Memorial** (地纪) three times,
then fly the **Celestial Halter** (天纲) three times,
and recite the incantations.
The incantations must not be spoken aloud (不得高),
lest human ears hear them—
for if heard, the **Heavenly Dragons** (天龙) and **Dao-spirits** (神) will not submit.*

The **Laozi** commands the **Seven Stars of the Big Dipper** (北斗七星):
*"Within the **Heavenly Dao** (大道),
the **Dao** is upright and balanced.
The **Dao-spirits** (神) are just and without malice,
the **Dragons** (龙) are upright and without excess,
and **ghosts and mischievous beings** (鬼妖) dare not move.
The unjust dare not act.
Why then does this **violent wind** (狂风) arise,
disturbing the **Heavenly Court** (天庭),
snapping trees and toppling houses?
The **Laozi** captures you—
the **Warrant** (符) and **Summons** (牒) are now invoked.
You **malicious Dao-spirits** (凶神) and **mischievous Dragons** (妖龙),
shall no longer generate wind.
As swift as the **Dao’s decree** (律令).*
When the incantations are complete,
dissolve into the **Yubu Steps** (禹步):
first three steps with nine traces (前三步九迹),
then transform into twelve traces (次即变为十二迹),
then transform into fifteen traces (次即变十五迹).
Then don the ritual garments (配衣),
turn the **Celestial Halter** (天关) nine times,
and point downward (转指之).
In secret, issue the **summons** (牒) to dispatch the **Day-Symbol Soldiers** (日神) and **Form-Symbol Soldiers** (式神) with their **Divine Cavalry** (兵马),
led by the **City Deities and Community Altars** (社稷神) and their forces,
to capture the **Wind-Generating Dao-spirits** (行风神), the **Dragons** (龙), and **ghosts** (鬼).
Sentence them according to their crimes (科央).
At the moment of invocation, the wind shall cease utterly,
swift as water and fire parting.
Twist the **mnemonic formula** (捻诀)—
the formula lies on the second joint of the left hand’s second finger,
the third joint of the second finger,
and the second joint of the third finger.
Twisting it shall halt the wind.

**Golden Lock, Flowing Pearl Scroll** (金锁流珠引) **Volume Twenty-Three**
**Golden Lock, Flowing Pearl Scroll** (金锁流珠引) **Volume Twenty-Four**

The **Grand Sovereign of the Dao’s True Perfection**, **Zaiwang Fangping**, **Zhang Daoling**, **Zhao Sheng**, **Wang Chang**, **Siziming Li Zhongfu**, **Mao Ying**, **Xu Yufu**, and others—these are the successive compilers and annotators of the **Chinese Daoists**. **Master Li Chunfeng** annotated the **Method of Summoning Dragons and Restraining Serpents**.

This is what **Lord Fan** and **Lord Liu** held in highest regard: in the human realm, there are venomous tigers and leopards; in the celestial realm, there are venomous dragons. This method is used to restrain them.

**Laozi said:** *"To summon dragons, one must do so at night in a pure chamber, free of women. Only then will it succeed. If a woman is nearby, it will not respond to the call."*

Within the chamber, do not enter a woman’s quarters, nor should a woman enter a man’s. After three days, one may tread the **Earthly Restraint** (*jì*) and the **Celestial Leash** (*gāng*), each three times.

Disseminate the **Yubu Steps** in nine strides, then **twist the eyes**—the **Dragon-Tiger Eyes**. With the left hand, grasp the talisman and summon nine times downward; it will arrive instantly.

Some say: *"Further, align the garments, turn the Heavenly Pass nine times, and it will surely come."*

Dragons and tigers are thus fully summoned, each with their respective talismans as prescribed.

In the past, during the **Later Han’s destruction of Wei**, **Fan and Liu** excelled in this summoning method.

According to *The Authentic Biography of Lady Fan*, Lady Fan was the twelfth-generation granddaughter of **Fan Kuai**, a high-ranking officer of **Emperor Gaozu of Han**. Her maternal grandfather was **Wang Zheng**, the seventeenth-generation descendant of **Wang Qiao**. Across generations, they inherited the **qi-sealing techniques**.

From childhood, Lady Fan lost her mother and was raised by her maternal grandfather, Zheng. As a child, she loved reading, and her grandfather taught her. At thirteen, she abandoned formal studies and devoted herself to reading the *Liujia* (Six Canons), the *Rites*, and the *Yijing*. Suddenly, in the secret archives of her maternal ancestor’s thirteenth-generation home, she discovered **Laozi’s *Liujia Talismans*** (seven volumes), the ***Seven Stars Step and Leash Rites*** (ten volumes), and this ***Summoning Scripture*** (over twenty volumes). She would steal away daily to read them in the woods near her home—sometimes a hundred paces, sometimes fifty—repeatedly.

After three years, while in the woods, she suddenly saw a young woman.

The woman asked: *"Do you love the Dao?"*
She replied: *"Though my years are young, I love the Dao greatly. I have studied this book, which teaches the art of eternal life and immortality. Later, I shall attain the Way of the Immortal. This world rarely hears such teachings. Common folk know nothing of this Dao-scripture, and the world would otherwise have none. Thus, in my youth, I cherished its words, reading them three or five times before committing them to memory."*

The female immortal said: *"I am the Immortal Alwang Xiao. I teach you to read this book. From now on, whenever you have leisure, come here. I will guide you further and teach you the methods of its practice."*

Thus, from that day forward, whenever she had free time, she would secretly go alone at noon. After two years, her maternal grandmother noticed her absence and secretly followed her to the forest, where she saw her reading with a woman. Delighted, she said nothing to others, but listened in silence for three years, until her Daoic studies were complete.

When her mastery was achieved, she could command ghosts and spirits like servants, bending them to her will as easily as turning her hand. She could communicate with spirits, summon and bind tigers and leopards—nothing was beyond her power.

During the reign of Emperor Wen of Wei, there was a great drought lasting over seventy days, with the sun blazing red and no clouds in sight. The emperor sought rain through every means but found no answer. The county officials recommended Lady Fan’s granddaughter, who had mastered Daoic arts, could summon tigers and leopards, and command ghosts and spirits to petition for rain.

The emperor ordered his concubine, Lady Zhao Dan, to write a request on silk, commanding her to seek rain. At the time, Lady Fan was indoors, ashamed and reluctant to comply. Lady Zhao reasoned with her: *"You are of the Wang clan by birth. Why conceal your lineage? Given the current drought, saving lives brings merit. If the people are at peace, how can you withhold such virtue?"*

Lady Fan then composed a letter to the Dragon King, which was sent into a deep pool. Rain fell immediately.

At fifteen, she married into the Liu family and traveled with her husband as an official across the empire. Later, her husband, Liu Gang, learned of her abilities and, with proper rites, requested her teachings. He received ten volumes of the scripture and was given diagrams of the Three Elements and Six Canons, along with the Seven Stars.

Over fifty years later, the couple both ascended as immortals. In the Eastern Mountains of Kuaiji, his wife sat upon a cloud-driven dragon chariot and departed. Her husband ascended a *zhaojia* tree and followed her. The Daoist records then conferred upon her the title of *Xian Guan*, a mid-ranking true immortal.

**The Supreme Lord Laozi’s Golden-Mouthed Edict: *The Female Qing-Shao Scripture for Protecting Households and Families (Zheng Ritual)***
*"Heaven is my resolute heart. My disciples and those who follow my teachings must act with sincerity and justice, rescuing beings from sickness and calamity."*

**Calamities** are of ten kinds:
1. Heavenly epidemic plagues—those who practice this teaching with sincerity shall not be blamed by Heaven.
2. Seasonal prohibitions—no harm shall come from them.
3. Official misdeeds—none shall be unjust.
4. Fire, 5. Water, 6. War.
7. Ghostly possession and malevolent spirits, 8. Poverty and hardship, 9. Deafness and blindness, 10. Internal ghosts.

For my summoned disciples, each year on the first day of the first month, before dawn when people are still asleep, they must issue talismans to protect their households, ensuring safety and freedom from disease and plague.

The **Supreme Lord Laozi’s Golden-Mouthed Edict** states:
*"The six Canons of the sixty days must be inscribed, listing the names of malevolent ghosts, along with the Female Qing Ritual, all contained within the Ghostly Statutes. Three copies must be placed at the head of the talisman: one at the community shrine, one at the ancestral hall, and one above the household door. After one year, the household shall forever be free from calamity, plague, and illness, and disputes shall naturally dissolve.*

*"Additionally, one must recite the *Diezhi Ji* and the *Feitian Gang* three times each, stepping in the Nine-Step Yujubu formation. The incantation is as follows:*

*'Sue poison, sue poison,
Sue disease, sue evil,
Sue ghosts, sue serpents,
Sue speech, sue tongue,
Sue rats, sue mice,
Sue waste, sue water,
Sue metal, sue fire,
Sue earth, sue wood,
Sue deceit, O Lord of Men!*

*One hundred twenty sues—sue swiftly, sue and disperse!*
*Swiftly, as the decree commands!*

*When reciting this incantation loudly, hold the written talisman in the left hand and pinch the *Dujian* talisman in the right, uttering each ‘sue’ while making a downward gesture with the hand—this brings great fortune."*

The Highest True Immortals perform this ritual annually without fail.

Laozi said: *"The path of Dao has gates, and the pursuit of Truth has roads. To obtain the gate is to attain *tong*—communion with spirits. When one studies the Dao and attains the gate, they possess *wei*—power to command ghosts, spirits, and the heavens, making them respond. This is called *shentong*—spiritual penetration. To obtain the road is to become an immortal. Immortals are the rank of True Persons. Those who practice the True Person’s Way and master this thirty-plus volume scripture, penetrating the Golden Talismans, later become known as the *Golden Lock Flowing Pearl Scripture*, harmonizing the Three Elements, emerging from the Upper Clarity, encompassing the Orthodox Unity—this is the path and the road to communion, enabling one to ride dragons and traverse the void, named the *Path of Daoic Cultivation to Communion*. Later, one may ride dragons and walk upon the clouds, wandering freely in the Purple Palace, near the rank of the Immortal Officials.*

*If practiced for nine years, a household shall have no sickness. If practiced for twenty years, the entire family shall attain Daoic power. This method is akin to the *Bazhe* (House-Transference) technique.*

**Note:** This ritual must be performed in the last days of the twelfth month (the 26th or 27th), inscribing the talismans and edicts of the Ghostly Statutes, with the master’s seal. At the stroke of three in the morning on the first day of the first month, the incantation must be recited. Modern practitioners no longer recite the words on the talisman—only the incantation is heard.

**A Comprehensive Ritual for Protecting Officials’ Households and Families from Calamity**
This is also included in the *New Chapter Rites*.

Laozi said to Master Xu: *"Xu Le, you are a master who protects and delivers from calamity. Now you are Zhang Ti, known as the Three Heavenly Orthodoxy Master. Now you are also Xiao Zhang, succeeding Da Zhang as the Celestial Master. You teach disciples to become national masters, to protect the inner palaces of the state and to pacify the distant prefectures and counties of the people.

First, present the Six Divine Writings of Heaven. Later, the Sage changed the titles and texts, making them into the Chapter Writings. The Most High approved them, granting talismans and edicts to the Five Sacred Mountains and Four Great Waters, to the cities and ancestral shrines. There are thirty-six volumes of grand proclamations and talismans. Twenty-four volumes are for pacifying the inner palaces, five volumes for the Five Sacred Mountains—the Sage later named them the Five Mountains, corresponding to the five phases: Wood, Fire, Earth, Water, and Metal. The remaining seven volumes: six are to be placed in sacred mountain caves, and one in the Water Palace. All these are rituals to be recited in a low, quiet voice, without musical resonance.

These are all Yang methods, human ordinances. The term *academy* (社) was once called *assembly* (斋), now changed to *gathering* (齐会). *Gathering* means to discuss and study scriptures. This is for beginners who have not yet entered the Dao. Do not let your disciples practice such methods—these are not the true, superior Chapter Rituals. The Chapter Writings originate from separate scriptures, containing five texts. The Sage-Emperor bestowed twelve talismans to pacify the nation, protect against calamity, and deliver from misfortune. Each has its own texts and rituals, detailed in the lower sections—examine and use them accordingly.

Laozi said: For the ruler of a kingdom—today’s prefects and magistrates—officials, and governors: do not use proclamations. Issue three edicts and thirty-six talismans. Twelve talismans pacify the Twelve Celestial Deities, twelve talismans guard the gates, and twelve talismans are placed within the household, to be worn by the head of the family and the eldest son. Commoners may practice this freely, but do not inscribe the thirty-six talismans. Three Chapter Writings are for officials, while commoners may use two or one.

When performing the talisman rituals, first step on the *Earth Measure*, then ascend the *Heavenly Rope*, each three times. Scatter the Nine Steps as the *Yugong Steps*, adjust the robes, and with nine fingers, dispel calamity and malevolent *qi* from houses and cities. Then, according to the talismans, place the edicts and talismans in their proper positions. For one or two years, there shall be no disasters.

To remove misfortune, pacify calamity, and protect households—use the same methods as before. Laozi’s statutes decree: Commoners use twenty-four talismans, two Chapter Writings, and practice according to the master’s intent. The secret is to pinch the first joint of the fourth finger on the left hand urgently.

When summoning a master or disciple-master, and summoning scribes and officials: If traveling with family or oneself to another prefecture, first issue an edict to the ancestral temples and city gods. These gods existed in the Jin Dynasty. The ritual of escorting, welcoming, and bidding farewell for protection is as follows:

Laozi commands the spirits of the shrines: When summoning, the master’s name must be written. For travelers with family, issue an edict five days in advance to the Nine Regions’ community leaders—Wu Zixu is one. If not summoning a proper master, issue an edict with the name written above and the scribe’s name below. If summoning a master from the Nine Regions, use a proper edict without talismans—talismans are on the edict’s head, not the seal. Laozi’s command states: Before the talisman is connected to the edict, the recording official—whether high or low—must be recorded. Today, people call Daoists *Celestial Officials*. For low-ranking officials, the edict states: ‘Regarding the aforementioned matter.’ Follow the official’s written edict, changing only the word *law* (法).

For secret edicts, follow the ritual: ‘Must issue an edict to the shrine, as follows.’ In official edicts, it states: ‘Must check the matter, as follows.’ Daoist edicts state: ‘Must issue an edict to the shrine gods and such-and-such deities, for escorting, welcoming, and bidding farewell, to protect within the boundaries. Safely convey the traveler by land or water, without any untoward incidents.’

The secret method is the same as before: pinch the first joint of the left hand.

**The Talisman of Punishment and the Destruction of Shrines**
*Punishment* refers to interrogating the talisman scribes and officials for delays or violations. If they do not comply urgently, hesitate, or fail to respond, it is called *Punishment Talisman*. *Destruction of Shrines* also interrogates the shrine and deity officials for failing to respond to talismans and edicts according to ritual. Thus, they must be punished with rods or demoted—there are other replacements—this is called *Destruction of Shrines*.

Lu Tianxuan transmitted the Golden-Mouthed Laozi’s ordinances: If one talisman is not honored, the blame falls on the direct scribe. *Rescript* refers to today’s Chapter Writings."

If the talisman is not honored, demote the direct scribe.

One may tread the earth three times while reciting the *Yǔbù* (步, "steps") threefold, and chant eighteen *sutra* (咒) of the *Golden-Mouthed Laozi’s* (太上老君金口) ordinances. Upon completion, disperse into the *Yǔbù* (禹步), nine strides and three steps, don the ritual robe (配衣), and shift the *Tiānguān* (天关, "Celestial Pass"). Point to a specific day and place.

The *earth* (地) refers to the *Yǔbù* (偃) as it aligns with today’s *jiǎzǐ* (甲子, "first heavenly stem and earthly branch"). If it is the *zǐ* (子) day, then the *jiǎzǐ* (甲子) is the *wángwénqīng* (王文卿) of that month and day. On this day, which talisman is being dishonored? The talisman scribes are instructed to carry out a certain matter, yet the matter is not executed. Thus, they shall be subjected to severe punishment, demotion, or replacement—cycling through these measures until compliance is achieved.

When questioning their offenses, follow the *Golden Ordinances* (金科) and *Jade Laws* (玉律) strictly. Upon completion, report as follows: *"Thus it is decreed."* As with the talisman scribes in the previous register, their swift punishment surpasses that of water or fire.

The *Destruction of Shrines* (破庙) may also be employed: tread the earth three times while reciting the *Yǔbù* (禹步), nine strides and three steps, don the ritual robe (配衣), shift the *Tiānguān* (天关), and point to a specific shrine or local deity—whether in a province, prefecture, or community—refusing to transmit talismans and edicts. The *Celestial Mandate* (天命) shall compel one to break their *yāngjǐ* (央脊, "central support"), demote, or replace them. If no replacement is made, it is simply *Destruction*. Upon completion, report.

The later *Saintly Master* (后圣君) told *Zhang Tiānshī* (张天师):

*"The Punishment of Talismans and the Destruction of Shrines*
are the ancient methods of the *Zhìzhēnrén* (志真人, "True Persons of Will"). They request the *Tiānshén Dàjiāngjūn* (天神大将军, "Celestial Deity Great Generals") and the *Dàguān* (大官, "Great Officials") to descend and oversee the interrogations, punishments, demotions, and destructions.

I now rely solely on the *originally appointed Three Generals* (元差三将军), whose responses align with my own. The *Celestial General* (某元将军) above corresponds to my body’s response below.

Simply invoke the *Upper, Middle, and Lower Originals* (上中下元), and observe their actions. Do not employ additional talismans or petition the *Celestial Officials* (天官) to descend for the *Punishment of Talismans* and *Destruction of Shrines*. These two methods have their own secret techniques (诀).

The secret technique lies on the third joint of the left hand’s third finger, on the right side. Twist it.

If this private method is practiced three or five times, upon completion, simply twist the secret technique—then the talisman scribes will naturally reveal those who have delayed or erred. Request their dismissal, and the technique shall always grant pardon. Thereafter, the talisman scribes will grow even more reverent.

At the mere thought of employing it, the action is initiated. Upon rising and reciting, the result is immediate.

Do not act rashly—this is the method of the *Zhìzhēnrén* (志真人, "True Persons of Will"). Be cautious!"*

「The Three Assemblies’ *Ritual of the Daoist Assembly* (三会日醮) and *Sacrificial Offerings for the Blind* (祭盲功) to Bestow Merit and Promote Officials and Soldiers (迁赏吏兵法)

For the *Ritual of the Assembly* (社庙), do not bestow merit with wine. Instead, have them sit outside the altar (坛).

The *Venerable Master Lao* (老君) said: Those who receive the *Law* (法) must follow the prescribed rituals (科仪) for the *Assembly Offerings* (醮祭), then auspiciousness (吉) shall follow; otherwise, misfortune (凶) will ensue. Those with *Lofty Aspirations* (上志之人) understand this *Way* (道).

The ritual states: On the *Upper Assembly Day* (上会) of the *Upper Month* (上元月), the *Assembly Offering* (醮) is made to *Heavenly Officials, Lord of the Upper Month* (天官君上元唐将军), and *Tang General of the Upper Assembly* (上元上部唐将军), whose surname is *Tang* and given name is *Short* (名短).

On the *Middle Assembly Day* (中会) of the *Middle Month* (中元月), the *Middle Assembly General* (中元中部葛将军) and others, including *Li General of the Middle Assembly* (上元中部李将军), serve as the *Assembly Offering* (醮) leaders. *Li General* commands the *Earthly Officials* (地官), while *Ge General* (葛将军) oversees the *Three Spirits of the Human Form* (人身三魂) and *Seven Souls* (七魄), the *Three Generals within the Body* (身中三将军), the *One Hundred Fifty Generals* (百五十将军), and the *Spiritual and Divine Officers and Soldiers* (仙灵将吏). Those who receive *Talismans and Ordinations* (符箓) as the *Divine Seat* (仙座) for the *Middle Month* (中元) are led by *Li* and *Ge Generals*, who command the *Heavenly Officials* (天官) and *Water Officials* (水官) and others. On this day, the *Three Months’ Generals and Soldiers* (三元将军吏兵), the *Functional Officials* (功曹司吏), the *Six Celestial Stems’ Generals and Soldiers* (六甲君官将军兵吏), the *Jade Boys and Jade Girls* (玉童玉女), and the *Direct Palace and Attendant Officials and Talisman Scribes* (直宫从官符吏) all gather to sit and receive the *Assembly Offering* (醮).

This day is the seventh day of the first month (正月七日). The *Upper Assembly* (上会) summons the *Nine Celestial Officials* (九天之官), the *Middle Assembly* (中会) invites the *Nine Earthly Officials* (九地之官), and the *Lower Assembly* (下会) calls upon the *Generals and Soldiers of the Human Form’s Talismans and Ordinations* (人身中法箓将军吏兵) and the *Water Officials’ Generals and Soldiers* (水官将军吏兵).

The *Later Sage-Emperor* (后圣君) instructed the *Heavenly Master* (天师): On the *Three Assemblies’ Days* (三会之日), the *Generals and Soldiers of the Three Officials* (天地水三官中大神君将军吏兵) all gather on this day for the *Assembly Offering* (社会), seeking to partake in the *Assembly Sacrifice* (求饮醮). This day’s *Assembly Offering* (醮) can expiate sins, bring blessings, and nurture fortune for all beings (福佑人物). It can also cultivate and nourish slaves, servants, cattle, and horses (育养奴婢牛马之类). Disasters and calamities will be averted (祸灭灾消), and joy and celebration will fill the household (身家喜庆). Why? Because on these three days, the *Three Officials* (三官) and the *Three Divine Generals* (三神) of Heaven, Earth, and Water all convene together (俱会於此日).

The *Most High Emperor* (上帝) graciously relents, and on these days, one need not attend the morning court assemblies (不朝集). Thus, blessings are obtained (所以获福).

Moreover, the *Assembly Offering* (醮) must be performed on the night of the *proper day* (正日). After the *people’s rest* (人定), during the *first watch* (一更时), or the *second watch* (二更时), the greatest blessings and protections (大福佑) can be secured. This is when all the gods gather (此时众神俱会之时). If the ritual extends beyond the *third watch* (三更) until the *fifth watch* (五更), it is absolutely unsuited for the *Assembly Offering* (切不堪醮). Why? Because the *Divine and Heavenly Officials* (神官仙官) and *Generals and Soldiers* (将军吏兵), all belonging to the *yin* (阴), appear as if seen by humans during the night. They attend the early morning court assemblies (日日早朝会家) and ordinary guests (闲客) may come. Important guests (要客) are summoned for official matters (皆有公事), and they only arrive after the court session concludes (直至衙退). The *Divine Officials* (神官), *Heavenly Officials* (仙官), and *Generals and Soldiers* (将军吏兵) from the *third watch* (三更) onward until the *fifth watch* (五更) are all eager to attend the morning court sessions (上朝天曹). Their minds are preoccupied with the affairs before them (心攻前排整), and they are busy with their attendants and carriages (车御忙). If their thoughts are scattered or distracted (心乱思), they will not come to receive the rites (不来受礼), or if they do come, they will stay only briefly (来亦不久), appearing and disappearing in haste (忽忽不多周匝). Thus, no blessings are gained, and misfortune is instead invited (所以不获福，却招恶).

For those who aspire to the *Way* (志人学道), they must first recognize this as a profound truth (先须知此为妙) and be cautious not to reveal it rashly to unworthy individuals (慎勿妄示非人). If unworthy individuals (非人) speak of erroneous doctrines (妄说异端), they will incur the *Heavenly Judgment* (天考).

The ritual further states: On the *Middle Assembly Day* (中会) of the *Middle Month* (中元月), the *Middle Assembly Offering* (醮) is led by *Earthly Officials, Lord of the Middle Month* (地官君上元中部李将军) and *Ge General of the Middle Assembly* (中元中部葛将军), among others.

The *Later Sage-Emperor* (后圣君) instructed the *Heavenly Master* (天师): Between Heaven and Earth (天地之间), following the *Two Principles* (二仪), there are the *Three Months* (三元), with the *Middle Month* (中元) being the joint master of Earth and humanity (地人两主). *Li General* commands the *Earthly Officials* (地官), while *Ge General* oversees the *Three Spirits of the Human Form* (人身三魂), *Seven Souls* (七魄), the *Three Generals within the Body* (身中三将军), the *One Hundred Fifty Generals* (百五十将军), and the *Divine and Spiritual Officers and Soldiers* (仙灵将吏). Those who receive *Talismans and Ordinations* (符箓) for the *Middle Month* (中元) are seated as the *Divine Seat* (仙座) to govern the *qi of the Middle Month* (中元之气), all under the command of *Li* and *Ge Generals*. They lead the *Heavenly Officials* (天官) and *Water Officials* (水官) and others. The *Three Months* (三元) are fully represented, and the *Generals, Officers, and Soldiers* (官将史兵) assemble.

First, the *Generals and Soldiers of the Upper and Lower Months* (上元及下元君官将军), the *Functional Officials and Soldiers* (兵士功曹司吏), the *Generals and Soldiers of the Six Celestial Stems* (六甲君官将军兵吏), the *Jade Boys and Jade Girls* (玉童玉女), and the *Direct Palace and Attendant Officials and Talisman Scribes* (直宫从官符吏) take their seats. Only then do the *Two Generals of the Lower Month* (下元徐周二将军二人), *Xu General of the Upper Water Assembly* (上元下部徐将军) and *Zhou General of the Middle Water Assembly* (中元下部周将军), along with their soldiers (及兵士), sit.

The *Master* (师主) must focus their mind and command the *Seat of the Assembly* (指撝座位). Only after this is settled (定后) should the ritual begin (方始启请). Each must be clearly provided with food and drink (分明一一饮食在). The *Master* (师主) must arrange and oversee the offerings (指摄安置), particularly the wine (上酒处分), and ensure the proper number of libations (般数取足).

Have someone prepare additional *secret gruel* (密浆之属) and other offerings, ensuring the *True Person of Will* (保真) sees *Venerable Master Li* (李尊师). They must add tea, offering three or four cups per seat (每座三四盏). The *True Person of Will* (保真) must then request *Ding* (丁) to conduct the *Assembly Offering* (醮) and transmit the *Law* (传法), bowing in reverence to their original teacher (伏依本师) and daring not to neglect or disobey (不敢违阙). They must ask that the teachings be passed down through generations (请后人相传继代), ensuring the *Way* of their original teacher is never lost (莫绝本师之教).

The ritual further states: On the *Lower Assembly Day* (下会) of the *Lower Month* (下元月), the *Water Officials, Lords of the Lower Assembly* (水官君上元下部徐将军) and *Zhou General of the Middle Water Assembly* (中元下部周将军), among others, lead the *Assembly Offering* (醮).

The *Later Sage-Emperor* (后圣君) instructed *Zhang the Heavenly Master* (张天师): On the *Upper Assembly Day* (上会), the seventh day of the first month (正月七日), the *Heavenly True Ones* (天真) descend to observe (下观). If one sets up the *Assembly Offering* (设醮) on this day, the *Heavenly Officials* (天官君), *Generals and Soldiers* (兵将), and *Earthly and Water Officials* (地水官) must wholeheartedly approach with sincerity and reverence (尽心须以虔恳), avoiding any impurity or vulgarity (勿秽浊), and receive boundless blessings (受福无量).

On the *Middle Assembly Day* (中会), the *Earthly True Ones* (地真) come to supervise the *Assembly Offering* (来监醮). The *Earthly Officials* (地官君), *Generals and Soldiers* (兵将), and *Heavenly and Water Officials* (天官水官君) must be invited. On the *Lower Assembly Day* (下会), the *Water True Ones* (水真) descend to supervise (来监醮). The *Water Officials* (水官君), *Generals and Soldiers* (兵将), and *Heavenly and Earthly Officials* (天地官君) must all be invited.

The *Middle Assembly Day* (中会) is the seventh day of the seventh month (七月七日). The *Lower Assembly Day* (下会) is the fifth day of the tenth month (十月五日). These three days are the *Three Assembly Days* (并是三会之日).

First, the *Generals and Soldiers of the Upper and Middle Months* (先领上元及中元君官将军), the *Functional Officials and Soldiers* (兵士功曹可吏等), take their seats. Only then do the *Two Generals of the Lower Month* (下元徐周二将军二人), *Xu* and *Zhou Generals* (徐周), along with their soldiers (及兵士), sit.

The *Master* (师主) must focus their mind and command the *Seat of the Assembly* (心分主领指撝座位). This is for those who receive the *Talismans and Ordinations of the Three Months* (受三元箓人) to conduct the *Assembly Offering* (自醮), as well as for those who invite disciples and fellow students (及入诸弟子等共醮). Thus, it is called the *Master* (师主).

The *Later Sage-Emperor* (后圣君) instructed the *Heavenly Master* (天师): You are the *Master of the Three Months’ Talismans and Ordinations* (三元法箓吏兵师主), so in ancient times, you were designated as the *Master* (师主) for disciples and fellow students (有弟子及同学人兵). When conducting the *Assembly Offering* (设醮), each must follow the prescribed words (各依辞). If the words are recited by oneself (如若自辞), then the prescribed words need not be used (即不用辞). After finishing the words (读词毕), one must recite the *Record of Merit and Deeds* (功状一遍).

The *Record* (状) speaks of merit and deeds (言功), the promotion and bestowal of officials and soldiers (迁赏吏兵). If there is indeed merit (如实有功), then it must be spoken of. If there is no merit (如无功), then the mention of merit must be omitted (即不用言功).」

The *Later Sage-Emperor’s* original *Record of Merit and Deeds* states:

*"If there is merit, it must be spoken of, and officials and soldiers shall be promoted. If there is no merit, though one’s family and self remain protected and at peace, this is not considered merit. However, if military achievements are spoken of, they are accepted. Historians and soldiers are not bound by the limits of promotion or merit—merely mentioning the reward of officials and soldiers suffices.*

*The Record speaks of merit and promotion: the legal documents of a certain prefecture, county, or village, or the appointment to a certain official post. The Daoist priest speaks of the Daoist of a certain mountain observatory. This pertains to the Heavenly Master’s ancient and modern *Taixuan* (太玄) *San Yuan* (三元) talismans and ordinations.*

*The *Yangping* (阳平) *Zhizuo* (治左平炁) oversees the *Menxia* (门下) *Dadu* (大都功), along with the *Zuoli* (左廉察) *Ban* (版署) *Jijiu* (祭酒). The *Shangqing Xuandu* (上清玄都), anciently known as *Taqing Wují* (太清无极), is the *Taishang Dadao Wují* (太上大道无极) *Fa Shi* (法师). The *San Dong* (大洞) *San Jing* (三景) disciple, the *Zhongyue Huangdi Zhenren* (中岳黄帝真人). This is the summary of the ancient *San Yuan* (三元) *Fa Jing* (法经) ordinations.*

*Your servant, [name], in the year [number], having passed [number] years, from the seventh day of the first month onward, or if it is the first month’s *Huì* (会) day, then from the fifth day of the tenth month onward, until the seventh day of the seventh month, has issued talismans and documents to save [number] people from illness, as well as those suffering from calamities, poverty, and destitution. The details include [number] people cured by talismans and medicinal prescriptions, [number] poor and sick individuals who lacked funds to buy medicine and were thus provided with money or medicine by your servant—each case recorded where recovery was achieved. Or [number] people suffering from official or private disputes and slander, who were rescued by your servant’s talismans and emerged unscathed, without facing severe punishment, with a total of [number] such cases recorded.

*Your servant dispatched the *Lingguan Jiangjun* (灵官将军), the *Shibing Gongcao* (史兵功曹), the *Yunü Yutong* (玉女玉童), who through their powers rescued and delivered [number] individuals, sparing them from illness, death, or punishment. These generals and soldiers have rendered merit, warranting promotion by one rank. All those saved have fully recovered.

*Additionally, your servant’s household has been protected, ensuring the well-being of your servant’s family and self, thus earning merit. The *Jiangjun* (将军), *Xianlingguan* (仙灵官), *Gongcao* (功曹), *Yutong* (玉童), and *Yunü* (玉女), along with the *Libing* (吏兵), have performed according to the regulations, and their merits are recorded: the *Jiangjun* (将军) with 200 merits, the *Xianlingguan* (仙灵官) with 150 merits, the *Gongcao* (功曹), *Yutong* (玉童), and *Yunü* (玉女) each with 100 merits, and the *Libing* (吏兵) with 100 merits as well. The *Zhifu* (直符) merits are 70. These rewards are bestowed upon those who have labored effectively to aid humanity and the state, elevating their true ranks.*

*Respectfully recorded.*

*This is the ancient ritual annotation. Today, we follow this form, though adjustments may be made. The wording and structure, however, should remain unchanged, adhering to the ancient tradition."*

「Promote one rank.
　　The number of individuals, all of whom have been approved for their positions, is recorded. Together, those who have safeguarded the well-being of my household and protected my family’s prosperity with merit, including the *Jiangjun* (将军), *Xianlingguan* (仙灵官), *Gongcao* (功曹), *Libing* (吏兵), and others, are granted promotions according to the established *ke* (科) and *fa* (法) rankings for their merits. The *Jiangjun* (将军) is awarded 200 merits, the *Xianlingguan* (仙灵官) 150 merits, the *Gongcao* (功曹), *Yutong* (玉童), and *Yunü* (玉女) each 100 merits, and the *Libing* (吏兵) 100 merits as well. The *Zhifu* (直符) merits are 70. These rewards are bestowed upon those who have labored effectively to aid humanity and the state, elevating their true ranks. Respectfully recorded.

　　This is the ancient ritual annotation. Today, we follow this form, though adjustments may be made. The wording and structure, however, should remain unchanged, adhering to the ancient tradition.

---

The Sun and Moon are clearly named and recorded, and their *jiào* (醮) rites and sacrifices have their own distinct *wén* (文) and *yí* (仪). After completing the *Jīnsuǒ liúzhū yǐnjuàn* (金锁流珠引卷) for the twenty-fourth time and the *Jīnsuǒ liúzhū yǐnjuàn* (金锁流珠引卷) for the twenty-fifth time, the *Zhōnghuá Zǒngzhēn Dàxiānzǎi* (中华总真大仙宰) Wang Fangping, Zhang Daoling, Zhao Sheng, Wang Chang, Li Zhongfu, Mao Ying, Xu Yufu, and others have compiled this text as a substitute.

　　The Daoist adept Li Chunfeng (李淳风) annotated the *Zhōnghuá Xiānrén* (中华仙人) text.

　　A memorial is submitted to request the *bǔkǎo* (补考) and *zhàofǎ* (召法) for the *Zhōnghuá Zhōnglíng Xiānrén* (中灵仙职) positions, along with promotions and rewards for the *Sānyuán* (三元), *Liùjiǎ* (六甲), *Qīxīng* (七星), *Jiǔtiān* (九天), *Èrshíbāxiù* (二十八宿), and the *Sānshíwǔshén* (三十五神官) and *Wǔyuè Jiǔzhōu Shèmiào* (五岳九州社庙) rites.

　　The *Lǎojūn* (老君) declared: "All the myriad deities within the cosmos are governed by their own leaders and officials. The grand Dao’s *yí* (仪) and *lǜ* (律) are strict and clear, with rewards and punishments duly administered. Both humans and deities who have earned merit are rewarded, and those who have committed faults are reprimanded—this is called *kǎozhào* (考召). Their duties and jurisdictions are defined by ordinances and regulations.

　　The regulations state: If there is a *kǎozhào* (考召) ritual conducted by a Daoist master, and a disciple is recommended who is capable of filling a vacant position among the celestial officials or bureaucrats, then the *Jiangjun* (将军) shall record 500 merits, the *Xianlingguan* (仙灵官) 400 merits, and the *Gongcao* (功曹), *Liùjiǎ Jiānglǐ* (六甲将吏), *Yutong* (玉童), *Yunü* (玉女), and *Zhifu* (直符) officials shall each record 300 merits. The *Zhǔlù* (诸箓) and *Libing* (吏兵) officials shall each record 200 merits. The *Zuǒshè Yòujì* (左社右稷) and the officials of the great and small temples and shrines shall each record 100 merits. Those already selected in the *Kǎozhào Yí* (考召仪) and recorded in the memorials are not listed here. The promotions and appointments follow their own prescribed rituals.

　　For regions and prefectures plagued by disasters—such as floods, fires, illnesses, and calamities—where people suffer unrest, the appropriate *fú* (符) and *zhāo* (章) are drafted to invoke *zhèn* (镇) and *yàn* (厌) rites.

　　The *Lǎojūn* (老君) instructed the Daoist master Luo (罗法师): "In the world, there are prefectures and regions afflicted by numerous disasters, where people and spirits are unsettled. You may now act to pacify them. Specifically, on the four *Mèng* (孟) days—*yín* (寅), *shēn* (申), *wèi* (巳), and *hài* (亥)—you shall tread the *Dìjì* (地纪) and invoke the *Fēitiān Gāng* (飞天纲), each three times.
