　　Afterward, you shall scatter the *Dàyǔ Bù* (大禹步) fifteen times, while simultaneously reciting the *Dūjiān Jué* (都监诀) with your left hand and holding the talisman with your right hand. Once the talisman is inscribed with the proper words, perform this rite and issue the talisman, commanding the practitioner to kneel and receive it before departing.

　　In accordance with the later edicts of the *Shèngjūn* (圣君) and the *Tiānshī* (天师), when performing the *Bù* (步) and *Gāng* (纲) rites, you must not be seen. After completing the rites, summon the practitioner to kneel and receive the talisman. The talisman is then sent forward.

　　Later, you shall compose the written record...」

「In the world, there are prefectures and counties plagued by frequent calamities, where people and things are restless. You may dispel such disturbances. Do so on the four *Mèng* days—*yín* (寅), *shēn* (申), *wèi* (巳), and *hài* (亥)—as specified.

Afterward, inscribe the talisman with the *Shànggǔ* (上古) twelve talismans and the *Zhāng Tiānshī* (张天师) twenty-four talismans, along with two additional talismans from the *Fēng* (风) tradition. The household head, wife, and local officials must also bear one talisman each. In total, distribute twenty-eight talismans of the *Dào* (道).

The talismans are listed in the *Dìngzhái Yí* (镇宅仪). The twelve talismans of the *Shànggǔ* (上古) are used to pacify the twelve deities overseeing the dwelling, while twelve talismans are affixed to the doors and windows, including the rear door and stove. Additionally, four talismans are posted above, and the household head and wife bear them as well. Once this is done, within three years, calamities and illnesses shall cease forever.

If you perform a second round of pacification, within six years, no calamities shall arise. Should they persist, perform another round as before, and then calamities shall never arise again for a hundred years.

The following ritual is prescribed: The *Gāozhēn Shàngshèng* (高真上圣) decrees that a well-pacified dwelling shall forever be free from calamities. This method was first recorded in the *Tàixuān Jīnsuǒ Liúzhū Zhèngyī Jīng* (太玄金锁流珠正一经). The *Zhào Tiǎng* (赵筒) edition cites its use for rescuing people and things alike.

For distant disturbances in prefectures, counties, or commanderies—where mountain demons (*Shānguǐ* 山魈), mountain ghosts (*Shānguǐ* 山鬼), or malevolent spirits cause chaos—employ this ritual to summon and banish them.

The *Lǎojūn* (老君, Venerable Lao) instructs the *Tàijí Zhēnrén* (太极真人, True Person of the Supreme Ultimate) Xu Fǎshī (徐法师): If you are the ruler of a prefecture, county, or commandery and perform this ritual to banish disturbances, first inscribe the talismans and affix them as directed.

Then, tread the *Dìjì* (地纪) three times, scatter the *Dàyǔ Bù* (大禹步) in three sets of nine steps, and simultaneously recite the *Dūjiān Jué* (都监诀), along with the *Shānguǐ Mù* (山鬼目) and the *Dāozhī Jué* (刀支诀) and others.

The *Shānguǐ Mù* (山鬼目) is located on the right side of the second joint of the left hand’s fifth finger; pinch it urgently. The *Dāozhī* (刀支) and others are on the third joint of all five fingers; pinch them urgently.

Afterward, issue the talismans, which are drawn from the *Sān Bù Záshuō* (三部杂符, Three Categories of Miscellaneous Talismans). The incantation for distribution is as follows:

*"Qián zūn yào líng* (乾尊耀灵), *kūn shùn nèi róng* (坤顺内荣)—so it is decreed."*

Again, it is issued with the words:

*"The moon’s constellation governs [certain deities] on the day of [certain deities]; thus, the *Xuānqǐ* (玄启) shall mark auspicious days and fine hours, the *Líhuì* (喜会) shall gather the host of celestial treasuries. Then, the *Xuāndiǎo* (玄澡) shall bathe in purity, and the *qīngzhāi* (清斋) shall be observed. Offer incense and treasures to the *Zhūtiān Dàsèng* (诸天大圣, Great Sages of All Heavens), *Huángdì Lǎojūn* (皇帝老君, Venerable Lao the Emperor), the *Běidǒu Qīxīng* (北斗七星, Seven Stars of the Northern Dipper), the *Èrshíbā Sù* (二十八宿, Twenty-Eight Lunar Mansions), and the eight *Shǐshén* (史神, Deity Historians) of *Qián* (乾), *Kàn* (坎), *Gèn* (艮), *Zhèn* (震), *Xùn* (巽), *Lí* (离), *Kūn* (坤), and *Duì* (兑).

With utmost reverence, I entrust my disciple [name] to receive these divine talismans. May the talismans of the *Dōngfāng Qīngdì* (东方青帝, Green Emperor of the East) be invoked to cure the *Jiǎo* (角, Horn) region, binding malevolent ghosts and delivering them to the prison for torture. May the talismans of the *Nánfāng Chìdì* (南方赤帝, Red Emperor of the South) be invoked to cure the *Zhēng* (征, Conqueror) region, binding malevolent ghosts and delivering them to the prison for confinement. May the talismans of the *Xīfāng Báidì* (西方白帝, White Emperor of the West) be invoked to cure the *Shāng* (商, Commerce) region, binding malevolent ghosts and boiling them in the caldron of *Tāng* (汤, Hot Water). May the talismans of the *Běifāng Hēidì* (北方黑帝, Black Emperor of the North) be invoked to cure the *Yǔ* (羽, Feather) region, binding malevolent ghosts and cooking them in the caldron. May the talismans of the *Zhōngyāng Huángdì* (中央黄帝, Yellow Emperor of the Center) be invoked to cure the *Gōng* (宫, Palace) region, binding malevolent ghosts and delivering them to the caldron.

All fivefold malevolent ghosts shall be subdued, and every demonic influence shall be eradicated.

From this day onward, may [name] of [prefecture/county/township/village] and all their households—great and small—thrive and flourish. May their granaries overflow with grain and their storerooms brim with silk and brocade. May all thousand calamities and ten thousand misfortunes be sent far away to other realms. May malevolent ghosts and wicked men become mere sources of slander, all vanquished and annihilated.

*"Chìduō!"* (叱咄, Rebuke!) *"Shúshú rú!"* (急急如, Swiftly as!)」

**The Supreme Female Qing of the Ghostly Capital’s Edicts Against Spirits**

Again, the incantation reads:

*"The Supreme Venerable Lord Lao,*
born before Heaven and Earth.
Illuminated by the Nine *Qi*,
he banished and subdued all spirits.
The *She* officials and their kindred,
though lacking true form,
assume names and deceive the world.
The dead who do not register in the Ghostly Ledger
shall be stripped of their false shapes.

When my talisman arrives,
they must reveal their true forms.
But you—mountain ghosts,
tortoises, cicadas, and the like—
shall not wrongfully harm or disturb,
nor bring illness or injury to Daoist adherents.
Let the three souls and seven spirits of [Name],
be urgently summoned back,
wearing their true forms as the Supreme Venerable’s.
*Swiftly, as the Edict commands!*"

**The True Person of the Supreme Polarity decrees:**
*"The Imperial Edict proclaims:*
Today, the duty-official [Name] presides.
The spirit, assuming the guise of today’s *jiāzǐ* (甲子),
declares itself as *Wang Wenzheng*,
with eighteen subordinates and two talisman scribes, *Tian Ji*.
The Edict must be carried out—
if not, report must be made.
*Swiftly, as the Edict commands!*"

Again, as the Supreme Venerable Lao’s Edict commands:
*"On this day, swiftly dispatch the talisman there,
coordinating with the Temple and City Deities,
uniting in strength to deploy troops,
apprehend, and interrogate—
as stated.
*As stated*—that is, if matters arise, they must be spoken,
and all must comply and give thanks.
If the matter is approved and completed,
report must be made to the Supervisory Bureau."*

**The True Person of the Supreme Polarity declares:**

*"The Venerable Lao instructs Master Xu and Master Luo:*
*'You who practice the *Kǎochāo* method—
constantly cultivate the mind to aid the state and stabilize the realm,
to rescue and heal the common folk.
All matters must be self-suppressed to silence slander.*

Within the Three Officials of Heaven, Earth, and Water,
there are many jealous ghosts and resentful spirits,
who constantly make one’s nature cruel and coarse,
unsettled and unaligned with the Dao—
thus causing one’s family and descendants to suffer from others’ tongues.
Each year on the Fifth of the Fifth Month,
write and carry a talisman—
and for the entire year, all slander shall cease.

Additionally, on the First of the First Month,
swallow a talisman.
For slander arises from the heart’s nature—
if the heart’s nature is extinguished, it does not arise;
externally, it shall not arise either.

If the heart’s nature is still and unmoved,
and one does not wrongfully slander others,
yet others persist in slandering you,
then on the First and Fifth of the Eighth Month,
within a secluded chamber,
recite the *Dìjì* (地纪) three times.
Do not use the *Fēitiān Gāng* (飞天纲),
but only the *Yǔbù* (禹步) on the ground.
When finished,
dissolve into three steps of nine traces,
then twelve steps again,
then fifteen turns—
and call out the name of the slanderer.
This person, who falsely slanders you with countless words,
must be silenced—
if they do not cease, they shall die.
*Swiftly, as the Edict commands.*

Recite the *Dìjì* incantation eighteen times:
*"From me, receiving the *qi* of Heaven and Earth,
I act as Heaven and Earth’s envoy—
until Metal attacks Wood,
Water extinguishes Fire,
and the Copper Mouth and Iron Tongue are silenced."
When the eighteen incantations are complete,
the slander shall never arise again.
If it persists, recite the incantation again—
and they shall meet ruin and die.*

Later, the Sage Emperor instructed the Heavenly Master:
*'This method is highly efficacious—
do not use it recklessly.
Only when truly justified may it be employed.
The Venerable Lao forbids misuse,
lest harm befall the innocent,
and you incur guilt, losing your immortality.*

If one is falsely slandered without cause,
first attempt to silence them.
If they refuse three times,
then this method may be applied.*

**For Officials and Commoners: The Method to Suppress Slander**
*The Venerable Lao declares:*
*'Those who practice the *Kǎochāo* method
must purify body and mind—
that is, body and mind must be pure.
They must not eat meat,
take a wife, or bear children,
but must keep the heart upright,
neither partial nor deceitful,
neither gluttonous nor lustful,
neither jealous nor resentful,
neither hateful nor fond,
neither encroaching nor stealing,
neither quarrelsome nor competitive,
neither licentious nor promiscuous.*

Later, the Sage Emperor instructed Master Zhang:
*'If one remains loyal and upright,
without favoritism or cliques,
and does not accept biased requests or demands,
then this method may be used.*

When body and mind are pure,
no licentiousness or theft arises.
The Heavenly Master said:
*"These two characters are difficult to explain—
I beg you to clarify for the ignorant masses.*
The Emperor replied:
*"One may have concubines,
but must not lust after others’ wives.
Children must receive scriptures and precepts—
do not falsely claim or steal them,
for such deeds are grave offenses.
Beware, for the Supreme Dao does not tolerate them.*

If a devoted scholar, with sincere intent,
practices the Dao and governs with purity,
yet is falsely slandered—
not merely defamed or accused of treachery,
but relentlessly beset by slander—
then three talismans may be written and carried,
and the slanderer shall cease.
These talismans are found in the *Sanbù Záshú* (三部杂符),
but their full text is not recorded here.
If they persist,
seal them with the *Liùrén Léigōng* (六壬雷公) formula and others.
The method is recorded in the *Shìjīng* (式经).
Within the *Shìjīng* are talismans and seals—
use them as prescribed, and the effect is swift,
like fire and water.

After sealing, within a pure chamber,
recite the *Dìjì* three times,
the *Fēitiān Gāng* three times,
then dissolve into three steps of nine traces,
adjust the clothing,
turn the *Tiānguān* (天关),
and point remotely.
The incantation is:
*"The Five Phases push one another—
Metal attacks Wood,
Water extinguishes Fire—
and so on."
Recite three times.
When finished,
pinch the talisman’s seal—
the seal is beneath the first fingernail of the left hand.
Pinch the slanderer’s mouth shut
and send them to water and fire.
This method is divine and secret—
guard it well.*

**For Officials and Commoners: The Method to Sever Internal and External Curses, Ghostly Bandits, and False Witchcraft That Kills Without Ceasing**
*The Venerable Lao declares:*
*'All people, noble or base,
suffer from curses—
internal and external deaths.
Ghosts enter homes,
demanding living souls to replace the dead,
thus creating curses.
Within families, brothers or fathers and sons may curse one another—
such cases are common.
The world calls this *mù* (墓).
Li Zūnshī Huìjǔ said:
*"This is the curse afflicting the family now—
it does not cease.
Those who seek to replace the dead
are tormented by worms devouring their souls,
as if bitten by insects—
terrified and in agony.
Thus, they seek a substitute.

If a Daoist possesses the method,
and can sever this curse,
their merit is great—
Heaven and Earth rejoice,
and the practitioner may attain the Dao.
Saving one family earns one hundred merits:
The living gain health and longevity,
while the restless spirits escape the suffering of worms devouring their souls,
and are reborn as humans,
free from the resentment of curses.

A Daoist may save and sever them,
ending life and death,
and earning gratitude from Heaven and Earth—
this is the Dao’s merit.*

*The Venerable Lao’s method to sever curses
includes five talismans,
along with decrees to the local deities, ancestral temples, city gods, and officials.
In ancient times, only ancestral temples were mentioned—
no city gods existed.
It began with King Ke of Wu,
whose tomb was in Wúzhōu (吴中).
During the Jin Dynasty,
Governor Liu Wénjǐng built a city there,
covering the tomb.
Each night, the city walls collapsed,
and the earth was carried away by yin-forces—
by dawn, no trace remained,
and this happened seven or eight times."*

The Governor acted swiftly that very night, ordering men to capture the spirits. In the night, he saw a single sovereign emerge from the earth, accompanied by tens of thousands of soldiers, who repelled the captors. The sovereign said to them: "I am King Ke of Wu. My tomb sinks two *zhang* (丈) into the earth—why do you persist in building a city over it? Each night, I cause the walls to collapse and the earth to be carried away by *yin-forces* (阴兵). By dawn, no trace remains, and this has occurred seven or eight times."

The Governor thus retained the tomb, moved the city walls to curve around it, and established a temple a hundred *bu* (步) away. Henceforth, there were city gods and spirit officials. Today, wherever there are graves in the *dìfǔ* (地府, Underworld), if they confer with the Underworld authorities, the Most High Celestial Emperor grants permission for the deceased to become the chief among the city gods and spirit officials of that locality. The talismans and decrees are issued with divine authority, and their efficacy in driving and subduing malevolent spirits is unparalleled, reaching even to the farthest corners.

When entering a certain state, county, or village, and a particular person’s household, to seize and capture the restless spirits, curses, and thieving ghosts—such is the practice. The decrees follow the prescribed rituals as outlined above.

The Most High Lao Dao/Way’s method to sever curses includes five talismans. Two of these are contained within this incantation, which demonstrates their efficacy. The remaining three are found in the *Sanbu* (三部) miscellaneous talismans—primarily within the *Zhèngyī* (正一, Orthodox Unity) *Sanbu*, not the *Língbǎo* (灵宝, Numinal Treasure) *Sanbu*. In the world, there exist the *Língbǎo* *Sanbu* miscellaneous talismans, the *Tàixuān* (太玄, Supreme Mysterious) *Sanbu* miscellaneous talismans, the *Liùjiǎ* (六甲) *Sanbu* miscellaneous talismans, the *Liùrén* (六壬) *Sanbu* miscellaneous talismans, and the *Liùdīng* (六丁) *Sanbu* miscellaneous talismans, among others. All these are compiled by the Most High Lao Dao/Way, totaling seventy-two volumes, and are also included in the *Lǎojūn Zhèngzhuàn* (老君正传, Lao Dao/Way’s True Transmission).

The two talismans of divine efficacy are detailed in this text. The remaining three are noted in the previous section. All talismans within these volumes are inscribed in red.

The following talisman treats those afflicted by curses and suffering from extreme exhaustion and emaciation. When swallowed, it alleviates their condition. One should ingest it daily.

The following talisman slays curses, restless spirits, and pests. Prepare it by writing on a clean, white tablet, mixing with water in a pure basin, and placing it before the afflicted person. For each individual, present the talisman and cast it into the water. After seven days, if the talisman sinks, the curses, restless spirits, and pests will all perish, and the person’s illness will be cured. This efficacy is genuine; do not recklessly transmit it to others.

The decrees and talismans are also hung on doors and gateways. The talismans are inscribed according to the rituals outlined above, and their efficacy is derived from the prescribed rites.

Later, the Sage Emperor instructed the Heavenly Master (天师): "If you wish to cure the plague for all people, you may tread the *dìjì* (地纪, Earthly Boundary) three times, scatter the *Yǔbù* (禹步, Steps of Yu) nine times, and don ritual attire, wearing the *dòu* (斗, Dipper) as your garment, so that your form resembles the Northern Dipper—this is the true Dipper Sovereign. Turn toward the *Tiān Guān* (天关, Heavenly Pass) and point in the direction of the afflicted person’s dwelling. Then recite the *Bāguà* (八卦, Eight Trigrams) incantation once.

The *Bāguà* incantation reads:
*Qián zūn yào líng* (乾尊耀灵, The Heavenly Trigram is revered, its brilliance is sacred),
*Kūn shùn nèi róng* (坤顺内荣, The Earthly Trigram is compliant, its inner grace flourishes),
and so on.

Then, seated, write the five talismans to sever curses and give them to the afflicted person to swallow or wear as an amulet, specifying the number of days by which their illness will be cured. When the days are up, the illness will indeed be cured—this method is highly efficacious.

**The Method to Sever Plagues for Officials and Commoners**
Lao Dao/Way said: "The plague’s *qi* (毒之气) harms all beings. When one person contracts the *qi*, it can kill ten others. When ten people are infected by its *qi*, they can spread and kill up to a hundred. Thus, there are many deaths. When one dies, ten others grieve for them. In the world, this is called the *wúyì bìng* (无义病, Plague of Injustice)—it does not discriminate between noble and ignoble, good and evil. Those who contract it rarely survive.

Since one person’s death leads to ten others grieving, and from ancient times to today, such cases are often seen, I often fear that those who practice the Dao may be afflicted, causing others to grieve. Therefore, I have issued this chapter to prevent disasters and malevolent spirits.

I possess nineteen talismans, and among those that can cure this plague, they are efficacious. If one has contracted the illness, swallowing this talisman will bring about a great cure in three days, and a minor cure on the very same day.

This talisman is the Most High Lao Dao/Way’s personal transmission to the Yellow Emperor, who practiced it and preserved it. It has been passed down through generations to this day. This is its original text, and it is highly efficacious.

The two talismans of divine efficacy are inscribed in this volume. The first talisman, when worn by the unill, and kept near the afflicted person during sitting or sleeping, prevents the illness from spreading. The first talisman, when swallowed by the afflicted person, causes sweat to break out and brings about a minor cure that very day, and a great cure within three days.

The following talisman is for the afflicted person to swallow. The following talisman is for the unill to wear, sharing sleeping and sitting spaces without risk of contagion.

**Lao Dao/Way’s Great Talisman**
Its length is one *chǐ* (尺) eight *cùn* (寸). At its base is a decree that reads:
*"Lǎojūn shénfú* (老君神符, Lao Dao/Way’s Divine Talisman),
controls the five *guǐwáng* (鬼王, Ghost Kings) of the *Wǔbù* (五部, Five Departments)—*Liú Yuándá* (刘元达), *Zhāng Yuànbó* (张元伯), *Zhào Gōngmíng* (赵公明), *Shǐ Wényè* (史文业), and *Zhōng Shìjì* (钟仕季)—
along with the *Wǔgǒu* (五蛊, Five Pestilential Spirits), the *Bǎidú* (百毒, Hundred Poisons), and the *Huángnú Bósāng* (黄奴伯桑, Yellow Slave Bossang),
as well as the vulgar *Liùdīng* (六丁) ghosts.
Those who obtain it will be decapitated at the waist,
without regard for past transgressions.
*Jíjí rúlìng* (急急如律令, Swiftly, as the decree commands).
This decree is also inscribed beneath the Great Talisman,
and hung on the main gate."

**Lao Dao/Way’s Method for Severing Pestilence**

This talisman lies within the *Three Departments* (三部) of miscellaneous talismans, so its full text is not recorded here. Among the *Three Departments* of miscellaneous talismans is a separate chapter for severing and prohibiting plagues (断禁瘟), and the talisman’s text must be carefully sought.

Later sage-rulers possess a grand chapter for severing plagues (断瘟大章), which, when appended above this chapter, will cause all cases of *kǒu wēn* (口瘟, oral plague) to vanish immediately. Before using this chapter, one must observe a period of abstinence from meat and strong flavors for three-five days (三五日), or three-seven days (三七日), or four-seven days (四七日), five-seven days (五七日), six-seven days (六七日), or seven-seven days (七七日) for a great expulsion. If one strictly observes abstinence for a hundred days beforehand, the efficacy will be even more potent.

This chapter is found in the upper register of *Jīnsuǒ Liúzhū* (《金锁流珠》), not fully included in this book. The chapter itself is in the first volume of *Jīnsuǒ Liúzhū*, comprising ten sheets of paper, already inscribed and not recorded here. To invoke this chapter, follow the established method.

Lao Dao/Way speaks: *"To sever pestilence, one must first obtain the name of the afflicted person, along with their residence—state, county, village, or neighborhood (郭言坊). The year, month, and day when they contracted the plague, and the severity of their illness: whether they were infected by a pestilential *guǐwáng* (鬼王, Ghost King) or *qi* (气), or whether they died or remain gravely ill. If they died, state ‘dead’ (死); if they did not, state ‘grave’ (重). After a certain span of months and days, another person is afflicted, and one fears a continuous chain of infections. I humbly beg the Great Dao/Way for compassion and request an order of prohibition for each case. I await the judgment of the Dao/Way and the officials (判). Now, another person is infected in succession. All details must be written as in the official report, with the Dao/Way’s officials issuing their judgment.*

*Once completed, inscribe the talisman in vermilion (朱书符) within a purified chamber (净室), reciting three times while tracing the ground (蹑地纪), and three times while invoking the *Fēitiān Gāng* (飞天纲, Heavenly Skybound Decree). Afterward, perform the *Yǔbù* (禹步, Steps of Yu) three times—three steps, nine traces (三步九迹)—left and right, then once more, totaling two sets of steps. Then recite the incantation:*

*'I rely upon the Three-Five (三五) and the Arcane Below (魁魁之下), where ten thousand ghosts and myriad spirits are all my servants to summon. All malicious and malevolent *jīngxié* (精邪, malevolent essences) and ghosts beneath the heavens submit to death beneath the Heavenly Skybound Decree, motionless and inert. The wicked hide in vain, officials dissolve them, slanderers are silenced, and the afflicted swiftly recover. Chì-chì-chì! Swiftly, as the decree commands (急急如律令).'*

*Once the incantation is finished, write the talisman. When the talisman is complete, pinch the pestilential ghost’s eye (捻瘟鬼目)—the eye is on the fourth finger of the left hand, at the third joint, where the scar of a blade is marked. Pinching it causes the ghost to die; this method is highly efficacious and auspicious (吉). Send it far to permanently sever the pestilence. If the ghost refuses to sever, invoke the *Dàchì Zhāng* (大赤章, Great Vermilion Chapter) to decapitate it, ensuring the ghost’s death and the person’s survival—this is also highly efficacious.*

*This plague must never be treated by monks’ incantations or magical rites (咒术加持); otherwise, the ghosts will not submit and may even retaliate with harm. In ancient times, the Wu King (吴王) Sun Quan (孙权) suffered this affliction in his inner palace. A monk named Fa Chao (法超) arrived from the Western lands, renowned for his incantations, and when he invoked them, he was slain by the ghosts. The fifth monk died, and among the hundreds afflicted in the palace, all perished as well. Therefore, all manner of talismans and decrees must be dispatched to distant states to capture and subdue the malevolent ghosts and spirits.*

Lao Dao/Way instructs the Yellow Emperor (黄帝): *"If you wish to summon ghosts (追鬼), inscribe their names on the talisman. The *Tàishàng* (太上, Supreme Sage) refers to the current decree (牒帖). In ancient times, this was called the *Tiānfú* (天符, Heavenly Talisman), invoked by both humans and ghosts. Now, humans recognize it as the Great Dao/Way’s talisman, while ghosts still call it the Heavenly Talisman as before.*

*To execute this talisman, each method and incantation must be followed precisely, as the techniques for summoning, interrogating, capturing, and expelling ghosts differ. Summoning is swiftest through water and fire. The Emperor inquires: ‘How does one know the ghost’s name?’ Lao Dao/Way replies: ‘Simply have the afflicted write their statement (作辞) saying: “My illness has persisted for so many days without improvement, and all medical treatments have failed. A malevolent ghost or spirit has afflicted me; I beg for the Great King’s pursuit and interrogation.” The Yellow Emperor then declares: ‘Order the Daoist to conceal and the officials to judge, and so forth.’*

*Across the Nine Regions (九州), the land spirits and local deities (灵祇) have evolved. In ancient times, there were only *Tiānshén Dìzhǐ* (天神地祇, Heavenly Gods and Earthly Spirits), with no shrines or temples. In the middle ages, there were *zuǒshè yòujì* (左社右稷, Left Communal Altars and Right Grain Offerings), but still no formal shrines or temples. From the Han, Wei, Jin, and Song dynasties onward, there were established *shèjì shén guān* (社稷神官, Communal and Grain Offering Deities). Later, during the Qi, Liang, Chen, and Sui dynasties, the *chénghuáng shén guān* (城隍神官, City Gods and Wall Deities) emerged. By the decree of later sage-rulers, the Daoist officials (法师) oversee the summoning and judgment, and these talismans are called *Miaozhí Fú* (庙直符, Temple Rectification Talismans). The City Gods and Wall Deities assist in summoning and interrogating, passing the talismans through their respective domains as officials pass decrees through counties and states, to sever deceit and capture malevolent spirits. This is the Dao/Way’s supreme method for nurturing humanity and binding ghosts, driving dragons and commanding spirits. It originates from the Celestial Palace (上天宫阙) and is transmitted through the ages to those with lofty aspirations (有道之志人).*

*Once summoned, the ghost’s name is revealed, and the Daoist issues the decree, ordering the illness to subside within a certain number of days. The ghosts are then prohibited from entering the *Dìyù* (地狱, Underworld Prison), which, in ancient times, was drawn on the earth as a prison (画地为狱). Three concentric lines formed the prison, confining guilty ghosts within. After ten or five days, they would submit to their punishment. Once the term is fulfilled, their sentence is carried out: the severely guilty are executed, and they do not escape, while those not deserving death remain confined. Thus, it is called the Underworld Prison (地狱). Later generations, misunderstanding the ritual timing, falsely claim there is an Underworld Prison beneath the earth where punishments are severe, misleading the world and inviting great retribution upon themselves. Now, Daoist practitioners affix talismans to communal altars and temples to prohibit ghosts, following the ancient method of drawing prisons on the earth. Once the illness subsides, the talisman is removed, and the ghosts are released, with the decree stating: ‘From this day onward, never again shall you cause harm; if you do, you will be executed.’*

Lao Dao/Way says: *"When inscribing talismans and decrees to be dispatched thousands of *lǐ* (里) away or within ten thousand *lǐ*, first complete the talisman and decree without sealing or stamping them. Then perform the ritual in a purified chamber (净室), tracing the ground three times (蹑地纪), and executing the *Yǔbù* (禹步) three times—three steps, nine traces—while donning ritual attire (配衣), turning the *Tiānguān* (天关, Heavenly Barrier), and pointing in the direction of the afflicted. Focus your mind and visualize the person thousands of *lǐ* away, directly addressing the official responsible for that day’s *liùjiǎ lúnrì* (六甲轮日, hexagram cycle of days).*

Now, take the talisman and decree, entrusting them to the Heavenly Gods, Earthly Spirits, Dragons, and Ghosts. In this age, it is unnecessary to invoke the Heavenly Gods and Earthly Spirits explicitly—simply dispatch them to the local shrines and temples, which will suffice. In recent times, the City Gods (城隍) have been established with full efficacy, and their methods are highly verified.

Issue the decree to the magistrate of a certain prefecture or commandery, ordering the capture of a certain ghost or malevolent spirit. If the illness improves swiftly and the matter is resolved, the decree must be executed promptly. Once the order is fulfilled and the report received, pinch the *dūjiān* (都监) talisman with your thumb—*dūjiān* refers to the first joint of the first finger on your left hand.

**Method for Dispatching a Decree to Distant Relatives to Ensure Their Safety and Receive News**

Lao Dao/Way says: *"When a practitioner of the Dao earnestly aspires to cultivate but has not yet attained mobility, yet has relatives in another state, and wishes to know their well-being or their moral conduct—good or ill—simply write a decree and entrust it to the Earthly Spirits (地祇). The Earthly Spirits of today are the City Gods (城隍) and the deities of local shrines and temples. Command the official of the day to deliver it, demanding a response within two days. For distances beyond a thousand *lǐ*, specify two days. For distances within ten thousand *lǐ*, specify five days, without delay or hesitation. Some may say five days for all cases.

After inscribing the talisman and decree, trace the ground three times (蹑地纪), execute the *Yǔbù* (禹步) in nine traces, don ritual attire (配衣), turn the *Tiānguān* (天关), and point toward the direction of the relative’s residence—this is the dwelling place of a certain individual, say, *Yǐ* (乙), who is my Daoist servant, *Xuán* (玄), a relative."*

「Or it may be an uncle or cousin—brothers, aunts, or other such relatives—whose names must be specified. Both good and evil deeds are fully reported; the talisman is sealed with the *niǎnxīng* (捻星) invocation. The invocation is held in the left hand’s fourth finger at its first joint.

Until nightfall, constantly observe the celestial region corresponding to the relative’s dwelling. If a star suddenly flies away, it signifies that the Heavenly Dao (天地) has dispatched a messenger to investigate there, who will then report back. The report must be true. If no star disperses into that region’s celestial division, the report will surely be false and cannot be trusted. You must reattempt the ritual—then the truth will be revealed.

If there are stars at night, observe them carefully. If stars disperse toward that direction, the report will certainly be true.

Later sages and rulers have decreed: The threefold tracing of the ground (*cèdìjì* 蹑地纪) stirs the *Tiānguān* (天关). When the *Tiānguān* dispatches a messenger to inspect and report, the account is true. If no star is sent to investigate, the report will be false—this is the deception of the talisman deities or officials. You must then reattempt the ritual, summoning the talisman deities and officials to question them again before sending the messenger. The saying goes: *"The talisman officials, if they do not follow the prescribed ritual, must be punished according to the severity of the crime."* The punishment begins with the celestial decree (*kējué* 科决) ten times; once completed, it is highly efficacious—do not speak of it lightly, and always keep it secret.

**Ritual for the Sovereign to Subdue Ominous Stars, Portents, and Malevolent *Yìqì* (异气) Before Disaster Strikes**

*Lǎojūn* (老君) says: When ominous stars appear, portents will surely follow. Stars are the "children of the sun" (日生), hence the upper character is *rì* (日, "sun") and the lower is *shēng* (生, "life/child"). Thus, the sages say: *"Stars are rebellious; they will cause ministers to betray their sovereigns, sons to defy their fathers, and disciples to abandon their teachers."* Such rebellious winds are often seen in this world. When the heavens display crimson *qì* (气), it is called an evil portent. These two phenomena presage the betrayal of ministers and their early demise.

The heavens, knowing of such evil portents, reveal them to mortals. Among humans, those skilled in Daoist arts (*dàoshù* 道术) can subdue them for the state—once they are ordered, these stars will not manifest. Thus, the ruler and ministers will have no worries.

If they are unaware or fail to act, the stars will appear again, aiding the state in attacking and subduing them early—this is the first great merit. When the celestial reward for this merit is complete, the practitioner ascends in broad daylight to the clouds, becoming a transcendent *xiānzhēn* (仙真).

Those who understand the Dao know this. They must avoid betrayal.

If there are Daoist practitioners (*zhìdào* 志道) within this realm, and they see the stars and *qì* descending upon their region, they must quickly leave to avoid it—this brings great fortune. Never dwell in that direction, lest these Daoists lose their Way.

Moreover, it is said that the *Lǐ* (李) family, inheriting the sovereign’s Daoist legacy, passed down this secret merit through generations. The heavens granted them this legacy.

If the ruler is virtuous, he will share this merit with them. *"Lǐshēn"* (僭申) refers to those who practice the Dao: they borrow the method of peaceful abode to aid the state, which is the later ritual.

If the ruler lacks virtue, the practitioner will change his lineage and hide his identity. He will flee to another realm, conceal his name, and this is called the *zhìrén* (志人) method for averting ominous stars.

*Lǎojūn* (老君) instructs: With abstinence from meat and purification of the heart (*sùshí zhāixīn*), the mind steadies, the Daoist resolve (*zhàizhèngxīnshén*) aligns the spirit. Thus, one must purify the heart. Reside in a separate chamber for three days, avoiding women for seven days; women must also avoid men for seven days.

Then, trace the ground (*cèdìjì* 蹑地纪) five times, and perform the *Tiāngāo* (天纲) once—this is the proper order. Execute the *Yǔbù* (禹步) three times: one cycle of three steps (九迹), two cycles of twelve steps (十二迹), and three cycles of fifteen steps (十五迹), before descending outside.

Recite the *Dìjì* (地纪) Great Incantation (*dàzhòu* 大咒) eighteen times, don ritual attire (*pèiyī*), turn the *Tiānguān* (天关), and point toward the target. Repeat this process daily for seven days, three times each day—at dawn, noon, and dusk—for a total of twenty-one cycles. The stars will then fall, the malevolence disperse, and the state will suffer no calamity.

Such practitioners bring great merit to the state, ensuring the people’s peace and boundless blessings. Ominous stars and malevolent *qì* will be extinguished. Even if some residual *qì* lingers briefly, it will collapse within a year and a half, vanishing on its own.

This method, when applied, also requires the invocation (*niǎnxīng*). Twist the talisman toward the direction observed, determining whether it aligns with *metal* (金), *wood* (木), *water* (水), *fire* (火), or *earth* (土), and invoke accordingly.

Later sages and rulers commanded the *Jiǔtiān Xuánnǚ* (九天玄女, "Mysterious Woman of the Nine Heavens") to descend and personally transmit the *Tenth Volume of the Outer Canon of the Golden Lock and Flowing Pearl* (*Jīnsuǒ Liúzhū Wàipiān* 第十卷, *金锁流珠外篇*), detailing the talismans and diagrams for the nine regions and ten Daoist circuits of myriad states. She taught this to *Lǐ Shìyè Jìng* (李仆射靖), who served as the Right Comrade of State (右仆射) and used divine communication to aid the state in military affairs, ensuring the people’s security with unwavering loyalty. He was thus honored as the *Shénjiàng* (神将, "Divine General"), commanding the *yīnbīng* (阴兵, "Yin-forces").

*Jìng* (靖) used his divine arts to assist the state and protect the people, and the sages’ grace bestowed upon him the title of Divine General. **Note:** Already detailed in *Liúzhū* (流珠); no need to repeat here.

*Lǎojūn* (老君) says: This method is called the *Luòxīng* (落星) Ritual—it knows only the method of ominous stars and removes them. There is no need to inquire about the names or lineages of those below.

This teaching reflects the *Tàishàng* (太上) Lord’s compassionate heart: seeing only the ominous stars in the heavens, he removes them for the state’s sake, without concern for the names or regions of those below. Thus, the Great Sage’s intent and compassionate words seek not to know of these individuals, hence this instruction. It is meant to guide the virtuous and noble, great regional lords, loyal ministers, and valiant generals, urging them to cultivate loyal and filial resolve, to honor and serve the heavens without wavering.

If the ominous stars are unseen in the heavens and the local *tǔdì* (土地, "Earthly Deities") are without malevolence, then no disaster will arise. The state will flourish, the people will be at peace, and the merit will be boundless. Often, those who act thus will ascend in daylight, attaining the rank of *Tàiqīng Zhēnrén* (太清真人, "Perfect Person of Supreme Clarity").

**Ritual for Officials of Prefectures and Counties to Sever Disasters, Malevolent Portents, and Disturbances in Households and Families**

*Lǎojūn* (老君) says: Common folk, regardless of rank, are all subject to malevolent *qì*, which may violently disrupt them, manifest as strange lights, or possess them through false apparitions. It may strike at household doors, burn dwellings, inflict illness, steal possessions, or frighten poultry and dogs. It may send venomous snakes, rats, foxes, or insects, and countless other spirits, beasts, and strange objects—all manner of blood and water entities—that invade homes as malevolent disturbances. These cannot be enumerated exhaustingly here.»

But the malevolent *qì* of myriad disasters and disturbances—those that come to terrify and afflict people—must all be countered with written talismans (*fú*), which shall forever banish them. Three talismans are recorded here. The remaining talismans are found in the *Sān Bù Záwén* (三部杂文, "Three Sections of Miscellaneous Texts"), which shall be examined and extracted as needed.

Once the talismans are inscribed, the ritual commands: tread the *Jìdì* (蹑地) three times, recite the *Sān Bèi* (纪, "Three Invocations") three times, and perform the *Yǔbù* (禹步) three steps with nine traces. When finished, don the ritual attire, invoke the *Tiānguān* (天关), and with the left hand point toward the household of the afflicted three times. This is to summon the talisman’s power to suppress the malevolent *qì* and disturbances within that family, causing them to exhale a purple cloud and depart from the home.

Then, divide and deliver the talisman to the designated *Yīnchāi* (引差) official or *Liùjiǎ* (六甲) deity of the day. The talisman shall be entrusted to the *Liùjiǎ* (六甲) deity of the day or the *Dìshén* (日神) of the *Liùjiǎ* (六甲) cycle. Present the talisman.

If the inscribed talisman is small, its power alone shall suffice to banish the disturbance. If it is large, then the talisman shall be carried as a written decree (*tiēdié*) to halt the affliction, and the effect shall not exceed one hundred days.

Should the malevolent *qì* persist in its disturbances, one must then take the decree and bind the offending entity, driving it beyond the boundaries of the world. If it returns, it shall be executed without fail. Thus, malevolent disturbances shall be forever eradicated.

**Talisman for Severing a Hundred Disturbances**
This talisman suppresses ill-omened disturbances within a dwelling—such as spectral lights, vengeful spirits, and malevolent dogs that shrink their noses and ascend to beds; boiling wells; venomous snakes and insects; or the sight of bloodied mice. The talisman shall be employed to decapitate these disturbances.

*Lǎojūn* (老君) instructed *Luó Wénqiáng Tiānshī* (罗文强天师, "Master Luo Wénqiáng of the Celestial Dao"):

"For disturbances caused by beasts, dragons, snakes, or *qiáng* (蛟), hang this talisman on a wooden board and affix it to a bamboo pole, raising it to a height of one *zhàng* (丈) two *chǐ* (尺). Within no more than ten days, the malevolent entity shall die, and none shall dare harm others. If the disturbance stems from *guǐshén* (鬼神, "ghostly deities"), then a higher decree of *Chìzhāng* (赤章, "Red Document") must be inscribed and executed to sever the affliction permanently."

The *Hòushèngjūn* (后圣君, "Later Sage-King") further instructed the *Tiānshī* (天师):

"When dragons or *qiáng* (蛟) disturb a household, the Sage-King shall personally issue a decree. The decree shall summon the spirits of the Five Peaks (*Wǔyuè* 五岳), the Four Great Waters (*Sìshè* 四渎), the regional deities of the Nine Provinces (*Jiǔzhōu* 九州), and the communal shrines (*shèmiào* 社庙) to form a united barrier at the thresholds, pooling their strength to capture and drive the malevolent entity.

Once done, the Sage-King shall ascend to the *Tiānguān* (天关), invoke the *Tiāngāng* (天纲), and seal the earthly gateways (*dìhù*). The ritual procedure is as follows: the *Tiānshì* (天式, "Celestial Pattern"), *Dìshì* (地式, "Earthly Pattern"), * Léigōng* (雷公, "Thunder Lord"), *Liùrén* (六壬, "Sixth *Rén* Day"), *Liùjiǎ* (六甲, "Sixth *Jiǎ* Day"), and the Four Seasons (*Sìshí* 四时)—these seven patterns shall be employed in concert to capture and expel the malevolent entity.

The Sage-King shall issue the decree as *Kǎozhào Tiānshī* (考召天师, "Summoning Master"), ascending to the threshold and invoking the *Tiāngāng* (天纲) while performing the *Yǔbù* (禹步). Having donned the ritual attire and invoked the *Tiānguān* (天关), he shall march no more than twenty *lǐ* (里), and within ten *lǐ*, the dragon or *qiáng* shall be captured and brought before him.

Then, perform the *Yǔbù* (禹步) three steps with nine traces three times, and advance with a mighty shout. When finished, grasp the blade (*dāozhī* 刀支) and behead the malevolent entity into two segments, thereby annihilating it permanently. This method is highly efficacious.

Perform the *Jìdì* (蹑地) and *Yǔbù* (禹步) each three times, completing all three iterations. Before each iteration, recite the mighty shout. When finished, issue the great cry anew.

Regardless of whether the disturbance originates in water or land, the Sage-King shall not personally transform or ascend to confront it. Instead, he shall rely upon the power of the earthly domain (*wéidì* 威地) and borrow the strength of the Dao to achieve this feat. The efficacy is profound.

But know this: when the Sage-King issues the decree, the ritual shall proceed in sequence. In the *Jìn* (晋) dynasty, *Xǔ Xùn* (许逊) performed this ritual, ascending to the heavens in broad daylight, and the heavens and earth rejoiced.

*Lǎojūn* (老君) said:

"Among malevolent *qì*, none surpass the dragon, for it can ascend to the heavens. Yet if humans can capture it, the malevolent *qì* shall be drawn to the *Xīngjiàn* (星剑, 'Celestial Blade'). As for the most terrifying and potent malevolent *qì*, none surpass the *qiáng* (蛟), for it can dive into water and hide. Even so, it shall be subdued by the prohibitive arts and captured within the instant.

Thus, the Sage-King is born of the heavens, and his potency is extraordinary. Only by refining one’s mind and calming one’s spirit, avoiding reckless action, and maintaining contemplation of the original Master, shall the ritual be perfected and the malevolent *qì* utterly eradicated.

The blade (*dāozhī* 刀支) for the water deity, water dragon, and *qiáng* (蛟) is located on the left hand’s third finger, on the third node, to the right side. Bind it with crimson silk, and release it on the day the malevolent entity dies.

Severing one dragon or *qiáng* shall yield three thousand times the merit. Ascending to the heavens in daylight, one attains the rank of *Dàxiān Zhēnrén* (大仙真人, 'Perfect Person of Great Immortality').

This method has been passed down through generations, with Daoists employing it to benefit the world and eliminate disturbances.

**Ritual for Daoists to Sever Malevolent Disturbances for Households and Families**

*Lǎojūn* (老君) says:

"In the world, households and families are often wrongfully afflicted by malevolent disturbances, causing unrest and insecurity. But if the Daoist presents a sincere petition to the *Dàdào* (大道, 'Great Dao') and invokes the *Kǎozhào* (考召) Master below, then the afflicted shall kneel and offer the petition. The Master shall employ the ritual to read the petition.

In later times, the *Hòushèngjūn* (后圣君) altered the command to compose a formal accusation (*zhàng*), and Daoists shall present their petitions accordingly. Officials and commoners shall submit true accusations as petitions, and the Master shall judge the accusations.

Once the judgment is complete, the *Kǎozhào* Master shall deliver the verdict, banish the malevolent entity, and issue the talisman. The current decree shall be written as a talisman.

The decree shall command: 'Bind and restrain the entity causing the disturbance, and it shall be immediately severed.' The talisman is found in the 'Miscellaneous Talismans' (*Záshìfú* 杂符文), and it is not fully recorded here.

If the petitioned entity refuses, then the Master shall employ the *Jìdì* (蹑地) three times and invoke the *Fēitiāngāng* (飞天纲) once. Another version states:

'When performing the ritual, the general method is to recite the *Jìdì* (蹑地) without using the *Fēitiāngāng* (飞天纲). Perform the *Yǔbù* (禹步) after dispersing the power, and no other methods shall be employed. After dispersing the power, don the ritual attire, invoke the *Tiānguān* (天关) and point toward the afflicted, then recite the eighteen *zhòu* (咒) of the *Shíbāpiān* (十八篇). The malevolent entity shall be annihilated at the Master’s command, and it shall never again cause disaster.'

*Lǎojūn* (老君) instructed *Huángdì* (黄帝):

"For the common folk who desire life, employ the *Bǎiguài Jié* (捻百怪诀). The incantation is inscribed beneath the nail of the left hand’s thumb, and one shall invoke it with the right hand’s thumb.

[End of] the *Jīnsuǒ Liúzhū Yǐn* (金锁流珠引) [scroll], the twenty-fifth.
[End of] the *Jīnsuǒ Liúzhū Yǐn* (金锁流珠引) [scroll], the twenty-sixth."

The **Great True Sage of Zhōnghuá**, the **Celestial Sovereign** Zàiwáng Fāngpíng, **Zhang Daoling**, **Zhào Shēngwáng**, **Cháng Sīmìng**, **Lǐ Zhòngfǔ**, **Máo Yíng**, **Xǔ Yùfǔ**, and others—**successive compilers**—
**Li Chunfeng**, the **Immortal of Zhōnghuá**, annotated.
**A ritual for kings and emperors to offer to the Great Primordial Celestial Wagon (Dàyuánchēn), the Five Tombs, to reverse death and bring rebirth, to dispel illness and ensure peace—fulfilling one’s wishes.**

This is the **later sage, Master Lǐ**, who transmitted it to the **Celestial Master Zhang Daoling**.

The **Emperor of the Golden Threshold (Tàipíng Jīnquè)** and the **Morning Sovereign (Dìchén)**, the **Later Sage (Hòushèng)**, the **Primordial High Dao Lord (Xuányuán Shàngdàojūn)**, instructed the **Celestial Master Zhang Daoling**:

*"All human lives have their measure of longevity and death, allotted by the Celestial Bureaucracy (Tiāncháo) and the Underworld Tribunals (Dìfǔ). Even the lowliest commoners belong to these authorities—how much more so kings, emperors, and great lords!

If one falls gravely ill or meets sudden calamity, then let the **Great Primordial Celestial Wagon (Dàyuánchēn) and the Five Tombs (Wǔmù)** be invoked to dispel the crisis, reverse illness, and grant the **Great Chapter of Reversing Death and Bringing Rebirth**.

Should one’s fate be exhausted and life’s term reached—such exhaustion of fate is indeed common. In the second year of **Hàn Ān**, on the fifth day of the seventh month, the Emperor was touring **Nánshān**. Along the path, he encountered an old man who reported to him:

*'Your Majesty, return swiftly! On the fifteenth of this month, at noon, the **Pursuing Officials (Zhuīshǐ)** will come to escort you. You shall not return.*

*'Return to Cháng’ān at once! Seek **Lǐ Shàojūn** and present the **Primordial Celestial Wagon Chapter** and the **Five Tombs Chapter of Reversing Death and Bringing Rebirth**. Only then will you be able to return to the Central Kingdom. If you do not act, you shall depart forever.'*

The Emperor, hearing this, was greatly alarmed. He turned and walked a hundred paces, then looked back—no trace of the old man remained. He ordered his attendants to search and summon him. The Emperor then asked: *'Who are you, official?'*"

The old man replied: *"It is the Golden Star. Lǐ Shàojūn is a Great Immortal. Only he can present the Chapter and move the Heavenly Sovereign with his profound virtue—he will surely be granted permission. Others cannot."*

The Emperor commanded his attendants to hasten and seek him out. They found him on the thirteenth day and ordered him to present the Great Chapter. After two recitations, the Emperor fell gravely ill on the fourteenth day, his life hanging by a thread. On the fifteenth day, the Pursuing Officials appeared in a dream to the Emperor, and he was granted an additional nine years as ruler.

At that time, a celestial decree descended, stating: *"You have obtained Lǐ Shàojūn’s Chapter of the Minor Lord, also known as Xuanzi—this is Shàojūn himself. Now present the Great Chapter of the Primordial Celestial Wagon and the Five Tombs of Reversing Death and Bringing Rebirth. You will thereby extend your lifespan, augment your celestial blessings, and be granted a new birth as a human king and sovereign lord. The earlier annotations explain this fully."*

The Heavenly Master imparted this Chapter, originally composed in three scrolls, which roughly aligns with the Lord Lao’s Great Chapter in minor variations but with many added benefits. This is the version now practiced in the world.

The Lord Lao instructed the Divine Farmer Emperor: *"Though humans have a natural lifespan, many do not fulfill it. Out of a hundred, eighty or ninety will not reach their destined years—these are the unlucky ones. Why? Because human decline brings calamity, and those with little fortune will succumb to it. If fortune is abundant, it will surpass the natural limit. Beyond decline and calamity, there are those who, through harsh and violent deeds, invite their own deaths—is this not due to human actions?*

*My own immortality comes from reciting these Chapters to ward off calamity, dispel decline, and preserve life and vitality. The lifespan that can be extended is thus granted, and I passed these writings to the Divine Farmer. The Divine Farmer, with his resolve to nurture life and protect vitality, possessed the nature of the Great Dao. He tested medicines to save people, used Chapters to rescue others from calamity, and compiled the Divine Farmer’s ancient texts into three scrolls: the first on Reversing Death, the second on Removing Malevolent Influences, and the third on the Auspicious Hours—this is the Chapter addressed to the Heavenly Sovereign.*

*The Lord Lao said: ‘I also taught the Divine Farmer the Step of the Dry Cloud as the method for reciting the Chapters. This is the same as the ‘Walking on the Earth’ rhythm, later known as the Yu Step—this is the Dry Cloud Step. It not only saves oneself but also brings longevity. Later, I instructed my disciples to practice this method of rescue and salvation, which was passed down through generations as the Dry Cloud lineage, never broken. Now, when reciting this Chapter, one must perform the Step of the Dry Cloud, manipulate the incantations, and summon the Three Officials of Heaven, Earth, and Water to release and redeem the soul and spirit, only then may one present the Chapter to the Heavenly Sovereign and beg for an extended term—thus achieving rebirth and transcending all decline and calamity, even if one’s time has come, one will still be reborn.*

*Lǐ Shàojūn has already rescued hundreds who were near death, and his disciples have long used the Dry Cloud Step to save others, all regaining their lives. The ritual states: First, issue the written Chapter. The Chapter is a declaration. When summoning the Master of the Ritual, he must first declare the Chapter, then notify the gods of the Five Mountains and Four Seas, the Nine Provinces’ ancestral shrines and community officials, and command them to first rescue and treat the afflicted, making sure to present it to the Heavenly Sovereign before the Chapter’s recitation and treatment, thus attaining approval and reaching the desired effect.*

*After the Master of the Ritual receives the Chapter, he seals it with the ancestral shrines and presents it together, ordering the illness to retreat swiftly. If the illness retreats within the set days, then he must perform the ‘Walking on the Earth’ rhythm three times, dress in ceremonial robes, and turn the Heavenly Gate, always pointing to the afflicted’s palace or residence. The illness will then retreat immediately. After presenting to the Heavenly Sovereign, the illness gradually improves. Within three days, manipulate the incantations of the Chief Inspector and others, including the ‘Heavenly Heart Incantation’ and the ‘Earthly Heart Incantation.’ These three incantations are used in the ritual to seal the Chapter and prohibit the calamity.*

*The incantations are found within the *Palm of Incantations*. The Heavenly Master said: ‘When the Son of Heaven presents a Chapter, he must use sincerity to govern all things. The earlier decree mentions a thousand bolts of silk and twenty stones of gold, all of which are separate ceremonial offerings for the Chapter. This Chapter does not require additional inscriptions. After presenting the Chapter, within three days there will be a report. These reports are all false, using different words to convey the message, not the actual words.*

*Why? Because the Son of Heaven is of the utmost reverence, so his reports come from the Heavenly Tribunals and Earthly Registries, not in actual words. If humans were to know these false reports before the matter was approved, they might spread baseless claims. Therefore, the report uses hidden words and deep meanings, not allowing common people to know. This is the method of the Heavenly Tribunals’ reports. It is done thus.*

*For the method of presenting the Great Chapter of the Primordial Celestial Wagon and the Five Tombs of Reversing Death and Bringing Rebirth to the lords of great and minor states, three-ranked and five-ranked officials, and others of high rank, the illness will be swiftly removed, and the afflicted will attain peace and safety as desired. For commoners who follow the diagram and believe in the Chapter, their illnesses will be reduced by a tenth, taking one part out of ten.*

*The Lord Lao said: ‘The minor states’ lords are the sires and kings—today’s prefectural officials. Among these lords, there are ranks of high and low. For those suffering from severe calamities and illnesses, lying gravely ill upon their beds, one may first issue a written summons. The summons is like today’s sealed orders. In ancient times, the term ‘summons’ referred to a ritual seal with three stamps: the Unbeginning Five Spirits Seal, today’s Later Sage Seal. The ‘Great Sage Seal’ is the supreme seal. There is also the ‘Heavenly Tribunals Seal,’ which is the seal of the Three Heavens’ Great Sage.*

*It is used to capture the Heavenly Fox and the Sacrificial Beast, as well as for the lords of minor states to treat illnesses. When receiving the talismans of the Five Deities—Green Dragon, White Tiger, Vermilion Bird, Dark Tortoise, and Yellow Court—one uses this seal to rectify one’s true *qi*, which is employed by the Immortal Officials. The summons will prevent malevolent spirits from acting against them. Afterward, one must set a limit for a certain day when the illness will be removed and healed.*"

The decree of the talisman shall not be written in full. If no harm is removed, then the full decree shall be written. In ancient times, this was called the *Upper Heavenly Sovereign’s Decree*. Now it is altered to read: *"The Most Peaceful Golden Threshold Emperor, the Morning Star, the Later Sage, the Mysterious Primordial Dao Lord"*—also called the *Jade Emperor of Heaven*—no longer bearing the title *Heavenly Sovereign*.

To the *Upper Heavenly Sovereign*, one petitions for a direct command to the Three Officials, requesting an extension of life and added years. If granted ten or twenty years, one then recites the step-curse. This follows the method of the *First Rank* in the previous section. The *Earthly Framework Step-Curse* is prepared as before, using the *Sovereign’s Method of Step-Curse*—though the written decree and talisman differ slightly. The text of the decree is separate and not detailed here; it is not recorded in its entirety. For commoners, the priest assesses their poverty or wealth, and those who can afford it take one-tenth of this decree in faith. If they cannot, they contribute according to their means, ensuring no deficiency, lest the matter fail to reach fruition.

**Method to Eliminate Locust Plagues and Protect Crops from Heavenly Fire**
The *Venerable Lord* says: This calamity is not wrought by Heaven, but by the local earthly spirits, who fail to assist in virtue and blessings, thus allowing the disaster to arise. On a *Bing-Yin* or *Ding-Mao* day, within the chamber, tread the *Framework* three times, with the Five Stars ascending from Wood to Fire. After three cycles, turn to the Fire Star and form the *Heavenly Pass Seal* with five pathways. Repeat this three times. Upon completion, face forward and perform the *Yu-Step* three steps, nine traces. Then, with the left hand, dispatch the talisman to the four corners of the cultivated fields, marking them with a bamboo pole twelve *chi* high. Gradually, the locust plague shall dissipate. This method is of great efficacy.

The *Later Sage Lord* transmitted the *Locust Plague Method*, found in the second joint of the left middle finger. The five-pathway talisman appears in the *Lingbao Threefold Miscellaneous Talismans* and shall not be repeated here. These five pathways originate from the *Upper Pure Capital’s Forbidden Precincts*, where the *Venerable Lord* bestowed them upon Emperor Yao to benefit the world. Thereafter, locust plagues diminished. Before Yao’s reign, the Nine Regions suffered such disasters annually.

**Regulations for National and Personal Dao Cultivation, Including Ritual Instruments and Ordinances**
From the *Venerable Lord’s Prohibitions and Ordinances*:

**Upper Rank Celestial Daoists** must wield nine swords to assist the Celestial Venerable, subdue the Nine Wilds, and sever Heavenly Demons. They are:
1. *Equal-Body Sword*,
2. *Purple Smoke Courtly Venerable’s Ornamental Sword*,
3. *Soul-Subduing Sword*,
4. *Evil-Beheading Sword*,
5. *True-Guarding Sword*,
6. *Spirit-Guarding Sword*,
7. *Heaven-Inspecting Sword*,
8. *Daoist-Inspecting Sword*,
9. *Self-Inspecting Sword*.
These are the *Heavenly Treasures*, worn as talismans.

**Middle Rank Immortal Daoists** use seven swords:
1. *Equal-Body*,
2. *Courtly Venerable*,
3. *Demons-Subduing*,
4. *Evil-Beheading*,
5. *Self-Guarding*,
6. *Spirit-Guarding*,
7. *Heaven-Inspecting*.

**Lower Rank Summoned Daoists** use six swords, corresponding to the *Six Heavenly Stems*:
1. *Equal-Body*,
2. *Courtly Venerable*,
3. *Demons-Subduing*,
4. *Evil-Beheading*,
5. *Self-Guarding*,
6. *Spirit-Guarding*.
The first governs the body; the latter five align with *Metal, Wood, Water, Fire, and Earth*.

These sword regulations also appear in the *Later Sage Lord’s Internal Title: The Venerable Lord’s True Chronology of the World*.

For **human Daoists of the Upper Law**—those with Daoist arts to benefit the world, aid the nation, and save the people—four swords suffice:
1. *Equal-Body*,
2. *Courtly Venerable*,
3. *Demons-Subduing*,
4. *Evil-Beheading*,
following the legal ordinances.

**Purple-Clad Daoists** (also of the Upper Law) use three swords:
1. *Command-Water*,
2. *Self-Protection*,
3. *Evil-Beheading*.

**Crimson-Clad Daoists** use two swords:
1. *Command-Water and Purify Impurities*,
2. *Evil-Beheading*.
These are the Daoists of the *Mid-Autumn Forty-Nine Ranks* and *Lower Element Eighty-One Ranks*, along with the *Single Stage Heavenly Master’s Dao* for regulating *qi*. They follow the *Heavenly Master’s Later Sage Lord’s Original Rites*.

If adhering to the *Heavenly Master’s Rites*, one falls under the false rites of *Tao* and *Lu*, who claim twenty-four ranks to govern the *Twenty-Four Qi*. They also assert that the *Lower Element* follows this pattern, but this is not the practice of the *Authentic One Red-Clad Daoists*—these are the *Blue-Clad Daoists*, who have not yet attained the *Yellow-Clad* rank.

According to the *Original Rites*, *Yellow-Clad Daoists* are granted two swords, while *Blue-* and *Green-Clad Daoists* are permitted one.

This is the teaching of *Wind the First Master*.

**General Regulations for National and Personal Dao Cultivation, Including Ritual Forms and Universal Aid**
The *Venerable Lord* says: Those who aspire to the Dao must first master the *Universal Spirit-Saving Method*, which summons spirits and commands ghosts—its efficacy is like the response of mouth and hand. Nothing surpasses this method.

This method employs two parallel systems: *talismans* (yang forces) and *ritual diagrams* (yin forces). As the *Classics* state: *"Talismans are the yang army; diagrams are the yin army."* When these yin-yang methods are applied universally—without bias or faction—the Daoist path is established, and ascension in broad daylight becomes possible. One may traverse clouds, ascend with body and spirit intact, and even carry one’s dwelling with them. Such feats have been achieved, as evidenced by *Zhang* and *Xu*.

When both talismans and diagrams are employed, Heaven and Earth become purified. This method’s efficacy is such that Heaven, Earth, the Sun, Moon, and Stars align in clarity, and *Taiyi* commands the subordinate forces. The divisions of Heaven and Earth, the Sun and Moon, stand unshaken. Winds and clouds disperse, and the *Magician Kings* flee in submission.

This Dao is subtle and profound, ascending to the Upper Pure. **As the commandments decree, so it shall be done.**

This Dao is the **Seal-Style Talisman** and **Imperial Edict Talisman** of Lord Lao. Another saying: Seal-Style, likewise spoken of. Lord Lao said:

*"Style"* is bestowed in ranks—
the highest rank for **Celestial Immortal Daoists**, who together hold **120 Styles**.
The middle rank for **Divine Immortal Daoists**, who together hold **81 Styles**.
The lowest rank for **Summoning Daoists**—
the ancient **Summoning Masters** of the Four Lords:
One Lord governs **Summoning**, one Lord governs **Orthodox Unity (Zhengyi)**, one Lord governs **Mind**,
all overseeing the **Three Lords** of Summoning.

Yet today’s men fail to grasp its meaning,
and all have altered it to **"Orthodox Unity Daoists"**,
abolishing the three ranks entirely—
thus losing the title of **Summoning Daoists**.

This is the **collective interpretation** of the three houses of **Tao (陶)**, **Lu (陆)**, and **Zhang (张)**.
Later seekers, lacking understanding of its **great Dao’s origin**,
lose the **resolve of the worthy**—
their paths are chaotic, their nature misguided.

Together, they hold **36 Styles**.

The **Later Sage Lord** instructed **Zhang the Heavenly Master**:
*"As Heavenly Master, you must know the three ranks of talismans.
The **Ancient Celestial Sage** previously expelled the three ranks of Daoists—
their Lords, ministers, officials, commoners, and lowest servants.
Now, I command the **Son of Heaven** to use the talismans of **Celestial Immortal Daoists**,
the **Prime Ministers and officials** to use those of **Divine Immortal Daoists**,
and the **nobles and commoners** to use those of **Summoning Daoists**.
If used correctly, the commoners may employ talismans to ward off ghosts and banish evil.
This is the **Six-Ren Style**.*

Lord Lao instructed **Lu Wenqiang (罗文强)**:
*"The gods of Heaven and Earth are all governed by the **Six Canons and Six Styles**.
If you can **reflect deeply and apply them faithfully**,
revering your **original master**,
he will never leave your side,
teaching and guiding you—
nothing shall remain unmastered.
Beware of reckless action for vain gain.
The worthy cultivate the Dao for the sake of their **nation and family**,
transmit **Dharma Seals** and **salvation for beings**,
and heal **sickness and disease**—
they employ the **Celestial Sage’s Ancient Seal**, the **24-Cell Seal**."*

Lord Lao said:
*"This Seal also has three ranks—
**Celestial Immortal Daoists** hold **24 Seals**,
**Divine Immortal Daoists** hold **15 Seals**,
and **Summoning Daoists** hold **12 Seals**.
With Seals and talismans to **command and dispatch**,
and **imperial edicts and documents** in use,
they also transmit **Dharma Seals, Seal-Passes, and Seal-Boards**,
employing them ceaselessly—
exceeding even the **official seals of the court**,
their use never ceases."*

Lord Lao instructed **The Celestial Sovereign Lord (天帝君)**:
*"The **great Dao of Seals and Talismans** is bestowed upon the three ranks of Daoists.
**Celestial Immortal Daoists** are titled **Heavenly Officials**,
governing the **36 Celestial Palaces** above.
Each palace has **24 departments**,
hence they hold **24 Seals**,
to **judge the affairs** of the **24 departmental lords and officials**.

The **Later Sage Lord** established the *Statutes of the Jade Capital Mystic Capital (玉京玄都制令律)*:
*"There are **36 Celestial Immortal Daoists**,
with two ranks of **Highest Officials**—
the **Heavenly Master** is titled **Supreme Chancellor, Supreme Prime Minister**.
There are also the **Three Dukes and Nine Ministers**,
the **Six Secretaries**,
and the **Two Attendants**,
all mirroring the **official ranks of the mortal Son of Heaven**.*

The **Later Sage Lord** further declared:
*"The **Son of Heaven** of the mortal realm,
receiving the **teachings of the Celestial Sage**,
is named **Son of Heaven**—
hence, the title **Heavenly Son**.
His ministers and officials,
like the **Heavenly Sage’s**, share the same ranks and numbers."*

Lord Lao said:
*"The **Celestial Immortal Daoists** use the **Seal of the Jade Sovereign of Upper Purity (上清玉皇)**,
then the **Seal of Yuan Shi (元始)**—
these are the **commonly employed** ones.
**Divine Immortal Daoists** use the **Seal of the Celestial Sage of Jade Capital (玉京太上)**,
also **six characters**,
its use aligning with that of **Celestial Immortals**,
though the **seal characters differ**.
Next comes the **Seal of the Flying Celestial Nine Wilds (飞天九野)**.*

**Summoning Daoists**—
in ancient times called **Summoning Lords**—
today are the **Four Heavenly Lords**.
They use the **Seal of the Celestial Sage of Lord Lao (太上老君)**,
a **three-character Seal**,
governing the **Three Primordial Officials of Heaven, Earth, and Water**.
This Seal is granted to **subdue and capture** unrighteous ghosts,
**deviant gods**, and **rebellious spirits**—
those who refuse submission,
who **craft malevolent *qi* to torment mortals**.
With this Seal, they **stamp talismans and edicts**,
and write **imperial commands** to **banish and sever** them.
If they still resist,
the **Seal is applied and petitioned**,
or **written and beheaded** in judgment.

Next, they use the **Seal of the Three Heavenly Celestial Sages (三天太上)**,
a **six-character Seal**,
governing the **Six Canons**.
This is for **Summoning Daoists**,
who have **meritorious deeds** toward **humans, gods, dragons, and ghosts**—
they may **employ the Seal to transmit Dharma**,
using **Seal-Passes, Seal-Boards, and Seal-Passes of Upper Purity**,
and **great documents** to **petition the Heavenly Departments**,
or **use this talisman** in conjunction.

If they employ **small Summoning documents** or **large talismans and edicts** alone,
they use the **Seal of the Celestial Sage (太上)**.
Beyond these two Seals,
there are **additional Seals and Talismans** for distinct purposes.

These **Seals and Talismans**—
where the **talisman resembles the Seal**—
are not the **orthodox Dharma Seals**,
but named **White Heaven Bestowed Rectangular Talismans**.

For **mortals**—
whether **Summoning Daoists** or **Green-Robed Blue-Robed Daoists**—
they may use **small Seal-Characters**,
or the **Seal of the Duke of Success (遂公)**,
which is a **single-character Seal**.

The **Two-Character Seal**—
one bearing **sole Seal-Characters**,
one bearing **sole Edict-Characters**—
is also called the **Seal of the Duke of Success**.

To **validate the Seal’s efficacy**,
walk **three times in the *Yu Step*** (stomping steps),
or **three strides of the Nine Marks** (散为禹步三步九迹),
**adjusting the robes** and **turning the Heavenly Lock** (天关)
—**left hand for men, right for women**.
Hold the Seal while **aligning with the stars**,
then **recite the invocation**:
*'Heaven’s spirit is holy, Earth’s spirit is holy,
the **Divine Seal descends**—
a hundred ghosts vanish in form.
As the commandments decree, so it shall be done.'*

After the Seal is applied,
then **seal the Talisman**,
and **apply the Seal again** upon it.
Thus, the method is performed—
its efficacy is **great and verified**.

If practiced for **three to five years**,
one shall **naturally attain communion with the gods**,
and **forevermore** need not employ **steps, talismanic arrays, or robe adjustments**—
only **sitting in meditation**, they **turn the Heavenly Lock**,
and **apply the Seal** upon **Talismans and Talismanic Documents**.
The **Talismans shall naturally take effect**.

The **worthy** cultivate the Dao,
fearing **calamities**,
or to **flee disasters**,
or to **aid the nation in flood control**—
they may **traverse water without drowning**,
for **Lord Lao** said:
*"In general, to **restrain the Sea God**,
one may **walk upon water without difficulty**,
as if treading the Earth—
water flows at the **command of the heart**."*

On the **sixth day of the wu-stem** (六戊日), one must always **tread the Earth’s Veins** (蹑地纪).
Doing so repeatedly for **three years** will perfect the **Art of Walking on Water**.

To **tread the Earth’s Veins three times** is to **dissolve into the Nine Steps of Yu’s Pace** (禹步三步九迹).
Then, **adjust the robe**, **turn the Heavenly Lock** (天关),
and **constantly summon the Sea God, River God, and Jiang God**,
asking them of the **matter of traversing water**,
and **commanding the waters to flow backward**—
all **hundred kinds of water arts** must be **enacted by the Sea God**.

Later, when teaching the **Art of Walking on Water**,
the **method without difficulty** must be **mastered through the Dao of the Pincers** (镊之道).
It shall not exceed **three years** before completion.

**Master Lu** practiced the **method of Treading the Earth’s Veins and Flying the Heavenly Ropes** (飞天纲),
but first, he **must learn the essentials of Fire and Water**—
only then shall the **Way be perfected**.

One must **record the sixth day of the wu-stem**,
and repeatedly perform the rites.
The **water spirits shall emerge and submit**,
and **support the walker upon the waters**.

For the **sixth day of the wu-stem rites**:
First, on the **wu-yin day of the seasonal month** (季月中戊寅日),
take **wu-stem soil** (六戊上土) to form mud,
**finger-sized and half-inch long**, and let it dry.
With **yellow thread**, bind it to the **Sea God’s Mark** (海神理),
seal it with **yellow honey**, and **stamp with the Great Auspicious Seal** (大吉印),
using the **Nine Perfections** (九巳).
**Eleven breaths of qi** (炁十一) must be **withheld**—
do not **scatter the qi**.

Then, **cover with the Heavenly Yang qi** (覆天刚炁) seven times,
placing it upon the **Sea God’s Mark** and the **fords to be crossed**—
**instantly, the crossing shall be achieved**.

The **Master’s oral transmission** states:
*"First, **grasp the Veins** (镊纪),
and **apply the Form with diligence**—
then, the method shall succeed.
If the crossing fails, perform it at the moment,
but there shall be **no response**."*

The **incantation lies beneath the feet**:
For crossing a **river**, use the **River God’s Mark** (河神目);
for crossing a **jiang**, use the **Jiang God’s Mark** (江神目).
Each has its own **Mark**.

Always take **dried wu-stem soil** and place it upon the **Mark**,
binding it with **yellow thread**.
To traverse **all rivers and jiaos** (江河),
it shall be **as walking on land**—
**no sinking, no drowning**.
This method is **wonderfully efficacious**.

Later, the **Sage Emperor** told **Master Zhang Daoling**:
*"This method of walking on water,
coming and going like upon land—
you must **transmit it only to the worthy**.
To others, **do not transmit it**,
for if you do, **Heaven shall punish**.
When punishment comes, **people shall drown**.
If someone else gains this ability,
walking upon water like land,
and **common folk** see them
**traversing waters in secret**,
if they do not engage in **theft**,
but are **caught and questioned**,
and **walk away unseen**,
**Heaven shall punish them with death**."*

**Lord Lao** said:
*"The **wu-stem soil** is shaped like a **human form**, two and a half inches long,
mixed with **wood-pulp mud** (木皮和泥).
**Wood-pulp** refers to **paper**—
the **tendon-like substance** (筋) of paper.
This is the **sound of ‘tendon’** (筋之义).
Let them use **mud made from old paper tendons**,
as previously recorded.
Also, on the **wu-stem day**, craft **yellow thread**,
bind it beneath the feet,
and **recite the Hexagrams of Six Ren and Six Gui** (六壬、六癸等诀),
to walk upon water as upon land.
Wherever one **frequently traverses**,
with **fords and crossings**,
there shall be **no obstruction**."*

Yet, in this age,
**many use it with malice and envy**,
hence, **do not practice it**—
**beware**.
For those who **pursue the Dao**,
if they **act recklessly**,
they shall **suffer this calamity and die** as the extreme.

In ancient times, **Ge Xuan** often did this,
and was **suspected by the world**,
called a **Sage**—
though he **avoided worldly punishment**,
he was **denounced to the Underworld**,
and **reported to the Jade Emperor of the Highest Sovereign**.
The **Highest Sovereign was enraged** and **demoted him two ranks**,
so that he **only attained the Way of Non-Death**.
Still, by **imperial decree**,
he was **ordered to traverse the Five Peaks on foot**,
**forbidden to lightly ride tigers and leopards**—
how much more so **not to ride clouds, dragons, cranes, or phoenixes to ascend to Heaven**?
Scholars must **know this as the supreme warning**.

---
**End of Volume Twenty-Six of *The Golden Lock and Flowing Pearl***
**Beginning of Volume Twenty-Seven of *The Golden Lock and Flowing Pearl***

**End of Volume Twenty-Six of *The Golden Lock and Flowing Pearl***
**Beginning of Volume Twenty-Seven of *The Golden Lock and Flowing Pearl***

---

The **Supreme True Daoist Sage of the Central Realm**, **Master Zhai Wang**, **Zhang Daoling**, **Zhao Sheng**, **Wang Chang**, **Li Zhongfu**, **Mao Ying**, **Xu Yu Fu**, and others, were posthumously composed by their descendants. **Daoist Master Li Chunfeng** annotated them. The method of **shrinking space to travel far and wide** for those who aspire to the Dao/Way is as follows:

**The Way of Entering the Celestial Abodes** is appended.

**The Highest Sovereign, Laozi**, said:
*"To earnestly study the Dao/Way with focused intent,
and seek the **manifestation of divine powers (shentong)**,
as the years accumulate, one must have **responses (youying)**.
After attaining **responses (youying)**,
this is **divine power (shentong)**.
Following **divine power (shentong)**,
do not recklessly employ or speak of it,
for the sake of pursuing the **Supreme Dao (zhidao)**.
If one can use **compassionate virtue/power (cixin)****
to rescue and aid living beings,
then this is permissible.
But do not frivolously display **divine powers (shentong)****
to show off to the world,
claiming them as my own.
Such a person is not one who truly aspires to the Dao/Way."*

The method states:
*"First, wear the **Earth-Axis Divine Talisman (Dizhou Shenfu)****
on the left side.
The **Earth-Axis Talisman (Dizhoufu)***
is the **Yellow Court General’s Symbol (Huangting Jiangjunfu)***,
with three scrolls and twenty-four generals.
These generals can **shrink the earth’s pulse (suedimao)***,
condensing a thousand *li* into five *li*,
or even into a space of a hundred paces,
and a ten-thousand *li* journey into ten *li*,
or even five paces.
In ancient times, **Master Hu Gong** could perform this,
and **Fei Changfang** encountered it.
After spending one night in Hu’s abode,
Fei’s arrival was delayed by three years.
Thus, he received this talisman,
and could **shrink the earth’s pulse (suedimao)***,
traveling ten thousand *li* in a day—
no one could catch up to him.

He only knew of **shrinking the earth’s pulse (suedimao)***,
but not that the earth’s pulse also belongs to the **Northern Dipper’s jurisdiction (Beidou suoguan)***.
Whether one wishes to **shrink or expand it (suediyu)***,
all is at one’s discretion.

**Fei Changfang** said:
*"I can expand a single pace of earth into a thousand *li* of rivers and mountains,
and condense a thousand *li* of rivers and mountains into a single pace of earth—
this is because **divine power (shentong)** is unrestricted.
As such, it is worn on the left side,
and when one treads the **Earth’s Measure (diji)***,
moving forward and backward, upside down and right-side up,
repeating five times,
this is called **completing the Five Phases (Jinmu Shuihuo Tu)***—
the **Five Phases (Wuxing)*** of **Metal, Wood, Water, Fire, and Earth**.

Again, one may scatter the steps as the **Yugong’s Steps (Yubu)***,
taking three steps with nine traces three times,
then transforming into twelve steps twice,
and again into fifteen steps twice.
Adjust the clothing,
turn the **Celestial Pass (Tian Guan)***,
point to the earth,
and pinch the **incantation (zhe)***.
The **incantation (zhe)*** is at the base of the right thumb,
inside the palm is the **Guan (监) Incantation**,
and below is the **Doushi (都使) Incantation**.
Then pinch the **Generals of the Earth’s Virtue/Power (Shen) and Earth’s Pulse (Dimao)***—
the **Doushi (都使) Generals of the Earth’s Pulse (Dimao)***,
and the **Doushi (都使) Generals of the Earth’s Core (Dixin)***.

Later, the **Sage of the Later Generation (Hou Shengjun)***
instructed the **Heavenly Master (Tianshi)***) thus:
*"On days of **Geng-Yin, Xin-Mao, Wu-Chen, Ji-Si***—
the **Earth-Pulse (Dimao)*** and **Earth-Core (Dixin)*** incantations—
