the **Earth’s Core (Dixin)*** lies on the left side,
opposite the joint of the right thumb,
and is always marked with **vermilion and ink (zhumofu)***.
This is to summon the **Earth’s Spirit (Dishen)***.
With the right hand, pinch the **Jue (决) Incantation**,
and with the left hand, pinch the **Gai (夬) Incantation**.

Before one’s studies are complete,
always remember this:
seal it with **vermilion and ink (zhumofu)***.
After three years,
suddenly apply it on one day,
and instantly arrive at a place ten thousand *li* distant—
in another province or district—
for this is the **Earth’s Spirit (Dishen)***
that moves one there,
and this often occurs in practice.*

**Laozi** said:
*"When **traversing the Dao’s qi (xingjinqi)***,
one **shifts and transforms the celestial lodges (duanjingxingzu)***.
To **sever rivers and condense earth (duanjian suedimao)***,
all are methods that can be passed on
only by those with **faith (xin)***—
not by others who would recklessly transmit them.
If one transmits them and then **recklessly employs (wangyong)***
them, yet does not **fully grasp the divine power (shentong)***,
and moreover, if one’s heart is **unbalanced and unjust (xingcusuo)***,
of **coarse and evil nature (xingcusuo)***,
acting in **haste and rashness (jicong)***,
with **poisonous intent (xindutuo)***—
then such a person must only be told of **the Way of Repentance (gaodao)***,
and **transmission to this person must be strictly forbidden**.
For this is the **supreme method (shangfa)*** of Daoism,
**shrinking space to travel far and wide (suedihuailai)***—
like turning one’s finger to reach the palm.

**The Way of Entering the Celestial Abodes**."

The **Venerable Sage** told the **Great King**:

*"The masters of the underworld—those **Celestial Immortals** of the **Cavernous Heavens**—possess only the **Way of enduring life and longevity**, known as the **Land of the Deathless**. Their ranks are divided into three titles: the first are called **Celestial Masters of the Cavernous Heavens**, the second **Record-Keepers of Fate**, and the third **Registrars of Deeds**.

If you wish to enter the Cavern, do so on the **sixth day of the third or ninth lunar month**, tracing the **Earth’s Measure** with **Yu’s Steps**—first stepping upon the **Earth’s Measure**, then performing **Yu’s Steps** three times with nine strides, followed by twelve steps, then fifteen. Upon completion, **adjust your celestial robe**, turn the **Heavenly Bolt**, and with nine movements of your fingers, point toward the **Cavern’s Gate**.

Often, within no more than three or five days, the **Cavern’s Gate** will suddenly open of its own accord. If a **woman** appears, do not follow her inside. Wait until the **Jade Maiden** enters first—then, after she has advanced roughly a hundred paces, you may enter. If a **man** emerges, you may follow him without hesitation.

The **Celestial Robe**, the **Heavenly Bolt**, and the finger-movements that open the **Cavern’s Gate**—when a person exits directly, another may enter directly in turn. If a **woman** is to enter first, calculate a hundred paces ahead before following behind—this is the **Lair of the Female Immortal**.

**Laozi said:**
*'To enter the Cavern, let the light of the sun and moon illuminate your path ahead. Invoke the **Wild Boar of Wu**, the **Mandarin Duck**, the **Lion**, the **White Crane**, the **Azure Dragon**, the **White Tiger**, the **Dark Turtle**, and the **Vermilion Bird**. With your **left hand**, pinch the **Cavern’s Gate Incantation**; with your **right hand**, apply **cinnabar and ink** to the **Cavernous Heaven Incantation**.

In your **left hand**, hold a **small dagger of the Earth’s Core**—this is the **Cavernous Heaven Incantation**. On the **center of your right palm**, near the elbow’s crease, inscribe the character **地 (Earth)**. When complete, this is called the **Cavernous Heaven Incantation**. Three to two months before entering the Cavern, repeatedly apply **cinnabar and ink** to it. Upon reaching the **Cavern’s Gate**, again pinch it with your **right hand**—then it will open of its own accord, and the **Spirit** will emerge to welcome you inside.

Once you enter the **Cavern’s Gate**, it will open by itself, and the **Spirit** will guide you in.

**The Method of Riding the Dragon, Mounting the Crane, and Traveling by Wind—Entering Heaven, Earth, Water, and Stone.**

**Laozi said:**
*'The **Immortal Adepts** practice such that they can **summon and tame dragons**, **control and ride cranes**. They ascend to Heaven, descend to Earth, and traverse water and stone.

On **days of the *Renchen* stem-branch (壬辰)**, trace the **Earth’s Measure** three times, then scatter into **Yu’s Steps**. On **days of the *Guihai* stem-branch (癸亥)**, recite the **Flying Steps** three times and chant the **Dragon-Riding Incantation**—the incantation is embedded within the **Flying Steps**. After three repetitions, scatter into **Yu’s Steps** three times, then **adjust your celestial robe** and turn the **Heavenly Bolt**.

Now, **point to the Eastern Azure Dragon’s ancestor, Lord Meng Zhang**—surname **Meng**, given name **Zhang**. He is the **Azure Dragon General**. Roughly speaking, the **Dragon’s primordial ancestor** bore the surname **Meng**. Later descendants adopted their own branches, aligning with human surnames. Today, there are those surnamed **Cui, Lu, Li, Zheng, Jiang, Tang, Liang, Chang**, and others. In the **Jin Dynasty**, two dragons arrived from the **Khotan Kingdom**, surnamed **Tian** and **Shi**, residing in the **Jiangnan region** and **Mount TianTai**, coming and going as they pleased. These were successive generations of **Dragon descendants**, as previously recorded.

Next, **point to the Southern Vermilion Dragon’s ancestor, Lord Ling Guang**—surname **Ling**, given name **Guangshi**. Roughly speaking, this is the **lineage of the Vermilion Bird General**. Later descendants changed their surnames to **Zhang, Wang, Zhao, Zhang, Yang, Ying**, and others—successive generations of **Vermilion Dragon offspring**.

Next, **point to the Western White Dragon’s ancestor, Lord Jian Bing**—surname **Jian**, given name **Bing**. Roughly speaking, this is the **lineage of the White Tiger General**. Later descendants adopted the surnames **Bai, Xia, Shang, Ren, Wen, Zhen, Chen, Qian, Yuan**, and others—successive generations of **White Dragon offspring**.

Next, **point to the Northern Black Dragon’s ancestor, Lord Zhi Ming**—surname **Zhi**, given name **Ming**. Roughly speaking, this is the **lineage of the Dark Turtle General**. Later descendants changed their surnames to **Liu, Pei, Yuan, Liu, Huangfu, Guan, Ruan, Kong, Shan, Chou**, and others—successive generations of **Black Dragon offspring**.

Finally, **point to the Central Yellow Dragon’s ancestor, Lord Huang Ting**—surname **Huang**, given name **Ting**. Roughly speaking, this is the **lineage of the Yellow Court General**. Later descendants adopted the surnames **Ding, Dai, Lei, Rang, Mei, Zhou, Chi, He, Ge, Luo, He**, and others—successive generations of **Yellow Dragon offspring**.

These successive **Dragon descendants**, such as those surnamed **Ding, Huang, Chen, Zhao**, and others who come on **direct days (直日)**, will hasten to you. I, as the **Celestial Official**, often enter the **Heavenly Gate**, using you to **ride and guide**. Urgently respond to my summons.

*Think upon Heaven and Earth—let Heaven and Earth brighten for me.
Think upon the sun and moon—let the sun and moon shine for me.
Think upon the rivers and seas—let the rivers and seas clear for me.
As I roam through Heaven and Earth, the sun and moon, the **Spiritual Mountains** and the **River’s banks**, urgently summon the **Sea Dragon**—it must arrive swiftly.
I traverse the **Eight Extremes**, ascending to the **Supreme Polarity of the Highest Purity**—urgently, as the **Law decrees**.

**The Venerable Sage instructs the Heavenly Master on the Dragon-Riding Incantation:**

*'Whether riding the **Dragon** or mounting the **Phoenix**, all rely on the **Heavenly Ropes of Qi**. Riding the **Wind**, the **Clouds**, the **Smoke**, the **Dust**, the **Mist**, or the **Wild Steed**—all use the **Heavenly Ropes of Qi**.

The **Yang Ropes** belong to **Heaven’s Court**, also called the **Heavenly Puff Qi**. The method of obtaining them is to know where **Heaven’s One** resides and apply the corresponding technique.

As in the **Yin-Yang Prohibitions**, there is no greater method than this.

When the time comes, face **Heaven’s One**, kneel, close your eyes, and inhale the **Qi of Heaven’s One** through your nose. Let it transform into a **purple cloud** enveloping your body—twenty-four breaths suffice.

Then, seek the **Heavenly Puff Qi** nine times as the **Guide**, and again five times as the **Heavenly Ropes Qi**.

When moving, lie upon the **Dragon Cloud**, searching as you rise. Pinch your **left hand’s fourth finger at the second joint**, clench your teeth twenty-four times to unblock them, then **stabilize your gaze**, close your **Qi**, and let the method manifest at will.

This technique binds the **Spirit’s Core** with a **thread**, encircling the **Divine Pupil**, then seals it with the **Temporal Divine Seal**—the **Seal of the Temporal Deity**.

The **Temporal Deities** correspond to:
- **January**: **Engaging Brightness (登明)**
- **February**: **River Chief (河魁)**
- **March**: **Following the Chief (从魁)**
- **April**: **Transmission (传送)**
- **May**: **Lesser Auspiciousness (小吉)**
- **June**: **Victory Beforehand (胜先)**
- **July**: **Supreme Unity (太乙)**
- **August**: **Heavenly Ropes (天纲)**
- **September**: **Supreme Rush (太冲)**
- **October**: **Functionary (功曹)**
- **November**: **Great Auspiciousness (大吉)**
- **December**: **Divine Sovereign (神后)**

The practitioner must stand ready according to these distinctions.

**Riding the Dragon or Mounting the Phoenix** depends on the **Dragon-Phoenix principles beneath your feet as the method."*

「The male practitioner rides the **Dragon**, the female mounts the **Phoenix**—these are the **Temporal Deities**.

In ancient times, **Liezi** practiced the **Dragon-riding method**, thus prohibiting this technique. The female practitioner mounts the **white goose**, and **Nüwa** mounts the **crane**; all are variations of this **Phoenix-riding** prohibition.

If one desires to ride the **Dragon**, they must first take the **Tianyi qi (天一炁)** nine times to cover oneself. Then, they take the **Tianxiang qi (天罡炁)** and the **Baihu qi (白虎炁)**, each eleven times, and also strike the teeth as prescribed. The practitioner then kneads the **Du (都)** point, takes a piece of iron from the **six Gēng (庚)** days, about the size of a little finger and one inch and four tenths in length, and hides it above the **Dragon-riding principle** beneath their feet. A white thread is used as a cord to bind it forty-nine times, sealing it with **white honey (白蜜)** and marking it with the **Baihu Seal (白虎印)** and the **From the Chief Seal (从魁印)**. The **Qinglong (青龙, Azure Dragon)** then manifests, and the practitioner may ride at will.

Upon completion, the seal and binding are removed. The practitioner kneads the second joint of the right thumb, exhales seven times, and the **Dragon departs**. All worldly practitioners must be cautious in this matter.

The prohibition of **Dragon-Phoenix riding** extends to **clouds, winds, mists, and dusts**—only those who seek **Daoist transcendence (求仙)** and are of the **absolute generation (绝代)** may achieve this. Otherwise, one must first observe strict **fasting (清斋)** and live in seclusion among the mountains, lest harm befall them by summoning these forces. Be cautious.

The methods for **Phoenix-riding** and **Dragon-riding** are fundamentally the same. Only the **Five Officials (五官)** of the **Temporal Deities (日神)** differ, along with the **hidden scriptures (隐文)** and **distinctive ear points (别耳)**.

**Laojun (老君)** said: The **Phoenix-riding method** is also similar, but the **Dragon-riding incantation (勑咒)** merely changes the phrase to **"eastern Azure Phoenix (青凤)"**. The **Five Directions’ incantations (五方勑请)** are analogous to the **Dragon-riding method**, with slight variations.

In the **Phoenix-riding incantation**, the **Phoenix principle** beneath the left foot is invoked, as depicted in the diagram: *"The Phoenix-riding incantation is this."* The **Dragon-riding incantation** pertains to the **Dragon principle** beneath the right foot, as shown in the diagram: *"The Dragon-riding incantation and its principle are already mentioned above, and both are included in the Palm Diagram (掌图)."* One may simply use a **small Dragon-Phoenix (小龙凤)** carved from **tung wood (桐木)**, painted with the five colors, and fastened to the corresponding **principle points (本文理)** beneath the feet. Five-colored threads are also used.

The **Lady of Qin (秦女)**, **Nongyu (弄玉)**, rode the **Luanfeng (鸾凤, mandarin duck and phoenix)** and traveled the **Eight Directions (八方)**, having learned these teachings from **Xiaozi (萧子)**.

Upon completion, she **stepped the Ji (纪) three times**, performed the **Yǔbù (禹步)** nine times, **aligned her attire (配衣)**, turned the **Tiānguān (天关)**, and pointed toward the **eastern Azure Phoenix (青凤)** in the sky, summoning it to control and guide her. She then rode it, circling the heavens and traversing the **Eight Directions** without wearying in the **Daoist palaces (仙府)**.

Regarding the method of **drawing circles on the ground to form rivers or mountains**:

**Laojun (老君)** said: *"When a practitioner of the Dao (志人修道) achieves the Dao (道成), they may move among mortals (因行人间). If they encounter malicious individuals (遇恶人) who pursue them, or thieves (贼) who wish to steal Daoist scriptures (仙经), talismans (符法), secret incantations (秘诀), or spiritual medicines (灵药), and are seen within ten or fifteen li (里), they may avoid danger by stepping into the path’s edge, stepping the Ji (纪) three times, then dispersing into the Yǔbù (禹步)—three steps, nine strides. Upon completion, they align their attire (配衣), turn the Tiānguān (天关), and point inward, transforming the ground into a river or sea (化地为江海), which the pursuers cannot cross. The practitioner then retreats and hides themselves; after the pursuers disperse, they return to the ground, which has reverted to its normal state, and alter the perception of the thieves’ eyes. In ancient times, many Daoists employed this method. If someone forcibly crosses, they will drown and die. This is because their **direct Tianqi (直炁)** movement clashes with the **Tianqi’s command to disrupt (炁干冲始要令)**—it appears as if they drowned.

If the pursuer is killed, it is by the **Northern Dipper’s martial forces (北斗中兵)**.

The **incantation of severing the pursuer’s blade (捻人刀支诀)** follows the **Five Phases (金木水火土)** incantations. Those from the **eastern direction (东方)** have names associated with **wood (木)**, those from the **southern direction (南方)** follow the **fire (火) incantation**, and the **Five Emperors (五帝)** are invoked for correspondence.

**Laojun (老君)** said: *"If a practitioner is maliciously pursued or captured by evil individuals, they must not rashly engage in killing. Instead, they should remain as before, stepping the Ji (纪) and Yǔbù (禹步), aligning their attire (配衣), turning the Tiānguān (天关), and pointing toward the grass and trees, forming a continuous mountain range (指草林木为山山相连接). They then enter this mountain and hide themselves. Once the pursuers disperse, they emerge from the mountain, which then reverts to its original state—no longer a mountain. The pursuers will be baffled by this inexplicable transformation, searching for the mountain’s location their entire lives without finding it, and eventually abandoning the pursuit.

Regarding the method of **transforming vessels into the Six Jia (六甲) and Seven Stars (七星), and appearing or disappearing in the Tianying (天营, Heavenly Encampment)**:

**Taishang Laojun (太上老君)**—*"Taishang (太上)" refers to Laojun (老君).*"

This is the **Taishang Laojun’s** lineage, thus the later sages of the Dao/Way reverently honor him as **Taishang Laojun**. He said: *"Today’s people do not know this. They merely use the name Laojun, without removing the Taishang prefix, which is incorrect."*

As for those who cultivate the **Six Jia (六甲)**, upon completion of the second level, they attain the rank of **intermediate cultivators**. Those of the highest level, however, are **Taishang Laojun himself**, who personally wears the **Six Jia talisman**. Another highest level is the **Lingfei Six Jia talisman (灵飞六甲符)**.

When practicing the **Ji (纪) and Yǔbù (禹步)**, upon completion of the third level, one must further receive the **San Yuan (三元) and Wu De (五德)**. **San Yuan** refers to the **San Yuan fa lu (三元法箓)**. **Wu De** refers to the **Five Deities’ talismans**: Green Dragon (青龙), White Tiger (白虎), Vermilion Bird (朱雀), Dark Tortoise (玄武), and Yellow Court (黄庭).

Those who have ascended through the **Thirty-Six Stages (三十六阶)** of Dao/Way cultivation and study this method must first receive the talismans to attain full qualifications. Only then can they **communicate with the spirits**, and through this, they can point to small vessels, causing them to contain the **Heaven and Earth**.

The marvelous and divine efficacy of this method is beyond measure. In ancient times, **Master Fu Gong (壶公)** taught **Fei Changfang (费长房)** this practice. The talismans, once fully received, naturally enable spiritual communication and unpredictable transformations—one can alter a vessel no larger than a **sheng (一升)**, making it vast enough to contain the **Heaven and Earth**, just as the original creation of the cosmos unfolded.

One can also obtain the **Spring Regengzi (春庚子)** and cultivate the **Xianhu (仙壶, Immortal Vessel)**. The **Xianhu** resembles a small **gengzi (罂子)**, capable of holding **one and a half sheng (一升半)**. With careful cultivation, one takes the **Regengzi day (庚子日)**—such as the **Regengzi day in the second month**—to sow the vessel in the **east-southeast (东南)** direction of one’s residence. If a woman plants it, she must not allow a man to see afterward; if a man plants it, a woman must not see afterward.

By the **eighth month**, when the vessel is ready for harvest, leave **three to five seeds** for ripening. The scriptures state: *"One seed left yields two; the three upper seeds are the middle. Only the middle and upper seeds are kept, while the lower ones are discarded, lest they be insufficient. Hence, more are not left."* Take two vessels with the **best, firmest color** and first fill them with **five catties of cinnabar (朱砂)**, though some say **six catties is the correct method**. Leave them for **sixty days**.

Next, add **one to two catties of male verdigris (曾青)** into the cinnabar, leaving it for **sixty days**. Then, add **sixty days’ worth of realgar (雄黄)**. Next, introduce **two catties of female verdigris (雌黄)** and **two catties of silver mud (银泥)** into each vessel, leaving them for **sixty days** each. Following that, add **two catties of gold mud (金泥)** and **one catty of barberry wax (胡燕脂)**, each for **sixty days**.

Having inserted all **eight substances** into the vessels, each left for **sixty days**, the total duration sums to **six times eight—four hundred and eighty days**. Once this period is complete, take the vessel filled with cinnabar first and recite the **Six Jia talisman of the second level (二等符)** **four hundred times**, inserting it into one vessel.

Hang both vessels on the **east-southeast pillar (东南柱)** of the **Jingzhong (靖中)**, using **wooden blocks of Chinese catalpa (梓木)** to insulate them from the **earthly qi (地炁)**, preventing any disruption that might harm the vessel’s potency.

On a **Jiāzǐ day (甲子日)**, begin the **Ji (纪) and Yǔbù (禹步)**. **Ji (步)** is the **Heavenly Constraint (天纲)**, **Yǔbù (蹑)** is the **Earthly Restraint (地纪)**—thus called **Ji and Yǔbù**. Perform each **three times**. Afterward, recite the **incantations for Heavenly Constraint (天纲)** and **Earthly Restraint (地纪)** in sequence: **eighteen incantations for Earthly Restraint (地纪)**, and **twenty-nine for Heavenly Constraint (天纲)**.

Once the incantations are complete, **dissolve the form** and perform the **Yǔbù (禹步)** three times—**nine steps each time**, totaling **fifteen steps**. Then, **align attire (配衣)**, **turn the Tiānguān (天关)**, and **point toward the two vessels (指二壶)**, nine times each vessel.

Afterward, recite the invocation: *"I wish to ascend as an Immortal, transforming you to contain the Heaven. I wish to establish governance, using you to contain the Earth. Left Camp and Right Camp, Six Jia and Seven Stars. The Left Camp controls talismans, the Right Camp commands forces. When talismans and forces converge, I receive the qi of the Six Jia and Beidou (北斗). After a thousand days, it will be spiritually efficacious."*

The Master of the Pot, **Húgōng**, once taught his oral precepts to **Chángfáng**. *"Fulfillment*—this is how we summon the divine and make it manifest. The divine transformations are boundless; they uphold me as I ascend to the Celestial Court. **Swiftly, swiftly, as the decree commands.** But only on days of the **Jia** stem, perform this—five years hence, the divine efficacy will be great, and you shall attain Immortality.

This is the **Tàishàng** receiving **Húgōng’s** oral precepts, which **Chángfáng** obtained and now transmits orally to me.

The **Lǎojūn** said: *"He who practices the Dao must first cultivate within the heart. If a person’s heart is sincere and can contain Heaven and Earth, then practicing this method will succeed. But if the heart is unbalanced, partial, crooked, or envious—if one learns these arts only to harm others or deceive them, abandoning the straight path—then though one dwells between Heaven and Earth, one will be slain by ghosts and spirits and will not die a natural death. How much less can one, with petty tools, transform into the **Dàluó** Heaven and Earth, unless one’s heart is utterly true, one’s spirit aligned with the sacred transformations, and one’s power in harmony with the **Ming**? Much less can one execute it with true efficacy.

If you encounter one who has received this, treat their heart as a treasure, for the method will not betray you.

The **Tiānshī**, after receiving the **Hòushèngjūn’s** command from the **Beidou**’s Nine True Ones, obtained **twenty-four true laws**. These command the **Beidou**’s lords, the **Dòushén**, the **Furen**, the **Jiaonǚ**, and the **Dùbing Dùguān Fùcáo Shǐzhě**—all to be driven and transformed according to these laws. They suppress, rescue, and deliver from calamities, reverse death, traverse fire and water, command armies, and vanish in plain sight—none shall fail.

Obtaining this gate and using it is as swift as water and fire. The **eleventh law** is found in the **Beidou**’s **ninth upper and lower scrolls**; the **thirteenth law** is in the **twenty volumes** below the **Bázhái** section. What they govern is also spoken of extensively within the **Beidou**.

The **Beidou** are Heaven’s messengers, the bridge and crossing of the Great Dao, the path of the law-gate. Both Heaven and humankind must rely on the **Beidou’s** methods for restraint—this is their authority.

The **Tàishàng Lǎojūn** said: *"Between Heaven and Earth, there are five **Dòu** True Ones. The **Zhōngdòu** is the chief—what mortals now call the **Beidou**. The **Zhōngdòu** is the sovereign, with the **Dìzūn** and **Yùdì** stars as his attendants. The **Beidou** is the minister, with seven consorts and favored daughters. According to mortal accounts, this too has its basis. Though the ancients called the **Zhōngdòu** the **Beidou**, no sage has yet clarified their distinction. Now, consulting the *Celestial Astronomy Diagram*, one may suspect there is another.

According to the *Tiānshī Zhuan*, the **Hòushèngjūn** revealed the names and titles of the five **Dòu** lords and spoke of the **Dìzūn** and **Yùdì** stars in the two **Dòu**. The *Liúzhū Jīng* also states this. Thus, it is known that the **Feibù** (flying steps) belong to the **Zhōngdòu**, while the consorts and favored daughters belong to the **Beidou**. Such celestial deities hold high rank, great virtue, and heavy responsibilities, with wives and children, overseeing inspections and wielding dual authority.

The **Hòushèngjūn** also entrusted the **Tiānshī** with the *Jīnsùo Liúzhū*, a secret not to be divulged. The sacred words were not lightly bestowed upon mortals, and common folk had no means to recognize them—hence the single name by which they are called.

Those of pure resolve who seek the Dao must follow this guidance to attain it—with proof and verification. When the law is applied, ghosts and spirits tremble in reverence and submit to command.

Now, regarding the **Twenty-Eight Constellations**, the **Twenty-Eight Constellations’ True Guidance**—though the *Liúzhū* has already explained them, some methods are omitted and cannot be used. If they are present, they are not spoken of. Beginning from the east and turning rightward, they conclude at the **Northern Dipper’s Central Enclosure**—this too is unsaid.

Those of resolve who seek the **Ultimate Dao** must always practice the **unsaid teaching**. Internally, they refine their bodies; externally, they rescue their families and others. The man of resolve, having obtained this book and its laws—the *Liúzhū*—must always follow the unsaid teaching. Internally, he depends on the law to refine his body, so that the **inner true self** is moved, the law’s efficacy is realized, and his spirit is tempered. Externally, he rescues his family and others, never practicing the external laws of **ritual speech, perception, or form**, which cause beings to cycle through the bonds of birth and death, the affections of life and death, and the hierarchies of nobility and lowliness—all of which are not the straight path.

The man of resolve must know this deeply: follow the Dao’s scriptures and practice the unsaid teaching, dwelling in **wuwei**, gradually awakening, and diligently refining himself, ascending in broad daylight.

The **Lǎojūn** said: *"The **Dōngdòu** Lord is a man of **Wú**, surnamed **Qín**, named **Chú**, with the style **Gànfàn**. Before the **Zhōu**, he attained the Dao and was ennobled as the **Shùdòu** Lord, overseeing the seven great officials of the **East** and the **ten thousand symbols** of the **East Wilds**, as well as the seven great **hosts** of the **East**—**Jiǎo, Hèng**, and the rest. If those born under these seven hosts suffer calamities or are afflicted by malevolent stars, follow the **Liúzhū’s** spoken incantations and methods, perform the rites, and conclude by **treading the Earthly Restraint** three times, dissolving into the **Yǔbù**, turning the **Tiānguān**, and pointing **eighteen times** toward the east. Pinch the **Sìmìng** and **Dōngdòu** incantations with the left thumb’s root, reciting them swiftly. Then chant the **eighteen incantations**—the **Earthly Restraint’s eighteen incantations**—seven times. Seven times. Thus, calamities are dispelled, misfortunes averted, and sicknesses healed. This is for self-practice.

The **Tiānshī** said: If one practices this constantly for **twenty-four years**, they shall become an Immortal. If one does it for a friend or kinsman in distress, it shall also succeed. The method is performed as one’s own; only the names differ.

The **Tiānshī** said: For the **Nán**, **Xī**, and **Běi Dòu**, follow the **Dōngdòu’s** method in steps, incantations, and execution. Only their lords’ names and surnames differ, as listed in the subsequent incantations."*

There is but one incantation, the **Step of the Halter and the Invocation of the Star**. When supplicating, let the words be composed spontaneously at the moment, and when uttering them aloud, rely on the **Twenty-Eight Constellations and their Named Stars**, all of which are detailed in the *Liuzhu Zhengjing*.

Use them according to one’s intent, and success shall follow. Next, the methods for the **Nán Dòu** and its **seven hosts**:

The **Lǎojūn** said: The **Nán Dòu** lord is surnamed **Táng**, named **Lù**, with the appellation **Xuāndào**. He hails from **Tàiyuán**.

Next, the methods for the **Xī Dòu** and its **seven hosts**:

The **Xī Dòu** lord is surnamed **Liú**, named **Qǐ**, with the appellation **Shíyīng**. He is from **Cháng’ān**.

Next, the methods for the **Běi Dòu** and its **seven hosts**:

The **Běi Dòu** lord is surnamed **Chén**, named **Fèng**, with the appellation **Bǎiwàn**, a native of **Jiāngxià**. And so forth, as recorded in the *Liuzhu*.

The four **Dòu** lords and their **twenty-eight Star Officers** are all assigned to the practitioner’s service, and their supplications are likewise performed in accordance with the **heart-hand resonance**. Do not perform them recklessly without cause—otherwise, it will invite retribution and harm oneself.

Next, the methods for the **Sīmìng** (lords of fate):

The **Lǎojūn** said: The **left Sīmìng** is one person, surnamed **Hán**, named **Sī**, with the appellation **Yuánxìn**. He is from **Chángluò**.

The **Sīlù** (recorder), **Sīfá** (punisher), and **Zǔmìng** (assistant to fate) have **thirty-six major officers** in attendance. The **right Sīmìng** is surnamed **Zhāng**, named **Huòyì**, with the appellation **Zǐliáng**, a native of **Guǎngyáng**. The **Sīlù** and others also have **thirty-six major officers** in attendance.

The **Tiānshī** said: The **Hán** and **Zhāng** **Sīmìng** are both ministers of **Emperor Gāo** of the **Hàn dynasty**. The **Lǎojūn** said: Upon obtaining the names of the **left and right Sīmìng**, one may perform the **six Jia days**, follow the **Earthly Restraint**, and recite the incantations as in the previous **Twenty-Eight Constellations** method. Only the incantations vary according to fate, being assigned as the **Sīmìng incantations**. Pinch them accordingly. If practiced diligently, in **two years**, one shall attain **long life**, and emerge with the secret methods of dispelling calamities and averting misfortunes. With prolonged and earnest cultivation, one shall ascend in broad daylight.

*(End of the **Jīnsuǒ Liuzhu** incantations, as recorded in the **Liuzhu Zhengjing**, Volume 27)*
*(End of the **Jīnsuǒ Liuzhu** incantations, as recorded in the **Liuzhu Zhengjing**, Volume 28)*

The **Zhōnghuá Zǒngzhēn Dàxiānzǎi Wáng**—**Fāng Píng**, **Zhāng Dàolíng**, **Zhào Shēng**, **Wáng Cháng**, **Lǐ Zhòngfǔ**, **Máo Yíng**, **Xǔ Yùfǔ**, and others—**are the successive compilers** of this text. The **Daoist Immortal Lǐ Chúnfēng** annotated it, and the **Lawmaster of Consideration** expounded the **Method of Inspection and Circulation** (*Xūnyóu Túfǎ*). The **Tàishàng Lǎojūn** instructed the **Wújí Zhēnréng**—**Dìngguāng**—saying:

*"Surname Zhēn, given name Dìngguāng. According to the* **Gě Xuān Zhuàn** *it states: There were three* **Zhēnréng** *(True Immortals), who descended to bestow the* **Xuānjīng** *(Mysterious Classics). I do not know if this is the* **Zhēnréng Dìngguāng** *(True Immortal Dìngguāng). Perhaps he shares the same name but does not bear the surname* **Zhēn** *due to confusion. Dìngguāng attained the Dao in the* **Liù Guó** *(Six Kingdoms) era and was a* **Qín** *(Qin) man. He ascended by* **bùjí** *(measured steps), becoming the left* **Wújí Zhēnréng** *(True Immortal of the Limitless).*

*To practice the* **bùjí** *(measured steps) Dao, one must first employ the* **Kǎozhào** *(Inspection and Circulation) method, benefiting all beings and establishing merit in the world of sentient beings—this is called* **xiūqiú** *(cultivation and seeking). It is the conduct of the* **Zhēnréng** *(True Immortals).*

*The* **Kǎozhào** *(Inspection and Circulation) method of the Lawmasters requires first the preservation of the* **Wǔdé** *(Five Virtues/Powers):* **Qīnglóng** *(Azure Dragon), Bái Hǔ** *(White Tiger), Zhū Què** *(Vermilion Bird), Xuánwǔ** *(Dark Tortoise), and Huángtíng** *(Yellow Court)—these are the* **Wǔdé Jiāngjūn** *(Five Virtues/Power Generals).*
*In ancient times, when the* **Lǎojūn** *(Laozi) promulgated this method, there were first the* **Sānyuán** *(Three Primordials), followed by the* **Wǔdé** *(Five Virtues/Powers).*
*Now, according to the* **Jīnluó Liúzhū Tú** *(Golden Talisman Flowing Pearl Diagram), the* **Wǔdé Jiāngjūn** *(Five Virtues/Power Generals) are depicted, yet the* **Sānyuán** *(Three Primordials) are absent. Perhaps the* **Sānyuán Jiāngjūn** *(Three Primordial Generals) were separately illustrated in three graded diagrams:* **Hán Hóng Tú** *(Primordial Diagram of the Upper Primordial), Zhōngyuán Tú** *(Diagram of the Middle Primordial), and Xiàyuán Tú** *(Diagram of the Lower Primordial). Their use is unified in the* **Hán Hóng Tú** *(Primordial Diagram of the Upper Primordial).*
*The* **Sānyuán** *(Three Primordials) are further accompanied by the* **Liù Jiǎ** *(Six Jia Days):* **Liù Dīng Liù Jiǎ** *(Six Ding and Six Jia), the* **Yùnǚ Zhēn Guān** *(Jade Maidens and True Officials).*
*The* **Liùjì Shí'èr Shén Guān** *(Six Restraints and Twelve Divine Officials), along with the* **Liù Róng Bā Mán** *(Six Rong and Eight Man tribes), must all be preserved as per the scriptures, ensuring their proper deployment.*

*When descending into the mortal realm, they suppress the malevolent, obstinate, and rebellious* **yāojīng** *(demonic spirits), preventing harm to all beings. They are summoned according to the prescribed methods. If they refuse to comply, they are bound by incantations as per the law. If they still do not submit, they are* **bùdòu** *(confronted in battle),*
*—that is, the* **jì Dìjì** *(Earthly Restraint) method, which follows later—*
*and then they are decapitated. Upon completion, a proclamation is issued to the ancestral shrines to forbid such spirits for a set number of years, determined by the Lawmaster’s household according to the month, day, and hour. A talisman is then given to that person, corresponding to the specified term.*

*To perform the* **bùdòu** *(battle method), one must first practice* **jì Dìjì** *(Earthly Restraint) three times in a purified chamber, dispersing into* **Yǔbù** *(Yu’s Steps)—fifteen steps in total—while wearing the prescribed attire. One then points to the location of the afflicted person’s household, or to the site for exorcism, as per the diagram. Lǐ Chúnfēng** *(Li Chunfeng) said: The immortals always preserve this diagram for use in ascending to the* **Zhēn Cháo** *(True Court) or exorcising a dwelling. It must be kept and applied as needed. One must always consider the original master first, then oneself following the master, never placing oneself before the master.*

*The* **Hòushèng Jūn** *(Later Sage-King) said: Those who earnestly seek the Dao must preserve this diagram every ten days. While traversing the world and its lands, they lead the generals and soldiers, advancing tens of miles beyond—akin to a great general deploying troops and forming battle arrays. They also preserve the* **Shèyù Qiánjūn** *(vanguard troops),*
*—the* **vanguard* **being the* **Hányuán Jiāngjūn** *(Upper Primordial General)* **Táng** *(Tang), the* **Zhōngyuán Jiāngjūn** *(Middle Primordial General)* **Gě** *(Ge)—marching left and right—while the* **Zhū Què Jiāngjūn** *(Vermilion Bird General) stands in the center, guiding the way as per the law. They brandish red halberds, banners, and flags, encircling the* **Zhōu Jiāngjūn** *(Zhou General) and the* **Wǔdé Jiāngjūn** *(Five Virtues/Power Generals) in multiple layers, uniting with the* **Xuánwǔ Liùjì Jiāngjūn** *(Dark Tortoise Six Restraint Generals) to form several battle formations. These fly through the sky, their banners and flags resplendent, covering heaven and earth, unstoppable by any foe. The original master also leads at the forefront.*
*They charge and annihilate the malevolent, obstinate, and demonic spirits.*
*Returning to formation, they shield the* **Zhèngzhēn Zhī Qì** *(True Qi of the Supreme Truth) and the body of the practitioner. They also rescue those who have yet to awaken from calamities and disasters, aiding the nation in stability, delivering those in peril, and dispersing warring armies when they clash. The practitioner’s prolonged sojourn in the world is a means of accumulating* **yīn gōng** *(merit in the unseen), and when this merit is complete, they ascend as an immortal.*

*This method is supremely efficacious, yet it must be kept secret and not recklessly transmitted to unworthy individuals.*

*The* **Lǎojūn** *(Laozi) said: The* **Jīnluó Tú** *(Golden Talisman Diagram) contains only the* **Wǔdé Jiāngjūn** *(Five Virtues/Power Generals), omitting the* **Sānyuán** *(Three Primordials). This is because the* **Wǔxíng** *(Five Phases) are deployed externally to rescue beings, while the* **Sānyuán** *(Three Primordials) internally guard the practitioner. The* **Sānyuán** *(Three Primordials) are stationed within, and the* **Liùjì** *(Six Restraints) and their retinues are bound within them to protect the practitioner’s body from malevolent ghosts.*

*The* **Tiānshì** *(Celestial Master) transmitted this to the* **Hòushèng Jūn** *(Later Sage-King), whose Daoist merit and power were slight, insufficient to rescue others. Thus, he could only guard himself, and the* **Sānyuán** *(Three Primordials) were preserved internally through their upper, middle, and lower diagrams, found in the* **Hán Hóng Zhèngyī** *(Supreme Primordial of the Upper Primordial). The upper diagram is in* **Hán Hóng** *(Primordial Encompassing), while the middle and lower diagrams are in separate* **Zhèngyī** *(Supreme Primordial) diagrams. The* **Wǔxíng** *(Five Phases) rescue beings, the* **Sānyuán** *(Three Primordials) shield the practitioner, and the* **Liù Jiǎ** *(Six Jia Days) capture ghosts—*
*—the* **Liù Jiǎ** *(Six Jia Days) are the direct* **Fú Mǎ** *(talismanic soldiers), following the sun and moon, and aiding in the pursuit and capture of evil ghosts.*
*The* **Qīdòu** *(Seven Battles) invoke the gods. All gods are the* **Běidǒu Shī** *(ministers of the Northern Dipper), who arrive swiftly upon being summoned. This is the* **Tiānshì** *(Celestial Master), the* **Běidǒu** *(Northern Dipper) itself. Yet, within a single day and night—one cycle of heaven—they inspect and patrol all the myriad gods of the earth, aligning with the* **Liù Jiǎ** *(Six Jia Days) in their cosmic harmony.*

*In the* **Jīnluó Tú** *(Golden Talisman Diagram), the* **Yùnǚ Guìfēi** *(Jade Maidens and Noble Consorts) are depicted first, leading and guiding the* **Kǎozhào Fǎshī** *(Lawmasters of Inspection and Circulation).*
*The* **Liù Jiǎ** *(Six Jia Days) include the* **Liù Yùnǚ** *(Six Jade Maidens), and the* **Běidǒu** *(Northern Dipper) has* **Qī Guìfēi** *(Seven Noble Consorts), all of whom are celestial maidens. Since ancient times, the* **Jīnluó Tú** *(Golden Talisman Diagram) has recorded this, and now it is the* **upper section of the* **Jīnsuǒ Liúzhū** *(Golden Lock Flowing Pearl) text.* *The* **Yùnǚ Guìfēi** *(Jade Maidens and Noble Consorts) are shown first, leading the Lawmaster at the forefront. This is to honor the Lawmaster in accordance with ancient practice.*

*This* **Xūnyóu Túzhèn** *(Inspection and Circulation Diagram Formation) is not singular in purpose but encompasses myriad applications. It may be used by kings, emperors, and nobles to heal illnesses, or to rescue beings from disasters and calamities. It may also be employed to deliver soldiers from peril, or when a practitioner encounters bandits, ferocious beasts, or is separated by water and fire. Or when there are epidemics and contagious diseases, or when malevolent humans and ghosts conspire to harm within a dwelling. Or when the children of* **Dàoshì** *(Daoists) and* **Shìjiè** *(Buddhists) clash in their methods, causing confusion and discord. Or when curses, sacrifices, and rituals contradict one another, leading the practitioner’s heart astray and their intentions awry. Or when officials falsely claim power to harm others, or when they fabricate petitions and memorials, falsely invoking ghosts and gods, recklessly submitting them—such calamities and misfortunes, all may be resolved by this* **Xūnyóu** *(Inspection and Circulation) method, bringing justice to all beings."*

「First, one must inspect and circulate for one’s own family, then proceed to others. This method is supremely subtle and wondrous; it must not be recklessly practiced or transmitted—be cautious.

*Lǎojūn* (Laozi/Old Master) says: "For those who wish to resolve the myriad prior calamities, they must first cultivate *Xūnyóu* (Inspection and Circulation) daily, storing one *qi* (存一, *cún-yī*) to perambulate that household. Thus, all toxins dissolve, all gods and spirits perish, and misfortunes are dispelled.

When first embarking upon the perambulation, one should first enter a pure chamber and tread *Yǔbù* (the Earth Step, *Yúbù*) three times, then scatter into *Gǔbù* (Turtle Steps, *禹步*). Three steps make nine traces, exhaling *qi* as a purple cloud, first covering one’s own body.

Once done, proceed to that household, covering the surrounding houses and the person’s body entirely. Whether in battlefields or myriad afflictions, all shall respond instantly and be resolved.

For all things respond to completion. Then, pinch the *zuǒ dūjiān* (Left Marshal, 左都監) and *yòu dūjiān* (Right Marshal, 右都監), followed by the *Yóushī jué* (Perambulation Master’s Secret, 游師訣) and the *Sānshī jué* (Three Masters’ Secret, 三師訣).

Afterward, don the ceremonial attire—*Qíqǔn* (Seven Battles, 七斗成)—where the seven stars and seven battles are all present upon the body. Grasping the *Zhìxīng* (Executive Star, 魒星), point to it three times, then recite the five verses of the *Dìjì zhòu* (Earth Step Sutra/Chant, 地紀咒).

The *Hòushèng* (Later Saints) taught the *Tiānshī* (Celestial Master’s) oral secrets: for great matters, always recite the *Dìjì zhòu* (Earth Step Sutra) in its entirety of nineteen verses, which is the highest. Nothing shall fail to respond as desired.

Pointing three times, all matters dissolve and perish instantly. Thus, one’s endeavors shall succeed, and all harm shall vanish, neither affecting oneself nor others.

The chant reads:
*"Tàishàng chuánjiào, hòushèng liúxíng.*
*Tiānshī qīnshòu, jiǔqiān wànbīng.*
*Xúnchá shífāng, shìqì sānqīng.*
*Shén wú xiōngdǎng, guǐ wú yāojīng.*
*Rén guǐ gèjū, bùdé yǒu zhēng.*
*Xínghuò zhě sǐ, xíngfú zhě shēng.*
*Huòfú wú zhī, suíshǒu fēnmíng.*
*Zuǒ zhǐ sānmiè, yòu zhǐ sìqīng.*
*Wù fàn wú dào, wú dào shèn píng.*
*Yǒuzuì wúshè, wúzuì zìníng.*
*Tiān cì wú fǎ, lìng wú ànxíng.*
*Mò fàn wú wēi, wēi měng qīxīng.*
*Yǐn rǔ xuè, shí rǔ jīng.*
*Yīqiè dàn píngděng, wú dào bù lìng xíng.*
*Yīqiè xīn dúpài, wú dào lìng zhǎnxíng.*
*Jíjí rúlìng shìng.*

Upon completing the chant, one must then visualize the diagram as instructed. The diagrams are of three ranks, as follows:

The first rank is the diagram of *Gǔbù* (Turtle Steps) and *Qǔndǎ* (Fist Battles, 拳打) from the *Liúzhū* (Falling Pearls, 流珠) upper volume, specifically the third step of the *Jīng* (Scripture, 纲) and the ceremonial attire for the *Qǔndǎ* (Fist Battles).

The second rank includes the diagrams of the *Sānyuán Sānwǔ* (Three Five Three-Element Generals, 三五三元) and the ceremonial attire for the generals.

The third rank encompasses the diagrams of *Zhōngyuán* (Mid-Element, 中元), *Xiàyuán* (Lower Element, 下元), and *Shàngyuán Hánhóng* (Upper Element Encompassing Grandeur, 上元含弘), as well as the *Liúshū* (Falling Pearls, 流珠) diagrams.

The practitioner who stores and implements this method shall achieve true results.

*Lǎojūn* (Laozi/Old Master) says: "Those who practice the *Kǎozhào* (Summoning and Inspecting, 考召) method and perambulate the ten directions of the world, rescuing and guiding beings, always acting in equanimity, benefiting the state and their own families, aiding people and saving all things, and performing meritorious deeds between heaven and earth—when their virtue is complete, the *Tàishàng* (Highest Venerable) shall command celestial beings to escort them upward, granting them the position of *Dàxiān Zhēn* (Great Immortal True Person, 大仙真). They shall ascend to the heavenly palaces in broad daylight.

In ancient times, there was a *Rénhuáng* (Human Sovereign, 人皇) who constantly performed hidden virtues for the people, reverently honoring the four categories of heaven, earth, water, and fire, and never failing to uphold them. Moreover, he would daily visualize his own body, perambulating the world within his mind, inspecting and judging beings, ensuring fairness and justice. Those who suffered wrongs or bore grievances wished to see their cases resolved, and in their dreams, they would encounter the *Rénhuáng* (Human Sovereign), who would explain their grievances to them. For fourteen years, he consistently cultivated this method, and whenever common folk faced injustice or bore grievances, they would dream of the *Rénhuáng* (Human Sovereign) resolving their cases. Upon waking, each would know their own guilt, and both parties would blame themselves. Countless thousands of people experienced this.

When his virtue was complete, the *Tàishàng* (Highest Venerable) granted him longevity, making him the *Rénhuáng* (Human Sovereign) with a lifespan of eighteen thousand years. Later, he ascended to the *Xiānqiū* (Celestial Mound, 玄丘) as an immortal.

In ancient times, there was a *Shùshì* (Magician, 術士) named *Lèbā* (樂巴), who skillfully practiced *Cúnxī* (Storing Thought, 存思) and the perambulation of the world, rescuing and aiding beings, subduing gods and pacifying spirits. For decades, he benefited people, and the populace erected temples in his honor across several districts.

Suddenly, a calamity struck the district, and the people sacrificed to *Lèbā* (樂巴). The calamity dispersed instantly. It was not because *Lèbā* (樂巴) himself possessed divine communication, but because his *cúnxī* (stored thought) and visualization evoked a response. Furthermore, the spirits and gods feared and respected his practice, foreknowing their own fate, and thus retreated and dispersed in advance.

Thus, it is known that this method’s divine communication is supremely wondrous. *Lǎojūn* (Laozi/Old Master) once descended to *Shǔjùn* (Sichuan District, 蜀郡) and told *Lèbā* (樂巴): "This method has seven extraordinary powers: first, it can rescue people and establish merit; second, it can command the reverence of ghosts and spirits; third, it can swiftly attain the Dao of immortality; fourth, it can enter battlefields without injury; fifth, it can enter water, fire, and epidemics without contamination; sixth, it can dispel all slander and disputes, both public and private; seventh, it can establish prohibitions against all venomous serpents, fierce beasts, and toxic creatures, compelling them to suppress their malevolent hearts so they dare not harm others—this is most efficacious.

To practice the *Kǎozhào* (Summoning and Inspecting) method, one must first, under a clear master’s guidance, receive the *Běnjīng guì* (Scripture and Talisman of the Original Scripture, 本經箓). The *Běnjīng guì* (Scripture and Talisman of the Original Scripture) refers to the *Jīnsuǒ Liúzhū* (Golden Lock Falling Pearls, 金鎖流珠). There are diagrams within the scripture, such as the *Sānyuán Wǔxíng* (Three-Element Five-Phase, 三元五行) method.

One version states: ‘There are no Three-Element Generals, only the Five-Phase Generals’ diagram, along with the *Liùjiǎ Qīxīng Yùnǚ* (Six Celestial Stems Seven Stars Celestial Maiden, 六甲七星玉女) diagram.’ Each of the Three-Element Generals has their own diagram, which is why they are drawn out. The three generals of the *Shàngyuán* (Upper Element, 上元) are included within the *Hánhóng* (Encompassing Grandeur, 含弘) diagram. Within the *Hánhóng* (Encompassing Grandeur) diagram, the sun, moon, and three elements, the five phases, six celestial stems, seven stars, eight trigrams, and nine palaces, as well as the *Léitíng Yǔshī Fēngbó* (Thunder and Lightning Rain Masters Wind Lords, 雷霆雨師風伯), are all depicted in full detail.

Only after three years may one receive this *Yǐnshū* (Summoning Scripture, 引書). If one has not yet received it, they must not dare to view this text. This text is the *Yuánshǐ qì* (Primordial Beginning *Qi* of Heaven and Earth, 天地元始氣), structured into scripture by the *Zhēnrén* (True Person/Immortal, 真人). Initially, it was a *Tiānshū* (Heavenly Scripture, 天書); later, scholars approximated it to *Rúshū* (Confucian Scripture, 儒書), which is why the world now knows this method as a means to seek immortality.

It dispels toxins and subdues demons to flourish the Dao/Way. From the Zhou and Qin dynasties through the Han, many practiced this method faithfully.»

The world was filled with crafty sorcerers, so the Immortals concealed their secrets and ceased transmission.

The earlier Immortals, after ascending, left behind their unparalleled secrets for seven hundred years without successors.

At the beginning of the Later Jin dynasty, there were the **Zuo** brothers—**Zuo Yuanfang**, a man of Jiangdong, and **Xu Xun**, a man of Qin, now in Jingyang County of Shu. They succeeded in their Daoist lineage.

At the source of Hongji in Jiangxi, they took ten disciples, all of whom became Immortals. Practicing this method, they wandered to heal the world, cultivated virtue, and one by one ascended.

Among the later eleven disciples, none took further disciples, and the lineage of Immortals thus ended.

A hundred years later, at the start of the Qi dynasty, the transmission resumed with **Ge Xuan** as disciple. After Ge Xuan’s era, two generations of **Zheng Siyuan** followed, yet no one could succeed them.

Scholars only spoke of the *qi* (器)—the great vessel, like the Confucian term *shuò* (硕)—yet none possessed even a single *hè* (合) of it. This was a metaphor for the world’s loss of the Immortal Way.

The **Laozi** told **Yin Xiānsheng**:

*"The Wandering Method—if one wholeheartedly seeks its use, nothing will be beyond one’s divine power. A single thought moves, and nothing obstructs it: above, it connects with Heaven; below, it connects with Earth; within, it connects with humanity; subtly, it connects with the numinous. Thus, one can repel ghosts and save people, never missing in a hundred uses, and no thousand evils dare approach.*

*In ancient times, Guangcheng Jun taught the Yellow Emperor to use this method, enabling him to attain *Tiānzhēn* (Heavenly Purity). The Mysterious Woman instructed the Yellow Emperor in this Wandering Method, and after nine years, his mastery extinguished ghostly threats and transformed his Dao. He rode the Ox and Horse to pacify the people—this was the Lady of the Fan clan. Through dream-wandering, she was inspired by the Immortal’s leveling method—this was Wang Jun. Those who wandered and paid respects were the Ten Thousand Spirits and Heavenly Masters, the Wandering Immortal’s music. The True Person of the Celestial Connection wandered to rescue all beings. The Perfected One’s Wandering was met by the Ten Thousand Emperors. The Later Sage’s Wandering saw all the Celestial Beings come to greet, paying homage to the Ten Thousand Saints, subduing the Hundred Spirits, and nurturing all living beings."*

Regarding the **Summoning Method for the Six Star Lords of Longevity**—the diagram for invoking the Six Star Lords of the Southern Dipper:

The **Laozi** said:
*"The Six Star Lords of Longevity are the Six Star Lords of the Southern Dipper. Flying from east to west, the Master focuses his mind toward the east, receiving them below. He also focuses on the Twelve True Persons flying from west to east, turning his face southward, gazing left and right. He further focuses on the Left Marshal of Destiny and the Right Marshal of Records, who oversee registries and calculations, all arriving together, riding flying dragons and phoenixes, dragons pulling grand chariots, with celestial boys and jade maidens holding the Ten Absolute Auspicious Banners. They scatter fragrant flowers in spiraling patterns, covering the sick person’s bed, scattering all manner of blossoms onto the patient’s body, penetrating to the bones and joints.*

*The medicines are administered by the Marshals of Destiny and Records, who then charge the household to guard the home. The Three Generals, the Kitchen God, and the Well Spirit are summoned to bid farewell to the deceased, to recount the origins of the illness, and to ascend to the Northern Palace of Heaven to save the life. The Master embodies the **Taishang Laojun**, holding the True Essence and the Glare of Anger, never straying from his form."*

The Master sits upon a thousand-petaled lotus, composed and solemn.
Though appearing wrathful, he commands the Three Generals guarding the home: *"How dare malevolent spirits intrude upon this dwelling and torment a virtuous and prudent person? Swiftly retrieve the patient’s soul!"*

He questions the Marshal of Destiny, then reproaches the household deities, territorial shrine officials, land and water spirits, and mountain cave deities: *"Which spirit governs this place? Which deity oversees this dwelling’s jurisdiction? Why do you allow these demonic bandits to harm the living?"*

Now, by urgent decree, examine the patient’s fate records—life span and destiny—and promptly address this illness within a set number of days. Dispatch a swift report for salvation.

This method shall be inscribed on talismans and orders, affixed to the household deities, the Three Generals guarding the home, the well and kitchen dragons, and all myriad spirits. It shall also be posted at shrines and ancestral halls.

These are the ancient *fǔxiá* (符檄)—today’s talismans. Another account states: *"Xí* (檄) is a scolding command, compelling malevolent spirits to tremble and depart. If they refuse, summon the shrine deities, the Three Generals guarding the home, and the door, well, and kitchen spirits to unite in seizing and binding them. Alongside the talismans and orders, issue simultaneous decrees to behead them—without guilt. Thus, the spirits are restrained, and the patient recovers within fourteen or twenty-one days without fail."

Later, the Sage Emperor informed the Heavenly Master Dao Ling: *"All mortals are born with their fates and destinies assigned..."*

The **Command** is the vital body itself. What mortals receive at birth as their assigned fate and virtue is their official rank and the land where they draw their stipend—all subject to life and death. The perils of life and death arise from the Five Phases clashing and malevolent spirits conspiring in their operations. If one foreknows this, then from within the Five Phases, one may calculate and restrain them, halting the affliction at once. If they refuse, one may tread the *dìjì* (地纪) three times, don the *dòuyīn* (斗身衣), seize and behead them—thus permanently severing the calamity. Then the person may freely pursue cultivation and attain eternal life.

This method further draws upon the Five Phases’ central alignments. Later, the Sage Emperor instructed Master Yin the True Person: *"To study the Dao, you must know the Six Jia Days. The Six Jia—Jiazi, Jiaxu, and the like—are six days in succession. Tread the *dìjì* three times, then scatter into the *Yǔbù* (禹步), three steps with nine traces, afterward donning the *dòuyīn*, preserving the Two Scenes and Three Elements, the Four Seasons’ *Qīnglóng* (青龙), *Báihǔ* (白虎), *Zhūquè* (朱雀), and *Xuánwǔ* (玄武)—these are the Four Seasons’ overseers of spring, summer, autumn, and winter. The Five Phases: as the Classics say, the Four Seasons’ deities, with the addition of the Yellow Court General, are called the Five Phases. It is also said: In Heaven, they are the Five Stars; on Earth, the Five Forms; in Man, the Five Phases—these are the Five Virtues, sealed by the Most High with their names.

The Six Jia are the direct-day deities and the Jade Maiden’s Lord. The Seven Stars are the Dipper; the Eight Trigrams are the eight directions of Earth. The Nine Palaces encompass Earth and the Central Palace, with the Human Sovereign’s likeness marking the Nine Provinces’ names, elucidating the Nine Palaces’ count. The Three Elements: one element yields three, hence ‘three threes as nine,’ all within the Five Phases. The Nine Palaces, adding the Central Palace, are called the Nine Numbers. It is also said: the Small Nine Palaces are the Nine Provinces’ lands. In the age of the Human Sovereign, this was also called the Nine Palaces—this explains the Small Nine’s count. Today, between Heaven and Earth, the eight directions and the Central Palace’s ninefold count are vast. Hence Zhuangzi said: Heaven has nine wilds, called the Nine Palaces. [Here follows the] containment of thunder and lightning strikes, as depicted in the diagram. The diagram is fully contained within the *Hán-Tóng Tú* (含弘图); retain its use. All methods are preserved for application. For warding off calamities, also employ the pinching technique of the Six Star Lords of Fate.

Often thus, one may save one’s own family and others’ illnesses, rescuing the dying and restoring life. Practicing this for six years, the Southern Dipper extends longevity, and the Six Star Lords—including the Lords of Fate and Records—descend to meet you, speaking of your merits in saving lives and healing diseases, and escort you to ascend to the Upper Clarity.

The Celestial Master told the Emperor: *"There are nine grades to this method. The first is to cultivate and remove one’s own calamities and illnesses. The second is to heal one’s family and kin. The third is to treat the illnesses of kings and ministers, each with its own rank and prescribed method. The highest is to treat the Son of Heaven’s ailments. First, contemplate the Upper Element’s Upper Division’s Tang General, then the Upper Element’s Middle Division’s Li General, then the Upper Element’s Lower Division’s Xu General, then the Middle Element’s Upper Division’s Tang General—this Tang is surnamed Tang, named Hóng, succeeding the Upper Element’s Upper Division’s Tang General in years. The Upper Element’s Tang General, named Duàn, was a man of the Heavenly Sovereign’s era, attaining the Dao with a body nine hundred million *zhang* long. The Middle Element’s Middle Division’s Ge General was a man of King Mu’s time, far removed in years. Next is the Middle Element’s Lower Division’s Zhou General—also from King Mu’s era, a minister of his court. Then come the Three Generals of the Lower Element: Li Huangwang. They were men of the Six Dynasties. Li General was surnamed Li, named Lìzhì, a native of Kuàiji Mountain. In the Qin era, he attained the Dao, and the Most High appointed him as the Upper General of the Lower Element. Next, contemplate the all-pervasive [method], as depicted in the diagram. This is the *Hán-Tóng* [method]."*

Now, summon the Six Longevity Star Lords—six in number—and the Twelve True Persons of the Southern Dipper. Next, summon the Nine Lords of the Northern Dipper, then the Lords of Destiny (司命君), the Lords of Records (司录君), and the Lords of Registers and Fate-Calculations (掌籍掌罔算君)—five in total. Then come the Southern Dipper’s Registrar of Births and the Northern Dipper’s Registrar of Deaths, all arriving together with their retinues of officials, soldiers, and countless myriads—speaking of "hundred thousands," meaning ten million, the number of the great assembly. All assemble in a certain realm.

The altar is set with thirty-four seats: seven to the east, seven to the south, seven to the west, seven to the north, seven in the central palace, two for the Eight Trigrams, two for the Sun Palace, two for the Moon Palace, and the remaining nine seats for the Seven Ancestors, totaling forty-nine. The platform is built with yellow earth spread upon the ground, with mats laid above, and upon the mats, green silk cushions for sitting, as prescribed.

*"As prescribed"* refers to the complete ritual for summoning the Six Longevity Star Lords, with their full ceremonial texts. The ritual text, once complete, already includes all required items and their proper counts—here, it is summarized rather than fully detailed.

Upon completion, meditate upon the Six Longevity Star Lords, as well as the Lords of Destiny and Records, and perform the rites according to the previous methods. No illness treated will fail to heal.

**Second Rank (for nobles and high officials):**
To treat the ailments of princes and ministers, first invoke the Upper Division’s Middle Element Li General, then the Middle Division’s Middle Element Ge General, and finally the Lower Division’s Middle Element Huang General. With the ritual fully prepared, meditate upon the Six Longevity Star Lords, the Lords of Destiny, and the Lords of Records, extending life and curing disease through the prescribed steps and incantations—no illness will resist.

**Third Rank (for officials and commoners):**
For governors, county magistrates, and the populace—regardless of gender—first meditate upon the Upper Division’s Lower Element Xu General, then the Middle Division’s Lower Element Zhou General, and finally the Lower Division’s Lower Element Wang General. With the ritual fully prepared, summon the Six Longevity Star Lords, the Lords of Destiny, and the Lords of Records to descend, prolonging life, curing disease, and saving those at the brink of death. Results manifest instantly.

For treating all manner of illnesses, these three ranks suffice—none will fail. The talismans are found in *The Three Departments’ Miscellaneous Talismans* (《三部杂符》), named according to the ailment, and all will prove effective when entrusted to the proper authority.

**Fourth:** Able to enter battlefields, rendering one unseen by harm or defeat, protecting oneself and others. The method follows as before, with talismans provided separately. These talismans appear in *The Yellow Emperor’s Gathered Mysteries* (《黄帝集灵记》), Volume One.

**Fifth:** Able to enter water, seizing water spirits, dragons, and aquatic creatures of the fish and reptile kind. The method involves stepping the *Earth Memoir* (地纪) seven times and the *Flying Heavenly Rope* (飞天纲) seven times. This is the *Flying Steel Rope*—though not traced on the diagram, one need only visualize the steps upon the ground as per the illustration to achieve it. If mastery of the steps is attained, the *Flying Rope* need not be invoked; visualization alone suffices. In urgent matters, focus the mind, recite the hand seals, and chant the incantation—divine response follows instantly. Why bother with steps or diagrams?

In ancient times, the Daoist adept Zhao Rui practiced the *Memoir-Rope* method for fourteen years. Upon attaining the Dao, he could summon its power with mere thought, requiring no steps. He habitually walked the *Yujian Steps* (禹步), nine strides nine times, mastering the Nine Rivers. He also transformed into twelve steps, governing the Four Seas. Binding his feet with six *ji* (己) earth seals allowed him to enter water as if walking on land.

At the moment of entering water, he would recite the *Six Wu* (六戊) incantation, commanding the water spirits at will—all obeyed.

**Sixth:** Able to guide one through mountains and grasslands without losing one’s way, causing venomous serpents and fierce beasts to submit, and entering fire without harm. All effects manifest as per the previous methods.

**Seventh:** Able to lead one into the Middle Immortal path, achieving longevity and immortality. On one’s birth-day, meditate upon the Southern Dipper’s Six Longevity Star Lords, as well as the Lords of Destiny, Records, Registers, and Fate-Calculations descending as per the diagram. The diagram appears in *The Golden Lock and Flowing Pearl* (《金锁流珠》), Middle Section.

Upon completion, step the *Earth Memoir* and *Flying Rope*—the *Earth Memoir* and *Heavenly Rope*. Scatter the steps, adjust the attire, and recite the nineteen incantations while manipulating the seals. Then recite the *Lords of Destiny* seals, found in the *Flowing Pearl*’s Lower Section, Volume. Finally, chant the nineteen incantations. Upon completion, cease. Practicing thus for four years grants the rank of Earthly Immortal.

**Eighth:** Able to lead one to the Great Immortal path. The Great Immortal is the celestial and terrestrial sage. Some say *Heavenly Immortal* and *Earthly Immortal*, dwelling in mountains.

**Ninth:** Able to guide one, through prolonged practice, to the rank of Supreme True Person. The True Person is the title of the Upper Clarity’s Great Primordial Sage Official. In antiquity, the Supreme Celestial True Saints—such as Guangchengzi and hundreds of other True Persons—all achieved their state through stepping the *Memoir-Rope*, donning the *Dipper Garments* (衣斗), and meditating upon the *Dippers*. The *Dipper Garments* refer to the Northern Dipper; *meditating upon the Dippers* refers to the Southern Dipper.

The Northern Dipper has nine stars, but two are unseen—commoners see only seven. Hence, they are called the *Seven Star Lords*, though unknown are the nine stars and the two *Precision Lords* (二精君). The Southern Dipper has eight stars, but two are unseen—commoners see only six, hence called the *Six Star Lords*, though unknown are the eight stars and the two *Trigram Lords* (二卦君).

The first is the Longevity Lord, the second the Lord of Destiny; the rest are the Lords of Registers, Fate-Calculations, and the Lords of Birth and Death. Those who know this path achieve immortality and become sages instantly—unbound by form, through prolonged cultivation, attaining Heavenly Immortality.

*Conclusion of Volume Twenty-Eight of The Golden Lock and Flowing Pearl*
*Beginning of Volume Twenty-Nine of The Golden Lock and Flowing Pearl*

「The Great True Sage of the Central Realm, Lord of the Dao, **Fāng Píng Zhāng Dàolíng**, **Zhào Shēng**, **Wáng Chǎng**, **Lǐ Zhòngfǔ**, **Máo Yíng**, **Xǔ Yùfǔ** and others, are successive compilers of this text. The Daoist Master **Lǐ Chúnfēng** annotated it. The **Consideration and Summoning Master** expounds the method of **invoking the Wood Official (木官)** to **erect a house (起屋)** and heal illness.

The **Venerable Laozi** instructed the **True Person of Saving the Suffering (救苦真人)**, **Zhèng Rén'ān**, saying: *"As a True Person practicing the Dao, nothing surpasses saving those afflicted with grave illness."* To save one person’s illness, the heavens and earth record it as one merit.

The human body is called a *dwelling-place (舍宅)*, akin to a house. Thus, to heal the sick, one invokes the **Wood Official (木官)**. The Wood Official is, among the Five Phases, the one who governs wood. For instance, if a person born in the **Year of Jiāzǐ (甲子)** has a **Metal Destiny (金命)**, then **Wùchén Wood Official (戊辰木官)** is invoked as the superior—never **Rénwǔ Wood Official (壬午木官)** to erect a house, lest harm befall the patient.

When descending, align with the patient’s **main house (正屋)** and **auxiliary house (正屋)**, as if tracing a diagram. **Felling trees to erect the main house**, **repairing beams and pillars**. Thus, in three days, all illnesses retreat and abate. Further, it is said: *"When a person’s illness is grave, and you, as a master, seek to heal them, merely visualize the patient’s main house and its trees felled—it shall manifest, and the illness shall retreat."* The scripture states: *"House upright, body upright; house crooked, body crooked. House fallen, body fallen."*

Another passage says: *"The human body is a house; if the surrounding trees are numerous, the soul and spirit scatter from the body and cling to the trees, often seen by others as luminous figures—these are the souls and spirits of the ailing."* As a healer, first invoke the **Wood Official** to **fell the trees on either side of the patient’s dwelling**, then **summon the wood and the illness**, constructing a house upon the **birth-qi (生炁)** of the land. The patient’s **Six Heavenly Stems (六甲)** and **Twelve Earthly Branches (行年)** determine the birth-qi location, or also **search the year’s birth-qi** to erect the house, or **repair the existing dwelling**. If all three houses are upright, the patient’s **three souls (三魂)** remain steadfast. But if one house is crooked, one soul shall not be fixed.

For the healer, first master this method, and it shall prove efficacious. The patient’s illness shall retreat, their spirit returning to the body. That night, they may dream of **ascending sages entering a valley of half-suffering (上仙入谷半苦)**—this is the spirit’s return. Upon waking, they sweat profusely, a sign of great recovery.

The **Venerable Laozi** said: *"This method has two applications: one to heal a person’s illness, the other to subdue rebellious subjects, disobedient children, or disciples who defy their master’s commands—then apply this method to them."* The practice is similar to the previous.

The **Venerable Laozi** said: *"For this method, first tread the **Earthly Trigrams (地纪)** three times, then scatter into the **Yǔ Steps (禹步)**—the initial **Nine Steps (初九迹)**. Then reverse and return to the **Trigram Head (纲头)**, and repeat the invocation. Open as **Twelve Steps (十二迹)**, then reverse and open as **Fifteen Steps (十五迹)**. Upon completion, align the **Left and Right Garments (左右配衣)**—the diagram shows both the **Left Garment Method (左配衣法)** and the **Four Battles (斗名)**. The **Right Garment Method (右配衣法)** is also called the **Four Battles (四斗)**—referring to the alignment of left and right garments. In the **First Step Diagram of the Flowing Pearl (《流珠》上卷第一步纲图)**, all follow the pattern of one left and one right. Simply verify and apply as needed.*

Invoke the **Wood Official** to **erect a house (起屋)**—this is to **rectify life (治生)**. **Felling the house (倒屋)**—this is to **rectify death (治死)**. Either method may be chosen at will. The **incantation** lies in the **middle joint of the left ring finger (左手第四指中节)**, twisting it. Or bind it with **five-colored threads (五色线)** for an extended duration.

**Conjure the Venerable Laozi**, the **Primordial Origin (先天地生)**—**conjure the withered wood to regrow branches and leaves (摄枯木花叶再生)**, able to heal a person’s illness swiftly and restore equilibrium.** **Summon and bind the soul and spirit (召摄魂魄)**, ordering them to return to their bodily form. **Upright house, upright body—quickly arise and complete.** *As fast as the ritual decree.*

The **Posterity Sage (后圣君)** said: *"When invoking the Wood Official to erect a house for the sick, there are numbers and hierarchical levels. The highest is for kings and emperors—erecting a main house and auxiliary house for **forty thousand people (四十万人)**, with **ten thousand per region (一方十万人)**. The middle is for prime ministers and high officials—**four thousand people (四千人)**, with **one thousand per region (一方一千人)**. The lowest is for the **five ranks (五品)** down to commoners—**four hundred people (四百人)**, with **one hundred per region (一方一百人)**. Together, they erect the main house and auxiliary house, fell trees and gather wood, grasp earth and clear grass—grass being the **commoner’s term for killing qi (杀炁)** or **calamity (殃)**. They raise pillars, install beams, and frame the house. At the appointed time, they visualize and complete it—house built, patient recovered."* **Proclaiming the decree:** *"The Wood Official swiftly constructs the house; house completed, the patient’s fortune flourishes. Fortune born, soul and spirit return to form. Illness vanishes, blessings received—long life attained."* *As fast as the ritual decree.*

The **incantation for restoring the soul and returning the spirit (捻还魂入神正魄诀)** is in the **middle joint of the left thumb (左手大指中节)**, binding it with **five-colored silk (五色丝)** for **forty-nine days (二七日)**.

The **Venerable Laozi** told **Luó Zhēnrén**: *"Luó Wénqiáng, a great minister of the **Yīn Dynasty (殷)**, was skilled in **ritual prohibitions and incantations (禁咒之术)**. He often aided people in averting disasters and healing illnesses, fulfilling his merits by the **third wǔ (三午)**. He ascended in broad daylight. This method has multiple applications: one to heal illness, two to **ward off evil (辟恶)**, three to **treat afflictions and harm (治患害)**, four to **dissolve slander (消口舌)**, five to **prohibit (禁)**, six to **translocate (移)**, seven to **defeat (败)**.* These seven methods can address both auspicious and inauspicious matters.

The rest I heard from my master’s lips, passed orally—keep it secret and do not divulge.

**The Consideration and Summoning Master** expounds the method of **visualizing the roaming body (说身巡游)** and **inspecting the patient’s home (病家图法)**.

The **Venerable Laozi** told **Wénqiáng Zhēnrén**: *"For a Daoist master to aid others as a healer, to tread and prohibit illnesses, is no simple task. They must first purify their body and calm their mind. Whether prohibiting or incanting, all serve to heal a hundred maladies—this is a great merit. This single method cures illness: the master first visualizes and enters the patient’s home, passing through the door into their chamber. Seeing the patient lying on their bed, the master invokes and summons, visualizing a **wild troop of horses (阵野马)** and **scattered soldiers (散吏兵)**, seizing clubs to drive them away, trampling them as **malevolent ghosts and thieves (祟鬼贼)**, startling them into fleeing and scattering. Again, visualize **great wild elephants (野堵大象)** and **lions (师子)** coming in one by one, entering the chamber, devouring food as **demonic spirits and wild ghosts (妖精野鬼)**, then fleeing."*

«Again, visualize **serpents (蛇)**, **centipedes (蜈蚣)**, and other venomous creatures (毒物), seizing and capturing them as **malevolent ghosts, thieves, and demonic spirits (祟鬼贼精邪)**, driving them away and scattering them.

Then, invoke the **specific demonic entity (某鬼)**—each has its own classification: **mountain ghosts (山鬼)**, **spirits (精鬼)**, **injury ghosts (傷鬼)**, **goblins and specters (魍魉)**, **demonic monkeys and rodents (邪精猴鼠)**, or **hobgoblins, forest imps, and other malevolent spirits (魑魅精鬼)**. These classifications are found in the *Liu Zhu* ["Falling Pearls"] **palm incantations (掌訣)**.

The **incantation method (法訣)** states: The master first treads the ground three times, stepping in the **Yugaito’s stride (禹步)**, three steps with nine traces (三步九迹), three repetitions (三遍), then adjusts their attire (配衣). After adjusting their attire, the master holds the **Arcid star (魒星)** with their left hand, pointing it seven times (七遍), then visualizes themselves clad in **purple robes (紫衣)** and a **traveler’s hat (远游冠)**, accompanied by **generals and soldiers (侍从将军吏兵)** as before. The master proceeds to the patient’s home—whether in **such-and-such State, County, or Village (某州县乡里)**, or a **certain official (某官人)** or **commoner (某百姓)**—declaring, *“This commoner (百姓) has contracted this illness,”* and so forth.

The master leads the soldiers with ropes to drive the horses, galloping and trampling the malevolent ghosts. In the *Liu Zhu Tu* ["Falling Pearls Diagram"], **lions (师子)** are not depicted—only **pigs and horses (猪马)** along with soldiers—though fewer in number. The master says: *“Visualizing the lion brings it forth; there is no need to draw it.”*

The **oral incantation (口訣)** states:
*“Snakes, centipedes, crows, and other fierce beings (禹乌之猛)—all that must be prohibited—are demonic spirits that devour ghosts. Using this method immediately cures illness (食鬼治病，用之立差).”*

When **lions (师子)** and other wild beasts are invoked, they charge into the dwelling, roaming left and right within and without. They seize and devour the malevolent ghosts, and the patient’s illness is immediately cured—there is none who does not recover (无有不差者).

The **Celestial Master (天师)** says: *“I transmit these oral incantations to the later sages. This method has three applications:
1. To heal human illness (救人病),
2. To cause malevolent individuals to fall ill themselves, preventing them from coming to harm me (令恶人自病，去不来害我),
3. To dismantle the dwellings of ghosts and spirits, which vanish immediately upon doing so (破鬼神居止之处，立即见消).”*

In the past, there was **Bian Que (扁鹊)**, who often practiced this method to cure the sick—all recovered (皆.差). Time and again, he did so.

One day, **the Highest Daoist Lord (太上大道君)** sent a messenger to bestow upon him the **method of reviving the dead (起死人之法)**. Suddenly, he could **split open the abdomen and treat the intestines (破腹治肠)**, distinguishing the **five viscera (五藏)**. He revived **Pei’s Crown Prince (虢太子)**, **Zhou’s Marquis of Shun (周顺侯)**, and **Yan’s King’s Concubine (燕王次妃)**, who had all died. Afterward, they lived for **twenty, thirty, or ten years (二十年、三十年、十年)** before dying again.

Que lived for **seventy-nine years (七十九年)** in this world, repeatedly reviving those who had died—no one knows the number.

Later, one day, **a wind officer (风吏)** and **a thunder master (雷师)** arrived to escort him to the imperial court (御前), with **the Azure Dragon (青龙)** and **the White Tiger (白虎)** supporting him on either side. Thousands of officials rode ahead, guiding him to **the Southern Mountains (南山)** before he departed. No one knows to whom he passed on the **method of reviving the dead (起死法)**.

In the present age, no one practices this method.»

「Again, there was **Zhao Mountain (赵山)**, who served as the **Magistrate of Xīhé (西河令)** during the reign of **Emperor Wǔ of Hàn (汉武帝)**. His wife, **Mistress Mèng (孟氏)**, was known as **Chángzhēn (常真)**, and from a young age, she studied under her father, earnestly seeking to master this **Daoist technique (此术)**.

**Mistress Mèng (孟氏)**, by nature, had a profound affinity for the **Dao (道)**. Even as a child of eight or nine, she could read and recognize characters. Upon seeing her father’s **Daoist scriptures (此书)**, she would repeatedly observe and recite them until she knew them thoroughly.

Later, someone suddenly fell ill, and she, with deep contemplation and **qi (炁)**-focused intent, went to aid them. Often, she succeeded in many cases, and soon, people came to seek her assistance in great numbers. Her husband, aware of this, forbade her.

Yet, whenever she heard of someone suffering from illness, she would simply **store their condition in her mind (心念)**, and so she did for **forty-five years (四十五年)**.

One day, **the Celestial Sovereign (太上)**—the **Venerable Sage (后圣李君)**—sent an emissary, presenting her with **the Six Jia talismans (六甲符文)** and the **Mèng family’s scriptures and ritual attire (孟氏书服)**. After **fourteen years (一十四年)**, she suddenly departed. Her physical body ascended into the sky and vanished into the mountains, leaving no trace.

She then learned **the Method of Summoning the Daoist Master (召法师存思说)** to invoke the **Four Celestial Guardians (青龙白虎朱雀玄武)** and the **Diagram of Vitality (镇疾图法)**—a technique taught by **Lǎozi (老君)** to **Chìdì (赤帝)**, who was **Zhèng Rén’ān (郑仁安)**. He had received this method in the **Western Realm (西国)**.

The **Four Celestial Guardians (四镇大神)** were summoned through talismans and commandments, declaring:
*"In this world, there are four great guardian deities, who can protect and guard humans, subdue and command malevolent spirits, and shield people from untimely death. Those who practice the **Dao (道)** with sincerity and devotion, when their merit is fulfilled, ascend to the heavens. The **Azure Dragon (青龙)** resides on the left; it is originally a deity of the **Wood Star (木星)** from the celestial realm.
